Elections Bd. v. Wisconsin Mfrs. & Commerce


No. 98-0596


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


227 Wis. 2d 650; 597 N.W.2d 721; 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 103


January 7, 1999, Oral Argument  
July 7, 1999, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended July 27, 1999.
Certiorari Denied November 1, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7153.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Sarah B. O'Brien, Circuit Court Judge. ON BYPASS FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state board filed an appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), dismissing its complaint against respondent corporations for refusing to comply with petitioner's order to file a campaign registration statement and campaign finance report. Both parties filed a joint petition to bypass pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 809.60, on the issue of whether the circuit court properly dismissed petitioner's complaint.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner state board administered campaign finance and election laws pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 11. Respondent corporations produced and aired election advertising on television, describing legislators' votes on certain issues. The featured legislators filed administrative complaints with petitioner. Petitioner issued an order finding that respondents engaged in express advocacy and required respondents to file a campaign registration statement and finance report. Respondents refused to comply. Petitioner filed a complaint seeking civil forfeitures and an injunction. Respondents moved to dismiss the complaint, which was granted. Petitioner appealed, and both parties filed a joint petition to bypass pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 809.60. Upon review, the court affirmed dismissal of petitioner's complaint because respondents' due process rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV were violated, since petitioner did not provide fair warning that respondents' ads could qualify as express advocacy in Wisconsin under a context-based approach. Further, the court held that petitioner could not engage in retroactive rulemaking in an attempt to apply a context-oriented standard of express advocacy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed dismissal of petitioner's complaint against respondent for failing to comply with petitioner's order to file campaign statements, because respondents' due process rights were violated for lack of fair warning that respondents' ads could qualify as express advocacy under a context-based approach. Further, the court held that petitioner could not engage in retroactive rulemaking to create a standard of express advocacy.

 

2 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Eberle v. Dane County Bd. of Adjustment


No. 97-2869


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


227 Wis. 2d 609; 595 N.W.2d 730; 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 104


May 5, 1999, Oral Argument  
July 7, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 221 Wis. 2d 597, 586 N.W.2d 699. (Ct. App. 1998-Unpublished). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: Sarah B. O'Brien.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff real estate developers sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), dismissing plaintiffs' claim asserting a temporary regulatory "taking" without just compensation against defendant county board, in violation of Wis. Const. art. I, § 13, and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, after defendant denied plaintiffs a special exception permit to build a connecting driveway on a tract of land to a public roadway.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff real estate developers obtained approval from a county to change the zoning of a tract of land to residential uses. However, the county restricted access of the land to certain public roads. Plaintiffs sold one lot to buyers, and sought a special exception permit to build a connecting driveway, which was denied by defendant county board. Plaintiffs filed a complaint for review, asserting that defendant engaged in a "taking" without just compensation, in violation of Wis. Const. art. I, § 13, and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The circuit court reversed and remanded defendant's denial of permit, but dismissed plaintiffs' other claims. Both parties appealed, and judgment was affirmed. Plaintiffs sought review of the decision. The court reversed and remanded the case because plaintiffs stated a valid claim for a temporary regulatory taking under Wis. Const. art. I, § 13, but determined that plaintiffs' claims under 42 U.S.C.S. §1983 were not ripe for review. The court expressly overruled that portion of Reel Enterprises v. City of LaCrosse, 146 Wis. 2d 662 (Ct. App. 1988), which held that no regulatory taking resulted when a court reversed a decision of a governmental entity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed judgment for plaintiffs on claim against defendant for temporary regulatory "taking" without just compensation for denial of permit, and remanded case for new hearing because plaintiffs stated a valid claim. The court affirmed dismissal of plaintiffs' federal claims for relief because they were not ripe for review. The court expressly overruled, in part, Reel Enterprises v. City of LaCrosse, 146 Wis. 2d 662 (Ct. App. 1988).

 

3 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Curiel (In re Curiel)


No. 97-1337


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


227 Wis. 2d 389; 597 N.W.2d 697; 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 80


May 4, 1999, Oral Argument  
July 2, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 221 Wis. 2d 596, 586 N.W.2d 698. (Ct. App. 1998, Unpublished). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: Jeffrey A. Kremers.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an unpublished decision of the court of appeals (Wisconsin), that upheld the circuit court's verdict and civil commitment order, which found that respondent state carried its burden to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that petitioner was a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. § 980 (1995-96).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of second degree sexual assault in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(e) (1985-86) and was sentenced to prison for a term of six years. Prior to his scheduled release, respondent state petitioned for his commitment under Wis. Stat. § 980 (1995-96), which governed civil commitment of sexually violent persons. Finding respondent carried its burden of proving beyond a reasonable doubt that it was substantially probable petitioner would engage in future acts of sexual violence, the circuit court committed petitioner. The court of appeals affirmed, concluding that respondent's expert testimony was sufficient evidence to support the circuit court's findings that petitioner was dangerous and the term "substantially probable" required no further definition. Petitioner sought further review. Holding that the legislature intended the term "substantially probable" to be read according to its common and appropriate usage, "much more likely than not," the state supreme court affirmed by holding expert testimony was sufficient to establish beyond a reasonable doubt that it was "much more likely than not" petitioner would engage in future acts of sexual violence.


OUTCOME: Holding the term "substantially probable," when construed according to its common and appropriate usage to mean "much more likely than not," was neither violative of equal protection nor unconstitutionally vague, the court applied criminal standard of review to affirm lower court's upholding of circuit court's verdict and civil commitment order because evidence adduced at trial was sufficient to find petitioner was a sexually violent person.

 

4 of 2046 DOCUMENTS



State v. Kienitz (In re Kienitz)


No. 97-1460


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


227 Wis. 2d 423; 597 N.W.2d 712; 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 89


May 4, 1999, Oral Argument  
July 2, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 221 Wis. 2d 275, 585 N.W.2d 609. (Ct. App. 1998-Published). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: Sarah O'Brien.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The petitioner sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) which upheld a dispositional order that found petitioner to be a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. § 980 (1993-94).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sex offender had twenty-five year criminal history in which he displayed insignificant improvement despite incarceration and treatment efforts. On probation and parole, petitioner deliberately violated conditions of release and denied his need for treatment. A dispositional order that found petitioner to be a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. § 980 (1993-94) was affirmed on appeal. Petitioner sought review. The court affirmed the finding that the evidence was more than sufficient to establish beyond a reasonable doubt that it was "much more likely than not" that petitioner would reoffend. Therefore, the court affirmed that a "substantial probability" of reoffending existed. Evidence in petitioner's record was supported by expert and lay witness testimony. The court also rejected petitioner's claim that his due process rights were violated under the state's dangerousness standard pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 980.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court that adjudged petitioner a sexually violent person because the evidence was more than sufficient to establish beyond a reasonable doubt that there was substantial probability that petitioner would engage in future acts of sexual violence. Petitioner's due process rights were not violated by the application of state standard for dangerousness.


 

5 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Riccitelli v. Broekhuizen


No. 98-0329-FT


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


227 Wis. 2d 100; 595 N.W.2d 392; 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 73


June 2, 1999, Oral Argument  
June 24, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reported at: 221 Wis. 2d 533, 585 N.W.2d 709 (Ct. App. 1998-Published). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: John A. Franke.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, directors of a medical residency program, appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin). The court of appeals held that plaintiff, a former medical resident, was not barred from bringing suit by failing to comply with the notice provisions of Wis. Stat. § 893.82 (1995-96), which governed suits against state employees. The court of appeals found that defendants had "dual personas" in their employment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a medical resident who was terminated from the residency program, brought suit against defendant program directors, alleging intentional interference with contract. Defendants moved to dismiss on the basis that they were state employees and thus plaintiff failed to comply with the notice provisions of Wis. Stat. § 893.82 (1995-96). The court of appeals held that defendants had "dual personas" because they were employees of both the medical school and the medical center and thus plaintiff was excused from complying with the statute. The court reversed. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 893.82 (1995-96) was constitutionally valid and barred plaintiff's cause of action. The dual persona doctrine only applied where the two persona were completely independent from each other. Defendant's work as a residency program director was entirely dependent on his employment as a faculty member. Further, neither judicial estoppel nor equitable estoppel prevented this defendant from claiming that he was a state employee. His testimony in an prior proceeding was not inconsistent with his present testimony because the prior proceeding did not involve defendant's employment status.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that plaintiff, a former medical resident, did not have to comply with the notice provisions of a Wisconsin statute when bringing suit against defendants, two program directors. Plaintiff had to comply with the statute's provisions when bringing suit against state employees. The "dual persona" doctrine only applied where the two personas of an employee were completely independent from and unrelated to each other.

 

6 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Sharp v. Case Corp.


No. 96-2559


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


227 Wis. 2d 1; 595 N.W.2d 380; 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 109; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P15,565


December 1, 1998, Oral Argument  
June 23, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reported at: 216 Wis. 2d 113, 573 N.W.2d 899 (Ct. App. 1998-Unpublished). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Racine. JUDGE: Emily S. Mueller.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tractor manufacturer appealed the affirmance by the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) of a judgment for actual and punitive damages in favor of plaintiff minor who was injured while clearing hay from a tractor attachment.


OVERVIEW: Actual and punitive damages for plaintiff minor were affirmed after a hay bailer attached to defendant manufacturer's defective self-starting tractor drive shaft amputated his arms. The tractor was manufactured in Wisconsin 20 years before the accident, and there was no statute of limitations for a product liability action filed in Wisconsin. An eight-year statute of limitations on product liability actions in Oregon where the accident occurred, did not apply to a claim based upon defendant's failure to warn of defects discovered after the product's manufacture. Submission of the punitive damages to the jury was proper although only one other instance of injury from self-starting of the drive shaft 12 years earlier was shown. While 87,000 tractors of the same type had been made, defendant had notice of self-startings that had occurred without injury. Defendant, despite knowing of the defect and potential harm, failed to take inexpensive remedial measures such as post-sale warnings.


OUTCOME: Actual and punitive damages for plaintiff minor were affirmed. Plaintiff's action in Wisconsin, where defendant's tractor was manufactured, was not barred by an eight-year product liability limitation statute in Oregon where the accident occurred because the Oregon statute did not apply to defendant's failure to warn of defects discovered after the manufacture.

 

7 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


City of Sun Prairie v. Davis


No. 97-1651


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


226 Wis. 2d 738; 595 N.W.2d 635; 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 65


March 3, 1999, Oral Argument  
June 18, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 217 Wis. 2d 268, 579 N.W.2d 753. (Ct. App. 1998, Published). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: Michael N. Nowakowski.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed default judgment against defendant by plaintiff municipal court. Plaintiff had entered default judgment against defendant for his failure to comply with an order that required defendant to personally appear at trial on a civil forfeiture action; on appeal, defendant claimed that the municipal court did not have inherent authority to enter such an order.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff municipal court entered a default judgment against defendant out-of-state resident for defendant's failure to comply with plaintiff's order requiring defendant to personally appear at trial on a civil forfeiture action, and defendant appealed. The reviewing court held that plaintiff did not have inherent authority to order an out-of-state defendant to personally appear at a trial on a civil forfeiture action, and reversed the court of appeals' decision. The court found no statutory authority for a municipal court to subpoena or order the presence of an out-of-state defendant. The court held that any such authority would have to be inherent authority and that there was no such authority within the area of inherent authority ensuring that the court operate efficiently and effectively to provide the fair administration of justice. The court found no such authority in any other area of inherent authority, either. The court concluded that plaintiff could not enter a default judgment on the out-of-state defendant where defendant's attorney appeared on his behalf.


OUTCOME: Judgment that affirmed a default judgment against defendant was reversed and remanded. Plaintiff municipal court did not have inherent authority to order the out-of-state defendant to personally appear at a trial on a civil forfeiture action. The existence of the municipal court and the orderly and efficient exercise of its jurisdiction were not dependent upon the personal presence of defendant, where his attorney appeared for him.

 

8 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bodoh


No. 97-0495-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


226 Wis. 2d 718; 595 N.W.2d 330; 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 66


April 13, 1999, Oral Argument  
June 18, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 220 Wis. 2d 102, 582 N.W.2d 440 (Ct. App. 1998-Published). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Calumet. JUDGE: Donald A. Poppy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed the judgment from Circuit Court of Calumet County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of injury by negligent handling of a dangerous weapon in violation of Wis. Stat. Ann. § 940.24 after his two dogs attacked a fourteen-year-old boy who was riding his bicycle.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant owned two dogs which attacked a fourteen-year-old boy who was riding his bicycle. After the trial court convicted him of injury by negligent handling of a dangerous weapon in violation of Wis. Stat. Ann. § 940.24, defendant appealed. On appeal, the court held that a dog owner can handle a dog in the manner by which he or she supervised, directed, and controlled the dog. The court affirmed the conviction because it held that a dog could be a dangerous weapon if it was used or intended to be used in a manner calculated or likely to cause death or great bodily harm. The court was convinced that there was sufficient and credible evidence to support the jury's verdict finding the defendant guilty of causing injury by negligent handling of a dangerous weapon.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed conviction because it held that a dog could be a dangerous weapon if it was used or intended to be used in a manner calculated or likely to cause death or great bodily harm.

 

9 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Horn


No. 97-2751-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


226 Wis. 2d 637; 594 N.W.2d 772; 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 64


March 4, 1999, Oral Argument  
June 11, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County, Bruce E. Schroeder, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), finding Wis. Stat. § 973.10(2), which required administrative revocation of probation, to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 973.10(2), which delegated to the executive branch the authority to revoke probation. The circuit court entered judgment for defendant, ruling that the delegation violated separation of powers and that § 973.10(2) was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed. Because sentencing was a shared, rather than exclusive, power, the legislature could mandate the scope of judicial discretion. Similarly, the court also determined that the legislature shared probationary power with the judiciary. The court then found that administrative revocation of probation did not unduly burden or substantially interfere with the imposition of criminal penalties by the judiciary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the finding that the statute was unconstitutional; the revocation of probation was within the shared powers of the branches, and the legislature's delegation of the power to the executive branch did not substantially interfere with judicial power.

 

10 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Arneson v. Jezwinski


No. 95-1592


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


225 Wis. 2d 371; 592 N.W.2d 606; 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 52; 15 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 48


January 6, 1999, Oral Argument  
May 5, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff-petitioner employee sought review of a decision by the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed the circuit court's denial of the defendants' motion for summary judgment on the grounds of qualified immunity.


OVERVIEW: In 1990, plaintiff-petitioner was an employee of defendant university when a subordinate employee filed a sexual harassment complaint against him. After a meeting, the university demoted the petitioner and reduced his pay. He sued defendants under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The defendants moved for summary judgment and the trial court denied the motion on the grounds that the defendants lacked qualified immunity. Defendants appealed and the appellate court reversed the trial court's denial of their motion for summary judgment. Petitioner sought review. Petitioner contended that the defendants were not entitled to qualified immunity because when they demoted him and suspended him without pay for 30 days, they violated his clearly established constitutionally protected property interests in his wages and continuous employment. The court affirmed and found that at the time of the incident, federal law did not clearly establish the amount of due process a tenured employee was entitled to receive prior to being suspended and demoted. Therefore, the defendants were entitled to qualified immunity when they suspended petitioner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's holding that defendants had qualified immunity for their suspension of petitioner. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment because at the time of the incident, it was not clear what process was due petitioner when he was demoted.

 

11 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Zarnke


No. 97-1664-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


224 Wis. 2d 116; 589 N.W.2d 370; 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 21


October 7, 1998, Oral Argument  
February 26, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 215 Wis. 2d 71, 572 N.W.2d 491 (Ct. App. 1997-Published). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Eau Claire. JUDGE: Benjamin D. Proctor.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded to the circuit court with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the court of appeals (Wisconsin), which convicted him of sexual exploitation of a child contrary to Wis. Stat. § 948.05(1)(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of sexual exploitation of a child contrary to Wis. Stat. § 948.05(1)(c) for his reproduction and/or distribution of photographs, electronically stored images, and other pictorial reproductions of a child engaging in sexually explicit conduct. Defendant moved to dismiss the sexual exploitation charges, alleging that section 948.05(1)(c) was unconstitutional because it did not require the state to prove that defendant had knowledge of the minority of the person depicted in such materials, but instead allocated the burden to defendant. The circuit court dismissed the charges because it found section 948.05(1)(c) unconstitutional, and the state appealed. The court of appeals reversed, and defendant appealed. The court found that Wis. Stat. § 948.05 on its face did not set forth the requirement that the state carry the burden to prove that defendant had knowledge of the minority of the child-victim depicted in the sexually explicit materials for which prosecution was being brought and that section 948.05 was unconstitutional as it applied to those activities, which did not include some interaction between defendant and the child-victim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals because statutory law was in violation of federal and state constitutions as it applied to distributors of sexually explicit materials and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

12 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Armstrong


Nos. 97-0925-CR, 97-0926-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


223 Wis. 2d 331; 588 N.W.2d 606; 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 2


September 17, 1998, Oral Argument  
January 21, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Racine County, Emmanuel J. Vuvunas, Circuit Court Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Racine County (Wisconsin) that denied his motion to suppress oral statements he made to police before Miranda warnings were given, and a written statement he made after Miranda warnings were given.


OVERVIEW: While incarcerated on an unrelated charge, defendant was questioned by police about a homicide. Prior to questioning, police failed administer Miranda warnings. After defendant made incriminating statements, police read the warnings and prepared a written statement which defendant signed, acknowledging that he understood his rights. At defendant's trial, he moved to suppress both the oral and written statements. The court denied the motion, and defendant was later convicted. Defendant appealed the denial of his motion, and the court affirmed. A person was in custody for purposes of Miranda when he was incarcerated. Therefore, police were required to read defendant the Miranda warning prior to questioning. However, the fact that police failed to read defendant his rights for the earlier statement did not render the written statement signed after defendant was Mirandized unconstitutional. The court overruled an earlier holding applying the "fruit of the poisonous tree" analysis to this situation and held that a failure to administer Miranda warnings which was unaccompanied by any actual coercion was insufficient to result in an imputation of taint to subsequent statements.


OUTCOME: Judgment denying defendant's motion to suppress oral statements he made prior to Miranda warnings and a written statement made after the warning was given was affirmed. Because the oral statements were not made under coercion, the written statement summarizing the oral statements was not tainted. Admission of oral statements, therefore, was harmless error.

 

13 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


County of Kenosha v. C & S Mgmt.


No. 97-0642


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


223 Wis. 2d 373; 588 N.W.2d 236; 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 4


September 10, 1998, Oral Argument  
January 21, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County, Bruce E. Schroeder, Judge. ON CERTIFICATION FROM THE COURT OF APPEALS. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Kenosha. JUDGE: Bruce E. Schroeder.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant management appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin) that fount it guilty of violating a municipal ordinance banning the sale of obscene materials.


OVERVIEW: Defendant management operated an adult bookstore. It was charged with violating a municipal ordinance that banned the sale of obscene materials after it sold copies of a sexually explicit video. A jury found defendant guilty, and the trial court imposed a fine. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed. The ordinance in question was not unconstitutionally overbroad and vague under U.S. Const. amend. I and Wis. Const. art. I, § 3. The ordinance was modeled after Wis. Stat. § 944.21 which in turn was drafted according to the United States Supreme Court's holding in Miller v. California. Under Miller, states could regulate obscene materials so long as the statutes were carefully limited. What this meant was that an average person under contemporary community standard had to find that the work, taken as a whole, appealed to the prurient interest; that the work depicted or described, in a patently offense way, sexual conduct specifically defined by the applicable state law; and that the work lacked serious literary, artistic, political or scientific value. Defendant failed to prove that the ordinance did not comply with this standard.


OUTCOME: Judgment finding defendant management guilty of violating municipal ordinance banning the sale of obscene materials was affirmed because the ordinance was not unconstitutionally overbroad and vague. Regulation under the ordinance was limited to materials which an average person in the community would find appealed to the prurient interest and which lacked value.

 

14 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


American Family Mut. Ins. Co. v. Department of Revenue


Nos. 97-1105 & 97-1106


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


222 Wis. 2d 650; 586 N.W.2d 872; 1998 Wisc. LEXIS 276


November 10, 1998, Oral Argument  
December 16, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 214 Wis. 2d 577, 571 N.W.2d 710 (Ct. App 1997-Published). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: Angela B. Bartell.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners insurance companies petitioned the respondent Wisconsin Department of Revenue for a redetermination of an assessment relating to the interest income on their franchise taxes. The department denied the petition. The tax appeals commission upheld the assessments. The circuit court affirmed the commission. The Wisconsin Court of Appeals reversed the order of the circuit court and the department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insurance companies argued that because the legislature exempted interest income from four state obligations from the calculation of the state franchise tax, franchise tax was discriminatory because it included interest income from federal obligations in the calculation of the state franchise tax but excluded interest income from certain state or local obligations from the measuring base of the state franchise tax. The supreme court disagreed. It held that the interest income from three state and local obligations identified by the insurance companies was not excluded from the calculation of the franchise tax under Wis. Stat. §§ 71.43(2), 71.45(2)(a)3 (1987-88) during the tax years in question. Accordingly the Wisconsin franchise tax was a nondiscriminatory franchise tax within 31 U.S.C.S. § 3124(a)(1) and the court of appeals erred.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

15 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hezzie R. (in Re Hezzie R.)


Nos. 97-0676, 97-0685, 97-1109


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


219 Wis. 2d 848; 580 N.W.2d 660; 1998 Wisc. LEXIS 79



July 3, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Clark County, James W. Rice, Judge. APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County, Thomas P. Donegan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded as to State v. Luis H., No. 97-0685. Reversed and remanded as to State v. Hezzie R., No. 97-0676. Affirmed as to State v. Ryan D.L., No. 97-1109.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner juveniles sought trial by jury after they were charged with first-degree assault. The Circuit Court for Clark County (Wisconsin) held that petitioners did not have a right to trial by jury in juvenile proceedings under the Juvenile Justice Code (JJC), Wis. Stat. § 938. Petitioners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The juveniles argued that the lack of the right to a jury trial during delinquency proceedings under the JJC violated their constitutional rights under Wis. Const. art. I, §§ 5, 7; the Fifth, Sixth, and Fourteenth Amendments; and the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of the Wisconsin and United States Constitutions. The supreme court affirmed the decision of the lower court, concluding that the provisions in the JJC, Wis. Stat. § 938 were criminal in nature because they subjected a juvenile to placement in an adult prison. Provisions pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 938.538(3)(a)1, 938.538(3)(a)1m, and 938.357(4)(d) that subjected a juvenile to placement in an adult prison were severed because they violated a juvenile's rights to a trial by jury under the Wis. Const. art. I, § 7 and the Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments. The remaining non-criminal portions of the JJC were constitutional because juveniles did not have a state or federal constitutional right to a trial by jury in juvenile proceedings.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the decision and remanded the case to the lower court as to the first juvenile. The court reversed the decision and remanded the case to the lower court as to the second juvenile. The court affirmed the decision of the court as to the third juvenile.

 

16 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cardenas-Hernandez


No. 96-3605-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


219 Wis. 2d 516; 579 N.W.2d 678; 1998 Wisc. LEXIS 89


May 27, 1998, Oral Argument  
June 30, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: Stuart A. Schwartz.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed defendant's conviction on two counts of perjury in violation of Wis. Stat. Ann. § 946.31 but reversed defendant's convictions on two counts of criminal defamation in violation of Wis. Stat. Ann. § 942.01.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and convicted of two counts of criminal defamation and two counts of perjury. Defendant appealed and the court of appeals reversed the criminal defamation convictions. On review, defendant challenged a trial court evidentiary ruling that disallowed evidence of an assistant state attorney's statements in a prior criminal proceeding. The court noted that before a court admitted into evidence a prosecutor's prior statement, the court first must be satisfied that the prior argument involved an assertion of fact inconsistent with similar assertions in a subsequent trial. The court found that defendant was not unconstitutionally denied an opportunity to present a defense. However, the court found that the court of appeals acted correctly in reversing defendant's convictions for criminal defamation. The court held that the absolute privilege against civil liability for statements made in judicial proceedings also applied to bar prosecution for criminal defamation for those statements. The plain language of Wis. Stat. Ann. § 942.01(3) provided that criminal defamation did not apply to communications that were otherwise privileged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals where the evidence supported convictions for perjury but not criminal defamation as the defendant's statements made during judicial proceedings were entitled to absolute privilege.

 

17 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Janssen


No. 97-1316-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


219 Wis. 2d 362; 580 N.W.2d 260; 1998 Wisc. LEXIS 102


April 9, 1998, Oral Argument  
June 25, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Outagamie County. JUDGE: John A. Des Jardins.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the circuit court's dismissal of the charge of flag desecration against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, upon his arrest, confessed to various flag thefts in the city and also confessed to defecating on the flag. As a result of his confessions, he was charged with two counts of theft, and one count of intentionally and publicly defiling the United States flag, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 946.05(1). Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the flag desecration charge on the basis that his act of defecating on the flag was a constitutionally protected expression. The circuit court entered an order dismissing the flag desecration charge. The court of appeals upheld the order. On appeal, the court affirmed the ruling of the court of appeals. The court held: (1) that § 946.05(1) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad on its face; (2) that its overbreadth could not be cured by a limiting construction or by severing any of its unconstitutional provisions; and (3) that the State failed to establish the statute's constitutionality. The court noted that, while defendant's conduct was repugnant and completely devoid of any social value, the statute was unconstitutional because it casted contempt upon any speech that was defiant or contemptuous of, or expressed distaste for the flag.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals, which had upheld the circuit court's dismissal of the charge of flag desecration against defendant.

State v. Chrysler Outboard Corp.


No. 96-1158


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


219 Wis. 2d 130; 580 N.W.2d 203; 1998 Wisc. LEXIS 104; 46 ERC (BNA) 1810


December 3, 1997, Oral Argument  
June 19, 1998, Decided  
June 19, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County, Patrick L. Snyder, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sued defendant corporation for violations of the Solid Waste Law, Wis. Admin. Code §§ RD 51.05-.06 (1969) and the Spills Law, Wis. Stat. § 144.76(3) (1977). The Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), dismissed those claims. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state sued the corporation for violations of the Solid Waste Law and Spills Law relating to the dumping of drums in 1970 that contained hazardous waste. The drums were not discovered until 1992. The circuit court granted the corporation's motion for summary judgment. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court affirmed the dismissal of the state's claim that the corporation violated the Solid Waste Law because the claim "accrued" at that time of the violation, thus it was barred by the statute of limitations. Further, the discovery rule was not applicable to that action. The court, however, reversed the dismissal of the state's claim that the corporation violated the Spills Law because that law was applicable in actions by the state to compel remediation of, and to impose penalties for, hazardous substance spills which, although initially caused in part by actions preceding the statute's May 21, 1978, effective date, continued to discharge after that date.


OUTCOME: The order dismissing the state's action pursuant to the Solid Waste Law as time-barred was affirmed. The order dismissing the state's action under the Spills Law was reversed.

Jackson v. Benson


No. 97-0270


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


218 Wis. 2d 835; 578 N.W.2d 602; 1998 Wisc. LEXIS 70


March 4, 1998, Oral Argument  
June 10, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] ON REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 213 Wis. 2d 1, 570 N.W.2d 407. (Ct. App. 1997-PUBLISHED). COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: Paul B. Higginbotham.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of a summary judgment entered in favor of respondents, individuals, a teachers' association, and a civil rights group, by the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which held that the Milwaukee Parental Choice Program (MPCP), Wis. Stat. § 119.23 (1995-1996), was invalid under Wis. Const. art. I, § 18 because it directed payments of money from the state treasury for the benefit of sectarian private schools.


OVERVIEW: The MPCP was enacted to permit certain low-income students to attend private schools at no cost to the students. The MPCP was subsequently amended to allow sectarian private schools to participate. Certain individuals, a teachers' association, and a civil rights group each filed separate actions, which were consolidated, challenging the amended MPCP on state and federal constitutional grounds and the public purpose doctrine. On appeal, the court held that the MPCP was not invalid under the Establishment Clause of the First Amendment because it had a secular purpose, did not have the primary effect of advancing religion, and did not create an excessive entanglement between the State and the schools. The MPCP similarly did not violate the state establishment clause set forth in Wis. Const. art. I, § 18 because students were not compelled to attend sectarian schools. The MPCP was not a private or local bill within the meaning of Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18, and it did not violate the public purpose doctrine because it fulfilled a valid public purpose. The civil rights group's equal protection claim failed as a matter of law because there was no proof of discriminatory purpose or intent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower appellate court's summary judgment in favor of the individuals, the teachers' association, and the civil rights group, and remanded the matter to the trial court with instructions to grant the State's motion for summary judgment. The court also instructed the trial court to dismiss the civil rights group's equal protection claim, and to dissolve the injunction barring the implementation of the MPCP.

State v. Phillips


No. 95-2912-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


218 Wis. 2d 180; 577 N.W.2d 794; 1998 Wisc. LEXIS 59


January 8, 1998, Oral Argument  
May 22, 1998, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed a judgment of conviction entered by the circuit court, which denied defendant's pretrial motion to suppress physical evidence that drug agents seized during a warrantless search of his home. After the circuit court's denial of his motion to suppress, defendant pled no contest to possession of marijuana as a repeat offender.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized during a warrantless search of his home. Defendant thereafter pled no contest to possession of marijuana as a repeat offender. The court of appeals reversed the judgment of conviction and the state appealed. The reviewing court found that defendant voluntarily consented to the search of his bedroom. The court held that the state had demonstrated by clear and convincing evidence that defendant's consent to search his bedroom was voluntary and was not the product of duress or coercion. The court determined that the agents did not use any misrepresentation or threats to entice defendant to give his consent to search his bedroom. The court found that the search of defendant's home took place under generally non-threatening, cooperative conditions. The court therefore concluded that defendant voluntarily consented to the search of his bedroom. The court additionally concluded that the consensual search of defendant's bedroom was purged of any taint created by the unlawful entry.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversing the conviction of defendant was reversed.

Roberta Jo W. v. Leroy W. (In re Roberta Jo W.)


No. 96-2753


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


218 Wis. 2d 225; 578 N.W.2d 185; 1998 Wisc. LEXIS 61


February 18, 1998, Oral Argument  
May 22, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] APPEAL from orders of the Circuit Court for Portage County, Frederic W. Fleishauer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult child challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin) that denied her request under Wis. Stat. § 767.51(3) for child support from respondent father following his identification in a paternity suit and terminated her court-appointed counsel upon filing of a notice of appeal.


OVERVIEW: Adult child sought retroactive child support from father following a paternity action in which he was identified. Her request was denied under Wis. Stat. § 767.51(3) because although she was not yet 19 years old when she commenced the action, she had already received her high school diploma. The court affirmed holding that the statute was consistent with precedent that the court had no authority to retroactively create a child support obligation for an adult because the legislature made no attempt to overturn settled law despite several opportunities. The court found that father was not required to make retroactive payments up to her high school graduation because she does not have a right to that relief simply because her paternity suit was successful, and the court was not required to enforce such an award because she did not have an existing right under Wis. Const. art. I, § 9. The court reversed in part finding that termination of court-appointed counsel for child upon the filing of a notice of appeal was erroneous because it was no longer within the circuit court's jurisdiction to take such action.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying adult child's request for child support from father following his identification in a paternity suit was affirmed because although she commenced the action before she turned 19, she had already received her high school diploma. And she had no existing right to enforce. The termination of her court-appointed counsel was reversed because the circuit court had no jurisdiction to do so upon her filing of a notice of appeal.

 

25 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Tomczak v. Bailey


No. 95-2733


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


218 Wis. 2d 245; 578 N.W.2d 166; 1998 Wisc. LEXIS 62; 117 A.L.R.5th 643


October 7, 1997, Oral Argument  
May 22, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant surveyors appealed from a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a lower court's order denying their motion for summary judgment in plaintiff home owners' action, which was based on a negligent survey. Defendants contended that the action had been brought after the six-year limitation period of Wis. Stat. § 893.37, and that the discovery rule was inapplicable to that statute.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff home owners relied on a survey done by defendant surveyors and had a house constructed. They were sued by adjacent landowners because their home extended beyond their boundaries, based on errors in the survey. Plaintiffs filed suit for negligence against defendants, and the trial court denied defendants' motion for summary judgment. Defendants appealed, and the court reversed, holding that the matter was time-barred under Wis. Stat. § 893.37 and that the discovery rule did not apply. The court held that the discovery rule did not apply to a statute of repose, which § 893.37 was. The court noted that by the wording of the statute, the legislature had already determined that the claim accrued on the date the survey was completed, not the date that the injury was discovered. Accordingly, the court held that the discovery rule was not applicable because it was meant for statutes which had no accrual date. The court also held that there was no equal protection violation because the different treatment of land surveyors and property owners had a rational basis in eliminating surveyors' long-term liability. Lastly, the court found that the survey constituted a single act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's affirmance of the denial of summary judgment to defendant surveyors in plaintiff home owners' action which arose due to a negligent survey. The court held that the matter was barred by a statute of repose, for which use of the discovery rule was inapplicable. The court further held there was no violation of equal protection because there was a rational basis for the time bar as to surveyors.

State v. Konrath


No. 96-1261-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


218 Wis. 2d 290; 577 N.W.2d 601; 1998 Wisc. LEXIS 60


February 20, 1998, Oral Argument  
May 22, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner individual brought a motion to vacate the order for seizure of his motor vehicle in accord with Wis. Stat. § 346.65(6). The seizure order resulted from the individual's fifth conviction for operating a motor vehicle under the influence of an intoxicant contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a). The Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) denied the motion. The individual brought an appeal raising three constitutional challenges.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected the individual's claim that the seizure of his motor vehicle violated the First Amendment to the U.S. Constitution. The court held that the individual lacked standing to assert this claim because the forfeiture was civil in nature and there was a nexus between the motor vehicle to be seized and forfeited and the crime. The court held that the individual could not assert a facial overbreadth challenge that Wis. Stat. § 346.65(6) could be unconstitutionally applied in instances that were not before the court. Similarly, the court held that the individual lacked standing to assert a double jeopardy violation because the forfeiture was an in rem civil forfeiture. Finally, the court rejected the individual's contentions under the Due Process Clauses of the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution and under Wis. Const. art. I, § 1. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 346.65(6) set forth procedural due process protections including providing notice of the seizure and a hearing prior to forfeiture of the motor vehicle. Moreover, the court held that the individual was notified of the impending seizure and possible forfeiture on several occasions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Meyer


No. 96-2243-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


216 Wis. 2d 729; 576 N.W.2d 260; 1998 Wisc. LEXIS 39


December 15, 1997, Oral Argument  
March 20, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Sheboygan. JUDGE: Gary Langhoff.



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed and, as modified, cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of possession of tetrahydrocannabinol with intent to deliver. In so doing, the circuit court denied his motion to suppress evidence seized during the execution of an anticipatory search warrant and also determined that the officers' act of dispensing with the rule of announcement was reasonable. The Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) reversed defendant's conviction and the state sought review.


OVERVIEW: In reversing defendant's conviction, the court of appeals concluded that the no-knock entry during the execution of the search warrant was in violation of defendant's rights under the U.S. Const. amend. IV. After consideration, this court concluded that the anticipatory search warrant was constitutional because it was supported by probable cause. It further concluded that the warrant was not unconstitutional merely because it lacked explicit conditional language stating that the warrant could not be executed until delivery of the contraband was made to the premises to be searched. Finally, this court concluded that an officer could dispense with the rule of announcement when executing a search warrant if the officer had a reasonable suspicion, based upon the particular facts of the given case and the reasonable inferences drawn therefrom, that knocking and announcing the officer's presence would be dangerous or futile or inhibit the effective investigation of the crime. Furthermore, in determining whether reasonable suspicion existed, an officer's training and prior experience in similar situations could be considered in combination with the particular facts.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was modified and affirmed as modified. The case was remanded to the circuit court for a determination of whether the officers had a reasonable suspicion that exigent circumstances existed to justify their no-knock entry.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county government and defendant union sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County (Wisconsin) that declared that plaintiff circuit court judges had exclusive, inherent authority to appoint and remove their judicial assistants regardless of the provisions of a collective bargaining agreement negotiated between defendants.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff circuit court judges filed a complaint that sought a declaration that they had the exclusive authority to appoint and remove their judicial assistants, and that such authority could not be modified by a collective bargaining agreement (agreement) entered into between defendant county government and defendant union. The circuit court decreed that the circuit courts had the exclusive, inherent authority to appoint and remove their judicial assistant. The court noted that the circuit court had exclusive authority in matters of judicial staff administration that generated from its inherent powers conferred by Wis. Const. art. VII, § 2. Because the removal provision obstructed the judiciary in its exclusive sphere, and thereby violated the separation of powers principles implied in the state constitution, the court in turn concluded it was void. The circuit court order was thus affirmed in part.


OUTCOME: The circuit court order that declared that plaintiff circuit court judges had the exclusive, inherent authority to remove their judicial assistants was affirmed.

State v. Howard


No. 95-0770


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


211 Wis. 2d 269; 564 N.W.2d 753; 1997 Wisc. LEXIS 85

June 26, 1997, Opinion Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which granted defendant's motion for a new trial on the ground that due process required that he receive a new trial on the issue of the dangerous weapon enhancer because the jury was not required to find beyond a reasonable doubt that he possessed a dangerous weapon to facilitate the commission of the drug offense.


OVERVIEW: The State charged defendant with, inter alia, aiding and abetting the unlawful delivery of a controlled substance (cocaine) while possessing a dangerous weapon, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 161.41(1)(c)(2), 939.05, 939.63(1)(a)(3), (2) (1987-88). The court held that because defendant was charged with the penalty enhancer of committing a crime while in possession of a dangerous weapon, Wis. Stat. § 939.63 required the State to prove a nexus between the underlying crime and possession of the weapon. Thus, defendant was entitled to a new trial because in his first trial the jury received no instruction on the nexus element. The fact that the defendant could not have foreseen the affect of subsequent decisions at the time of his appeal constituted a sufficient reason for not raising the issue at an earlier date.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision below.

 

32 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Norquist v. Zeuske


No. 96-1812-OA


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


211 Wis. 2d 241; 564 N.W.2d 748; 1997 Wisc. LEXIS 83


May 1, 1997, Oral Argument  
June 25, 1997, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Dismissed without prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In this original action before the court (Wisconsin) for declaratory judgment, petitioners, a mayor and other landowners, sought leave to commence an original action against the secretary of the Wisconsin Department of Revenue pursuant to Wis. Const. art. VII, § 3(2) and Wis. Stat. § 809.70(1)(1995-96). The petitioners had brought this action to challenge the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 70.32(2r).


OVERVIEW: The issues before the court were whether the petitioners had standing to challenge the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 70.32(2r), and whether §§ 70.329(2r)(a) and (b) violated the Uniformity Clause of the Wisconsin Constitution. The court held that the injury necessary for standing had to be actual or threatened. The court held that the landowner's property values might have decreased resulting in higher real property taxes relative to other agricultural land. Thus, the court determined that the landowner satisfied both the actual injury and logical nexus requirements, and had standing to challenge the constitutionality of § 70.32. However, the court found that the landowner had not offered any evidence that his property was over assessed or that other agricultural land was under assessed. The court found that the landowner asserted that because some agricultural land will change in value, it would not be taxed uniformly, and, therefore, his property would not be treated uniformly. Accordingly, the court held that the record was not sufficiently developed and that a decision in the case would have been premature.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the action without prejudice.

 

33 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Wisconsin Dep't of Corrections v. Kliesmet


No. 96-2292


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


211 Wis. 2d 254; 564 N.W.2d 742; 1997 Wisc. LEXIS 84


May 29, 1997, Oral Argument  
June 25, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, John E. McCormick, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wisconsin Court of Appeals, by certification, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County in favor of defendant county sheriff vacating a permanent injunction that had been obtained by plaintiff Wisconsin Department of Corrections (DOC). Under the injunction, which had been obtained in 1987, the sheriff had been enjoined from refusing to keep DOC detainees in the county jail for longer than five days.


OVERVIEW: The DOC argued that it was authorized by Wis. Stat. § 302.31 (1995-96) to place its detainees in the county jail and that the sheriff could not refuse such placement. The court found that under Wis. Stat. § 806.07(1)(g) it was appropriate to review the order to determine whether changed factual circumstances warranted revision of the decree. The concluded that the overcrowding that existed at the jail was substantially greater than had existed when the suit had been filed more than 20 years earlier. The court noted that the number of inmates housed at the jail stood at nearly twice its design capacity and ruled that reconsideration of the injunction was appropriate. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 302.31 was ambiguous and that it should be construed to provided that the DOC was vested with the authority to temporarily keep its detainees in county jails but that such authority was not without bounds. Instead, the DOC's ability to keep detainees at the jail was limited by the sheriff's duty to vigilantly guard the safety of the jail and the inmates. Thus, the sheriff could refuse to accept or retain DOC detainees based on concerns relating to safety and overcrowding at the jail.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court in favor of the sheriff.

Estate of Makos by Makos v. Wisconsin Masons Health Care Fund


No. 96-0174


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


211 Wis. 2d 41; 564 N.W.2d 662; 1997 Wisc. LEXIS 75


March 6, 1997, Oral Argument  
June 20, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order and judgment of the Circuit Court for Marinette County, Charles D. Heath, Circuit Court Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, estate and heirs, appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Marinette County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their medical malpractice action against defendants, doctor, his practice, and health care funds, for exceeding the statute of repose in Wis. Stat. § 893.55(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: The court found that the deceased did not discover that a growth was cancer until nine years after the doctor had diagnosed it as non-malignant. The court determined that Wis. Stat. § 893.55(1)(b) required that actions against health care providers be brought within five years from the date of the act or omission. The court reversed the dismissal of the medical malpractice action by the estate and heirs against the doctor, his practice, and the health care funds. Because, under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, the deceased had a right of access to the court for an opportunity to be heard, the court concluded that Wis. Stat. § 893.55(1)(b) was unconstitutional as applied to the deceased, who, after discovering her injury, had no opportunity to file an action. The court also determined that § 893.55(1)(b) was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt as applied to the deceased, under Wis. Const. art. I § 9, because that provision guaranteed every person a remedy for wrongs committed against them, and § 809.55(1)(b) denied the deceased any opportunity for a remedy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order dismissing a medical malpractice claim by the estate and heirs against the doctor, his practice, and the health care funds and remanded for a trial on the merits.

 

36 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


City of W. Allis v. Sheedy


No. 96-3579-OA


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


211 Wis. 2d 92; 564 N.W.2d 708; 1997 Wisc. LEXIS 73


May 29, 1997, Oral Argument  
June 20, 1997, Opinion Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Rights Declared.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original action for declaratory judgment, petitioners, cities and villages, asked the court to determine whether respondent, a chief judge, exceeded his statutory authority when he issued a directive providing that when a municipal court case was transferred because of a substitution of judge, the case was prosecuted by and the fines and forfeitures which resulted from the action stayed with the municipality in which the new judge sat.


OVERVIEW: The judge argued that he issued the directive at issue pursuant to the exercise of his administrative duties and powers as stated in Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 70.20, 70.19(3) and under the authority of Wis. Stat. § 800.05(3) (1995-96). The court held that the judge had exceeded his authority. To interpret Wis. Stat. § 800.05 in the manner in which the judge suggested would be to deny municipalities participation in their own lawsuits, lawsuits that interpreted and enforced their own ordinances. Under the judge's interpretation, whenever a judge was substituted in a case, the municipality that commenced the action, though remaining a party, would in effect be appointing an attorney, namely the prosecuting attorney of the municipality in which the substituted judge sat. The judge's interpretation of Wis. Stat. § 800.05(3) (1995-96) would not allow a party municipality to choose its own attorney for prosecution of its ordinances and, if the ordinances were found to have been violated, would not allow the party municipality to retain fines and forfeitures resulting from the violations. This could not be the result intended by the legislature. Section 800.05(3) did not authorize the directive.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the judge issued the directive at issue without authority.

L.L.N. v. Clauder


No. 95-2084


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual filed suit against defendants, priest, diocese, and others, alleging that the diocese negligently supervised the priest in that the priest engaged her in a sexual relationship, and the diocese was vicariously liable. The diocese appealed.


OVERVIEW: The individual argued that the diocese knew or should have known that the priest posed a risk of abusing his position as a hospital chaplain to sexually exploit patients whom he counseled because a parish pastor had observed the priest have a fight with another woman. I.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court in favor of the individual was reversed.

 

38 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Jacque v. Steenberg Homes


No. 95-1028


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


209 Wis. 2d 605; 563 N.W.2d 154; 1997 Wisc. LEXIS 53


January 29, 1997, Oral Argument  
May 16, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Manitowoc. JUDGE: Allan J. Deehr.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) affirmed an order that granted defendant trespasser's post-verdict motion to set aside a punitive damages award of $ 100,000 that was awarded to plaintiff property owners in addition to nominal damages of $ 1.00, after it found that the trespasser intentionally trespassed on the property owners' land. The property owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: Despite adamant protests by the property owners, a trespasser plowed a path through their snow-covered field and delivered a mobile home to the property owners' neighbor. In their intentional trespass action, they were awarded $ 1.00 in nominal damages and $ 100,000 in punitive damages. The trespasser contended that judicial precedent precluded the punitive damage award. The court held that when nominal damages were awarded for an intentional trespass to land, punitive damages may be awarded in the discretion of the jury. Because the property owners' legal right to exclude all others from their land was involved, the court noted that the law recognized that actual harm occurred in every trespass. In the case of intentional trespass to land, the nominal damage award represented the recognition that actual harm had occurred. The decision, which carved an exception to precedent, applied to the trespasser as a reward to the property owners who persevered in attacking an unsound rule. The court also held that the amount of punitive damages was not excessive because the trespasser's conduct was egregious and deceitful.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that set aside the punitive damages award and remanded the case with directions.

Hoepker v. City of Madison Plan Comm'n


No. 95-2013


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


209 Wis. 2d 633; 563 N.W.2d 145; 1997 Wisc. LEXIS 52


April 9, 1997, Oral Argument  
May 16, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 202 Wis. 2d 651, 551 N.W.2d 63 (Ct. App. 1996). UNPUBLISHED. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: Gerald C. Nichol.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In proceedings concerning plat approval for appellant developers' residential subdivision, the Wisconsin Court of Appeals held that appellee city could not condition approval of the plat on annexation but could condition approval on use of part of the plat as an open space corridor. The developers appealed the decision as to the open space corridor, and the city appealed the decision as to annexation.


OVERVIEW: Property developers sought approval for the development of a plot of land to be used as a residential subdivision. The city conditionally approved the development provided that an open space was reserved for recreational trails and that the tract be annexed by the city. The developers filed suit to challenge the conditions. The trial court dismissed the suit, but the appellate court found that the open space condition was valid while the annexation provision was not. On review, the court agreed that the annexation condition was not valid because it had the effect of economic coercion on the developers. However, the developers' claims that the open space provision violated the takings clause of the Fifth Amendment was not ripe because the city failed to tell the developers how much land would be reserved and how much the developers would be compensated for the land. Further, the developers had not utilized the inverse condemnation procedure to determine those issues. On remand, then, the city was required to be more specific as to the open space plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court as to the annexation issue, but reversed on the open space issue, finding it not ripe for adjudication.

MCI Telecomms. Corp. v. State


No. 95-0915


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


209 Wis. 2d 310; 562 N.W.2d 594; 1997 Wisc. LEXIS 51


April 8, 1997, Oral Argument; May 13, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
May 13, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff telecommunications utility sought review of an order of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed an order of the trial court and held that defendant Public Service's Commission of Wisconsin's interpretation of Wis. Stat. § 196.85(2) was a correct interpretation of the statute, in that it was consistent with the language of the statute.


OVERVIEW: The telecommunications utility provided long distance services that originated in Wisconsin and terminated both within and outside of Wisconsin. The Public Service Commission (PSC) interpreted the term "intrastate operations" in Wis. Stat. § 196.85(2) to include revenues from all telecommunications made from a telephone located within the state, regardless of whether the call terminated within our outside of Wisconsin. The telecommunications utility filed suit. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the telecommunications utility. The PSC sought review. On appeal, the appellate court reversed. The telecommunications utility sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the appellate court. The court held: (1) the PSC's determination of Wis. Stat. § 196.85(2) was the correct interpretation; (2) Wis. Stat. § 196.85(2) was ambiguous, however, the conclusion of the PSC was supported through the study of extrinsic evidence, such as the legislative history and purpose of the statute; and (3) the interpretation of the phrase "revenues derived from intrastate operations" included revenue from interstate telecommunications originating in Wisconsin.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that reversed an order of the trial court and held that the PSC's interpretation of a statute dealing with revenues from interstate activities was a correct interpretation of the statute, in that it was consistent with the language of the statute.

Jadair Inc. v. United States Fire Ins. Co.


No. 95-1946


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


209 Wis. 2d 187; 562 N.W.2d 401; 1997 Wisc. LEXIS 44


January 9, 1997, Oral Argument  
April 29, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied December 1, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 7122.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Waukesha. JUDGE: Walter J. Swietlik.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner company sought review of the order of the court of appeals which affirmed the dismissal of company's appeal because its notice of appeal was signed by its nonlawyer president.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff engine owner brought suit against company for damages to an aircraft engine incurred during an overhaul performed by company. Respondent insurance company was named as a defendant for denying coverage and moved to dismiss company's appeal because its notice of appeal was signed by company's president who was not a lawyer. The appellate court dismissed the appeal, and company sought review. The court affirmed because, under the plain language of the rules and statutes, only lawyers could appear on behalf of, or perform legal service for, corporations in legal proceedings before Wisconsin courts and the legislature plainly intended that the signing and filing of a notice of appeal on behalf of a corporation was the practice of law. The court held that an effective notice of appeal was a prerequisite to jurisdiction and the prohibition against nonlawyers was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was affirmed.

LaCrosse Queen, Inc. v. Wisconsin Dep't of Revenue


No. 95-2754


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


208 Wis. 2d 439; 561 N.W.2d 686; 1997 Wisc. LEXIS 37


January 28, 1997, Oral Argument  
April 18, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 201 Wis. 2d 537, 549 N.W.2d 261 (Ct. App. 1996). PUBLISHED. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: Michael B. Torphy, Jr.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporation filed a petition for review of respondent Wisconsin Department of Revenue's assessment of sales tax against the corporation for ticket sales on an excursion boat it operated on the Mississippi River. The Tax Appeals Commission and the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) affirmed the assessment. On appeal, the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) reversed. The department petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: The corporation's boat picked up passengers at a dock in La Crosse, Wisconsin, and cruised several miles up the Mississippi during which it crossed into waters of the State of Minnesota. The boat then turned around and returned to the La Crosse dock where the passengers disembarked. Passengers purchased their tickets at La Crosse. The court of appeals held that the boat was engaged in interstate commerce and remanded to determine whether the boat was primarily engaged in interstate commerce and was therefore eligible for the sales tax exemption in Wis. Stat. § 77.54(13). On the Department of Revenue's petition for review, the court reversed. The court held that the boat was not engaged in interstate commerce simply because it sailed into Minnesota waters on its trip up river. The court held that where the purpose of the boat cruises was entertainment and not transportation, where the boat sailed from and returned to the same point in Wisconsin, and where there was no interstate business conducted on the boat, the boat was not engaged in interstate commerce. Accordingly, the court held that the boat was not entitled to the sales tax exemption provided in § 77.54(13).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals.

State v. Hall


No. 94-2848-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


207 Wis. 2d 54; 557 N.W.2d 778; 1997 Wisc. LEXIS 4


September 24, 1996, Oral Argument  
January 24, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 196 Wis. 2d 850, 540 N.W.2d 219 (Ct. App. 1995). PUBLISHED. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: RICHARD J. CALLAWAY.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convicted drug dealer sought review from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which held that Wis. Stat. § 139.91, the drug tax stamp law, provided appellant with derivative use immunity regarding self-incrimination issues. Appellant challenged the constitutionality of the laws, which required dealers to purchase tax stamps for illegal drugs in their possession and affix the stamps to the drugs.


OVERVIEW: Appellant convicted drug dealer was taxed by appellee government under Wis. Stat. § 139.91, the drug tax stamp law, after he was convicted of drug related offenses. The lower court approved the tax and held that the law provided appellant with derivative use immunity regarding self-incrimination issues. Appellant sought review and challenged the constitutionality of this law, which required dealers to purchase tax stamps for illegal drugs in their possession and to affix the stamps to the drugs. Appellee government argued that the stamp law provided protection that was coextensive with the privilege against self-incrimination and, therefore, was constitutional. On review, the court indicated that identifying and prosecuting drug dealers was a laudable purpose, but the legislature failed to use constitutional means to achieve this purpose. The court concluded that, because the stamp law failed to protect against the derivative use, in a criminal proceeding, of information it compelled, it violated the privilege against self-incrimination and was, therefore, unconstitutional. The court struck down the drug tax stamp law as unconstitutional and the decision was reversed accordingly.


OUTCOME: The court struck down the drug tax stamp law as unconstitutional and the decision was reversed because the stamp law failed to protect against the derivative use, in a criminal proceeding, of information it compelled. Therefore, the law violated appellant drug dealer's privilege against self-incrimination and was, therefore, unconstitutional.

Wisconsin Retired Teachers Assn. v. Wisconsin Educ. Assn. Council

September 4, 1996, Oral Argument  
January 17, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended January 21, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW OF A DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS. Reported at: 195 Wis. 2d 1001, 537 N.W.2d 400 (Ct. App. 1995). PUBLISHED. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Dane. JUDGE: Angela B. Bartell.



DISPOSITION: Modified, and as modified, affirmed, and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state administrative officials, and plaintiff associations sought review of a published decision of the Court of Appeals of Wisconsin regarding the constitutionality of 1987 Wis. Act 27, §§ 436m, 684r, and 688km, under which Wisconsin Retirement System (WRS) trust funds were used to pay a "Special Investment Performance Dividend" (SIPD) to certain WRS annuitants.


OVERVIEW: After receiving the attorney general's advice that Act 27 did not violate the contracts clause of the Wisconsin constitution, Wis. Const. art. I, § 12, and the extra compensation clause, Wis. Const. art. IV, § 26, defendant Department of Employe Trust Funds and defendant Employe Trust Fund Board implemented the SIPD legislation. The court concluded that Act 27 and its implementation constituted a taking of plaintiffs' property without just compensation, in violation of Article I, § 13 of the Wisconsin constitution. Accordingly, the court ordered defendants, state administrative officials, in their official capacities, to replenish the WRS fixed annuity reserve account in an amount equal to all funds paid out of the account pursuant to Act 27, plus interest at the effective rate. The court also concluded that defendant Department of Employe Trust Funds and defendant Employe Trust Fund Board did not breach their fiduciary duties by implementing Act 27 because they acted in good-faith reliance on the attorney general's opinion. Finally, the court determined that plaintiffs were entitled to reasonable attorney fees to be paid out of the recovery under the "common fund" doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court modified the appellate court's decision as to the measure of just compensation, and affirmed that decision as modified. The case was remanded to the circuit court with directions.

State v. Harris


Case No. 95-1595-CR & 95-1596-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


206 Wis. 2d 243; 557 N.W.2d 245; 1996 Wisc. LEXIS 120


October 17, 1996, Oral Argument  
December 27, 1996, FILED
