Richland Sch. Dist. v. Dep't of Indus.


No. 90-1750


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


174 Wis. 2d 878; 498 N.W.2d 826; 1993 Wisc. LEXIS 369


February 1, 1993, Oral argument  
April 29, 1993, Decided  
April 29, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals, 166 Wis. 2d 262, 479 N.W.2d 579 (Ct. App. 1991).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district sought review of a decision of a Wisconsin court of appeals, which ruled in favor of respondents, employee and Department of Industry, Labor & Human Relations (DILHR), holding that the employee was entitled to substitute paid leave for unpaid leave under the Wisconsin Family and Medical Leave Act (WFMLA), Wis. Stat. § 103.10, and attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: A school district employee adopted a child and asked to substitute accrued paid leave for unpaid leave under WFMLA. The school district refused, and DILHR issued a make-whole order to the school district, directing it to pay the employee's legal fees. The lower court affirmed DILHR's order, as did the court. The court held that, when an employer provided leave, the WFMLA did not limit the employee's power of substitution, nor was the right limited by the terms of a collective bargaining agreement. The court further held that the employee was entitled to attorney fees at the administrative, trial court, and appellate levels. The court also held that the employee was entitled to the attorney fees even though he was not personally liable for them, reasoning that representation without charge did not mean without cost, and an award of fees to counsel for providing legal services without charge to the client did not constitute a windfall or unjust enrichment of the individual litigant or of the organization awarded the fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court in favor of the employee and the DILHR, and against the school district.

Rolo v. Goers


No. 91-2330


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


174 Wis. 2d 709; 497 N.W.2d 724; 1993 Wisc. LEXIS 360


November 4, 1992, Oral argument  
April 14, 1993, Decided  
April 14, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County, Thomas S. Williams, Circuit Judge. On certification from the court of appeals.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the circuit court is affirmed. Rights Declared.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State Department of Health and Social Services challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which declared that the Department was responsible for funding the conditions of release for indigent persons conditionally released from mental health institutions. Respondent inmate had sought a writ of habeas corpus against the Department and the county seeking his placement or his unconditional release.


OVERVIEW: An inmate, who was an indigent person, was found not guilty of a felony by reason of mental disease or defect, and was committed to a mental health institution pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 971.17 (1987-88), was conditionally released therefrom, on the condition that he would be placed at a residential facility that could monitor his compliance with administering his medication. Neither the State nor the county was willing to pay for the funding required to implement the conditions of the release, and, two years after the order was issued, the inmate filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus for declaratory and injunctive relief seeking his placement or unconditional release. On appeal from the trial court's judgment placing the financial burden on the Department, and, on certification from the appellate court, the court held that: (1) under § 971.17(1), the inmate was committed to the Department until discharged; (2) conditional release was an alternative to discharge, thus an individual conditionally released was not "discharged;" and (3) as such, the Department was financially responsible to fund conditions set forth under the order for the inmate's conditional release.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which had declared that the Department was responsible for funding the conditions of release for indigent persons conditionally released from mental health institutions, in the inmate's petition for writ of habeas corpus against the Department and against the county.

State v. Pittman


No. 91-1413-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


174 Wis. 2d 255; 496 N.W.2d 74; 1993 Wisc. LEXIS 31


November 4, 1992, Oral Argument  
March 10, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals. COURT: Circuit. COUNTY: Milwaukee. JUDGE: FRANK T. CRIVELLO



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(d) in the Circuit Court of Appeals, Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) for having sexual intercourse with a person who the defendant knew was unconscious.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered the apartment of the victim's boyfriend and had sexual intercourse with the victim while she was sleeping. The victim awoke and she and her boyfriend notified authorities. Defendant claimed the victim had consented but that she denied consent out of remorse. Defendant was convicted of violating § 940.225(2)(d) after the trial court excluded expert opinion testimony as to the victim's blood alcohol level and the effect of alcohol on sleep, and the amount of stimulation needed to arouse someone from sleep. On appeal, the court held that the expert testimony was properly excluded as it was irrelevant and did not assist the trier of fact, in that the purpose was to refute the victim's claim that she was asleep during intercourse and thus went to her credibility, which was solely the province of the jury. The court further held that § 940.225(2)(d) was not unconstitutionally vague because it gave clear notice that sexual intercourse with a person who was asleep was illegal and provided an objective standard for applying the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction.

Leean v. State Gaming Com.


Case No. 92-1861-OA


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


1993 Wisc. LEXIS 16



January 20, 1993, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS OPINION IS SUBJECT TO FURTHER EDITING AND MODIFICATION. THE FINAL VERSION WILL APPEAR IN THE BOUND VOLUME OF THE OFFICIAL REPORTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, members of the Wisconsin Legislature, requested leave from the court to commence an original action for a declaratory judgment against respondents, the State of Wisconsin Gaming Commission and the State of Wisconsin Lottery Board concerning the meaning of the term "lottery" in Wis. Const. art. IV, § 24.


OVERVIEW: The members sought a declaratory judgment that the provisions of the Wisconsin Constitution prohibited all forms of gambling and that Wis. Const. art. IV, § 24(6) only authorized the legislature to create a certain type of lottery. The members also sought to enjoin the Gaming Commission and the Lottery Board from authorizing casino gambling and other forms of gambling not specifically authorized by the Wisconsin Constitution. The court denied the petition because it presented no justiciable controversy ripe for adjudication by declaratory judgment. The court noted that there was a difference of opinion with respect to the meaning of the word "lottery," however, there was no adversity of interest between the named parties. The court further noted that the Gaming Commission and the Lottery Commission did not assert allegiance to any one of the three interpretations of the meaning of "lottery." The court stated that there was no claim of right asserted by the members and there were no documents, writings, or contracts that gave rise to any rights of the parties. The court concluded that a determination of the matter would not have legally affected the members in any way.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition to commence an original action.

 

96 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Hartford v. Kirley


No. 91-1390-OA


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


172 Wis. 2d 191; 493 N.W.2d 45; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 770


September 3, 1992, Oral argument  
December 16, 1992, Decided  
December 16, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Action.



DISPOSITION: Rights Declared.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner city filed an action against respondents mayor and city clerk for a declaratory judgment that proposed tax incremental bonds did not constitute debt within the meaning of Wis. Const. art. XI, § 3.


OVERVIEW: The city created a tax incremental district. The city issued general obligation anticipation notes to pay part of the costs. The city planned to issue tax incremental bonds (TIBs) to pay the remainder of the costs. The mayor and the clerk objected, and argued that issuance of the TIBs would cause the city to exceed the debt limitations of Wis. Const. art. XI, § 3. The city filed an action for a declaratory judgment that the TIBs were not debt under art. XI, § 3. The court held that the TIBs would constitute debt pursuant to art. XI, § 3. The court held that although Wis. Stat. § 66.46(9)(b) stated that TIBs were not to be included in the computation of the constitutional debt limitation, the court would look to the substance of the bonds and the legislature's characterization was not controlling in the determination of the constitutional issue. The court held that although the city could avoid obligation under the bonds when the district terminated and the bondholders could not enforce their rights against the city, the city would be obligated to pay a portion of its tax revenues into the district fund; therefore, the TIBs were debt.


OUTCOME: The court held that the bonds were debt within the meaning of the Wisconsin Constitution.

In Interest of Jamie L.


Nos. 90-1990, 90-1991, 90-1992, 91-0148, 91-0149, 91-0150


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


172 Wis. 2d 218; 493 N.W.2d 56; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 771


October 5, 1992, Oral argument  
December 16, 1992, Decided  
December 16, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Reversing and remanding 166 Wis. 2d 1050 (table), 481 N.W.2d 707 (Ct. App. 1991).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the court of appeals is reversed, and the cause is remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner guardian ad litem filed a petition for review to challenge a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed the trial court's order to terminate the parental rights of appellant mother and denied the mother's request for post-termination relief. Respondent county had initiated Children in Need of Protection or Services hearings against the mother and had sought to terminate the mother's parental rights to her children.


OVERVIEW: A county held Children in Need of Protection or Services hearings, and dispositional orders were issued finding three children in need of protection or services, and their mother was informed orally that her parental rights could be terminated if they remained in continuing need of protection or services. She was given a copy of the dispositional orders, which contained a warning summarizing grounds for termination of parental rights. Later, the county sought to terminate her parental rights alleging abandonment and continuing need of protection or services. The trial court found the children were in continuing need of protection or services issued a termination order. The appellate court reversed and held that in the dispositional hearings, the written orders did not give "specific" notice, under Wis. Stat. § 48.356(2), of the grounds for termination. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the court could not use legislative history where a statute was unambiguous; and (2) § 48.356(2) unambiguously provided that the written orders needed only to contain the same information as the oral notice and did not have to give "specific" notice of the applicable grounds for termination.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment, which had reversed the trial court's order to terminate the mother's parental rights and had denied mother's request for post-termination relief, in the county's petition for termination of the mother's parental rights to her children.

State v. Grayson


No. 91-0756-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


172 Wis. 2d 156; 493 N.W.2d 23; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 769


September 3, 1992, Oral argument  
December 15, 1992, Decided  
December 15, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Affirming 165 Wis. 2d 557, 478 N.W.2d 390 (Ct. App. 1991).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction, on defendant's plea of no contest, for four counts of nonsupport contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.27(2). Each of the four counts was for failure to pay court-ordered child support for more than 120 days during a separate calendar year.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted, upon a plea of no contest, of four counts of failure to pay court-ordered child support contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.27(2), with each count representing the failure to pay support for more than 120 days during a separate calendar year. Defendant challenged the judgments of conviction, which were affirmed on appeal. On further appeal, defendant contended that he was entitled to vacatur of his convictions on the ground that the four charges were multiplicitous. The court employed a two-prong test and determined that the convictions were not multiplicitous. The court held that defendant failed to rebut the presumption in favor of multiple counts. The court held that a common sense reading of Wis. Stat. § 948.22 established a legislative intent to permit multiple counts of felony nonsupport where defendant failed to pay child support for one continuous period. The court ruled that § 948.22(2) permitted the prosecutor to charge one count of felony nonsupport for each 120-day term that defendant failed to pay child support, even if defendant failed to pay over one continuous period.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's affirmance of the judgment of conviction for four counts of failure to pay court-ordered child support.

 

99 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Betthauser v. Medical Protective Co.


No. 90-2687


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


172 Wis. 2d 141; 493 N.W.2d 40; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 772


October 8, 1992, Submitted on briefs  
December 15, 1992, Decided  
December 15, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals. Affirming 164 Wis. 2d 343, 474 N.W.2d 783 (Ct. App. 1991).



DISPOSITION: The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for medical malpractice, defendants appealed a judgment of the appellate court (Wisconsin), which reversed the trial court's judgment.


OVERVIEW: As an infant suffering from an upper respiratory infection, plaintiff was prescribed an intramuscular injection that allegedly resulted in injury requiring the amputation of his lower right leg. At the time of his injury, Wis. Stat. § 893.33 authorized plaintiffs to bring an action at any time before plaintiff's 19th birthday. When plaintiff was five years old, § 893.33 was replaced with § 893.56, which, if applied to the present case, required plaintiffs to bring the action before plaintiff's 10th birthday. Plaintiffs filed the claim against defendants when plaintiff was 18 years old. The trial court dismissed the claim because it applied § 893.56. The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court, which held that § 893.33 applied. The court found that there was no indication that the legislature intended retroactive application of § 893.56. If it were applied retroactively, § 893.56 would have immediately extinguished the claims of many children, extinguishing their constitutionally protected causes of action. Plaintiffs filed their cause of action within the time period allowed under § 893.33.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court.

Brookfield v. Milwaukee Metro. Sewerage Dist.


No. 90-1263


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


171 Wis. 2d 400; 491 N.W.2d 484; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 555


September 1, 1992, Oral argument  
November 13, 1992, Decided  
November 13, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for reconsideration denied. Motion for clarification granted and mandate is modified by adding last sentence.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County, Robert T. McGraw, Circuit Judge. On certification from the court of appeals.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the circuit court is vacated and the cause remanded to the circuit court for dismissal. Such dismissal is without prejudice to the District's right to refile within 60 days collection actions for 1985, 1986, 1987, 1988 and subsequent charges.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, municipalities, sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which granted plaintiffs' motions for summary judgment after determining that defendant Sewerage District had improperly attempted to change its rate-charging methods.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, municipalities, brought an action against defendant Sewerage District after defendant attempted to change its method of charging from a usage based formula to a property value based formula. The circuit court granted plaintiffs' motions for summary judgment. The court concluded that the circuit court should have deferred to the Public Service Commission (PSC) and that it did not give adequate consideration to several relevant factors, including: the PSC's expertise in ratemaking; its familiarity with the operating procedures of the industry; and the fact that the legislature had vested the initial power to determine unreasonable sewerage charges and practices in the PSC, not the courts. The court further held that 1981 Wis. Laws, § 282, which enacted Wis. Stat. § 66.888(1)(c)2-5, had a single subject and that subject was reflected in its title; therefore, § 66.888(1)(c)2-5 did not run afoul of the constitutional requirements of Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18. Finally, the court found that because Wis. Stat. § 66.888(1)(c)2-5 came within the "public purpose" doctrine of Wis. Const. art. IV, § 31, it therefore did not violate that provision.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the circuit court and remanded the cause to the circuit court to dismiss the action because the initial venue for determining unreasonable sewerage charges vested with the Public Service Commission, not the courts.

School Dist. of Shorewood v. Wausau Ins. Cos.


Nos. 90-1440, 90-1707


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


170 Wis. 2d 347; 488 N.W.2d 82; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 339



August 27, 1992, Decided  
August 27, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed on September 16, 1992. This petition was not disposed of at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume. Motion for Reconsideration Filed on September 16, 1992. This petition was not disposed of at the time the volume went to press. Its disposition will be reported in a later volume.
Concurring Opinion at, Dissenting Opinion at Sch. Dist. of Shorewood v. Wausau Ins. Cos., 174 Wis. 2d 726, 498 N.W.2d 823, 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 1073 (Wis., 1992)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a decision and order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County, Victor Manian, Circuit Judge. On motion for reconsideration. Withdrawing 168 Wis. 2d 390, 484 N.W.2d 314.
School Dist. of Shorewood v. Wausau Ins. Cos., 168 Wis. 2d 390, 484 N.W.2d 314, 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 200 (Wis., 1992)



DISPOSITION: The decision and order of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school districts brought suit against defendant insurers in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), seeking to require the insurers to pay defense costs, remedial costs, and attorneys' fees incurred in underlying discrimination lawsuits. The circuit court granted summary judgment for insurers, and school districts appealed.


OVERVIEW: The lower court granted summary judgment for insurers, holding that the policies provided coverage for actions seeking damages, not those seeking declaratory and injunctive relief. The court held that the policies provided coverage for school districts, because the underlying complaint alleged that school districts were "affected by" discriminatory acts of other governmental agencies. However, insurers had no duty to defend or indemnify school districts in that action because the declaratory and injunctive relief sought did not constitute damages under the policies. Damages were legal compensation for past injuries and were generally pecuniary in nature. Insurers had no duty to defend or indemnify school districts based upon the request for attorney's fees. Fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 were treated as "costs" of litigation, distinct from damages. Insurers had no duty to indemnify for fees, because insurers had no duty to defend from the outset. Insurers had no duty to indemnify school districts for fees paid under a settlement agreement because insurers did not participate in or consent to the settlement agreement and the policies excluded coverage for contract liability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order and decision of the circuit court.

State v. Mitchell


No. 90-2474-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


169 Wis. 2d 153; 485 N.W.2d 807; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 323


February 26, 1992, Oral argument  
June 23, 1992, Decided  
June 23, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Mandate Vacated September 9, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Wisc. LEXIS 758.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals, 163 Wis. 2d 652, 473 N.W.2d 1 (Ct. App. 1991).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed and the cause remanded to the circuit court for resentencing on the aggravated battery conviction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the lower court's conviction of defendant for aggravated battery and party to a crime, and which found that defendant had intentionally selected the battery victim because of the victim's race in violation of the hate crimes penalty enhancer, Wis. Stat. § 939.645. Defendant contended that § 939.645 unconstitutionally violated his U.S. Const. amend. I rights.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated battery and of being a party to a crime, and his sentence was enhanced based upon the finding that defendant had intentionally selected his victim based on race, under Wis. Stat. § 939.645. Defendant contended that the statute was unconstitutional because it violated his U.S. Const. amend. I right of free speech and his right to due process and equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court reversed and remanded the sentencing, holding that § 939.645 violated U.S. Const. amend. I directly by punishing offensive or bigoted thought. The court noted that the statute targeted and punished the actor's motive, which was a violation of the right to free speech. The court also held that the statute was overbroad in that protected speech was potentially chilled, also in violation of U.S. Const. amend. I.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for aggravated battery and for being a party to a crime. The court held that the sentence enhancement, based upon the hate crimes statute, required reversal and remand for resentencing, because the statute was found to be unconstitutional. The court held that the statute violated the First Amendment, in that it punished bigoted thought, and that it had a chilling effect on free speech.

State v. Comstock


No. 90-2080-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


168 Wis. 2d 915; 485 N.W.2d 354; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 328


February 24, 1992, Oral argument  
June 17, 1992, Decided  
June 17, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals, 163 Wis. 2d 218, 471 N.W.2d 596 (Ct. App. 1991).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed and the cause is remanded to the circuit court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed an order dismissing four felony charges against defendant and that defendant's previously vacated no contest pleas remain vacated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with four felonies, and entered no contest pleas to two reduced misdemeanor charges. The State agreed to dismiss the other two charges and the trial court accepted the pleas. The trial court later set aside the pleas and another trial court reversed. The intermediate appellate court reversed, and the State sought review. The court reversed, holding that the first trial court was prohibited from setting aside the no contest pleas, because jeopardy had attached. Defendant had been convicted, because a presentence report had been prepared, and was only to be prepared after a conviction. Wis. Stat. § 972.15. The trial court had accepted defendant's no contest pleas to the misdemeanor charges, therefore, the court reinstated those pleas. The State made the motion to dismiss the remaining charges, and therefore, reinstatement of those charges was barred.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and reinstated two misdemeanor charges and previously vacated no contest pleas against defendant.

Jones v. Milwaukee County


No. 91-0817


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


168 Wis. 2d 892; 485 N.W.2d 21; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 331


March 24, 1992, Oral argument  
June 17, 1992, Decided  
June 17, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied, August 11, 1992. As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a decision of the circuit court.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the circuit court is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant social services department sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which determined that Wis. Stat. § 49.015 (1985-86), which required dependent persons to have resided in Wisconsin for at least 60 consecutive days to be eligible for general relief, was unconstitutional under the equal protection clauses of the federal and state constitutions. Appellee residents had been denied relief.


OVERVIEW: The residents were denied general relief benefits because they had not resided in Wisconsin for 60 consecutive days. The issue was whether the 60-day waiting period penalized an individual's right to travel by preventing migration to Wisconsin by the withholding of welfare relief to individuals such that the waiting period promoted a compelling state interest under the strict scrutiny standard. The court held that the trial court improperly found that the waiting period penalized the residents' right to travel. Thus, the traditional equal protection standard, and not strict scrutiny, should have been applied such that equal protection was denied only if the classification was without any reasonable basis. On the merits, the court held that § 49.015 was constitutionally valid because the government offered a reasonable basis for the 60-day requirement, which was the objective of encouraging individuals to support themselves through employment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which found the residence requirement to be unconstitutional.

 

105 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Elfelt v. Cooper


No. 90-1326


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


168 Wis. 2d 1008; 485 N.W.2d 56; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 334; 92-2 U.S. Tax Cas. (CCH) P50,338


April 28, 1992, Argued  
June 17, 1992, Filed


NOTICE:

 [**1]


PRIOR HISTORY: REVIEW of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant widow challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a lower court judgment declaring that plaintiff purchasers became the owners of an undivided one-half interest in the home of the widow as tenants in common. The purchasers were the successful bidders at a tax sale of that interest in the home, which was owned by the widow's deceased husband, for the collection of unpaid income taxes owed by the husband.


OVERVIEW: The widow argued that the Internal Revenue Service (IRS) did not have authority under I.R.C. § 6331 to sell the interest in the homestead property without her consent and that the sale was, therefore, invalid. On appeal, the court agreed. In applying the Internal Revenue Code, state law determined the nature of the legal interest that the widow had in the property. Under Wis. Stat. § 706.02(1)(f), the nature of homestead property held in joint tenancy between a husband and wife was indivisible by one spouse without the consent of the other. As such, the husband could not have conveyed any interest in the jointly held homestead without the widow's consent. Consequently, the IRS, which stepped into the husband's shoes, had no authority to convey the husband's interest at the tax sale, such that the sale to the purchasers was ineffective. Moreover, because the husband was deceased, the court held that the widow owned the property in fee under her right of survivorship. As a result, the appellate court's judgment was reversed and the matter was remanded with directions that the widow was to be declared the sole owner of the property in fee simple absolute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals and remanded the matter with directions to the trial court to enter judgment declaring the widow to be the sole owner of the property in fee simple absolute.

State v. Annala


No. 90-2162-CR


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


168 Wis. 2d 453; 484 N.W.2d 138; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 306

DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the circuit court at the age of 20 for a sexual assault he had committed at the age of 15. The Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) affirmed the judgment of conviction and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: At age 15, defendant sexually assaulted a child. The child's mother agreed not to press criminal charges. During a counseling session at age 20, defendant informed her counselor of the incident. The counselor reported the information to the district attorney, who, after discussions with the victim's family, their attorney, and the victim's therapist, reluctantly instituted criminal charges against defendant. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the juvenile court did not have jurisdiction over allegations against an adult defendant, regardless of defendant's age when the alleged offense occurred; (2) the trial court's interpretation of Wis. Stat. § 48.12(1) did not violate equal protection because the legislative classification based on an individual's age at the time of prosecution rather than an individual's age at the time of the alleged offense was rationally related to the purposes of the Children's Code; and (3) the district attorney did not abuse his prosecutorial discretion in charging defendant because his decision to prosecute defendant was based upon factors which he properly could have considered and upon which, in his discretion, he properly could have prosecuted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court decision affirming defendant's conviction for sexual assault.

Sch. Dist. of Shorewood v. Wausau Ins. Cos.


Nos. 90-1440, 90-1707


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


168 Wis. 2d 390; 484 N.W.2d 314; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 200


November 26, 1991, Oral argument  
May 20, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Filed, June 8, 1992. Motion for Reconsideration Filed, June 9, 1992. Motion for Reconsideration Filed, June 8, 1992. Motion for Reconsideration Filed, June 8, 1992. Concurring and Dissenting Opinions Dated April 15, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from judgments of the circuit court for Milwaukee County, Victor Manian, Circuit Judge. On certification from the court of appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgments of the circuit court are reversed and the cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insureds appealed from judgments of the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) which granted the motions of defendant insurers for summary and declaratory judgment and which denied the insureds' motions for summary and declaratory judgment. The court accepted the appeal on certification from the court of appeals pursuant to Wis. R. Civ. P., Wis. Stat. § 809.61.


OVERVIEW: The insureds settled a federal civil rights action that had been brought against them for declaratory, injunctive, and remedial relief. The insureds then brought an action for declaratory judgment against their insurers by which they sought to recover attorney fees and expenses that they incurred in defending themselves in the underlying litigation and monies that they expended in order to comply with the settlement agreement. The lower court held that the underlying action and the attorney fees did not constitute actions for "damages" within the policies, and granted the insurers' motion for summary judgment. On review the court reversed the judgments. The court held that in applying the ordinary usage of the term "damages," the term "damages" in the insurance policies included the insureds' expenditures to comply with injunctive or equitable relief because damages did not depend on the nature of the relief sought but rather on the use of the legal system to compel the insureds to make a payment or to take certain action. The court held that the statutory characterization of attorney fees as costs was not conclusive for purposes of interpreting insurance policies.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments and the case was remanded to the circuit court with instructions to grant the insureds' motion for summary judgment and to determine the amount due under the policies in order to reimburse the insureds for their own attorney fees and for the expenditures they incurred in abiding by the terms of a settlement agreement.

State v. Borrell


Nos. 90-2241-CR, 90-2332-CR

DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgments and orders of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of both first-degree murder and armed robbery in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin. After the trial court sentenced defendant, he claimed that his parole eligibility date under Wis. Stat. § 973.014 was unconstitutional. The trial court ruled otherwise, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to serve two consecutive sentences of life imprisonment for first-degree murder and 20 years for armed robbery. The court held that defendant's later parole eligibility date under Wis. Stat. § 973.014 was constitutional. The court found that defendant was required to serve an extra five years in connection with the armed robbery conviction prior to being eligible for parole release, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 304.06(1)(b). The court held the legislature permitted sentencing courts to use discretion when setting parole eligibility dates under Wis. Stat. § 973.014(2). The court held that defendant did not have a due process claim because the possibility of parole did not create a claim of entitlement nor a liberty interest. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 973.014 was constitutional and did not violate the separation of powers doctrine, effective assistance of counsel provisions, protections against cruel and unusual punishment, or rights to meaningful appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments and orders.

Le Fevre v. Schrieber


No. 90-2705


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


167 Wis. 2d 733; 482 N.W.2d 904; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 192


February 26, 1992, Oral argument  
April 22, 1992, Decided  
April 22, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Calumet County: Hugh F. Nelson, Judge. On certification from the court of appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the Calumet county circuit court is reversed and the cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On certification from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), the court considered whether plaintiff posthumous child was entitled to maintain an action against defendants, driver and insurers, for wrongful death under Wis. Stat. § 895.04 related to the death of his father. The trial court held that the child lacked standing to sue, refusing to recognize a posthumous adjudication of paternity.


OVERVIEW: The child's mother was not married to his father. Shortly before the child's birth, his father was killed in a car accident. After the child's birth, his paternal grandfather, as personal representative of the father's estate, filed a petition under Wis. Stat. § 767.54(1)(e) to establish paternity to obtain workers' compensation benefits for the child. Although paternity was established in the family court, the trial court refused to recognize the adjudication, holding that the child had not established paternity under Wis. Stat. § 852.05(1) and that posthumous paternity actions were not maintainable. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the adjudication of paternity was valid because Wis. Stat. § 767.45(1) allowed a paternity action to be filed by the personal representative of the father's estate. The court held that because the paternity adjudication was valid and under Wis. Stat. 852.03(4) the child was an heir of his father's estate under Wis. Stat. § 852.05(1), the court held that the child had standing to maintain a wrongful death action under Wis. Stat. § 894.04.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that dismissed the wrongful death action filed by the posthumous child against the driver and insurers.

 

111 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Piper v. Popp


No. 88-2406


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


167 Wis. 2d 633; 482 N.W.2d 353; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 186


November 25, 1991, Oral argument  
April 14, 1992, Decided  
April 14, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied June 3, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals, 156 Wis. 2d 823 (table), 458 N.W.2d 390 (Ct. App. 1990).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate challenged an order from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a judgment of the trial court against the inmate in plaintiff's action to recover for gunshot wounds imposed upon him by the inmate. The court granted review to determine whether an indigent prisoner was entitled to appointment of counsel to represent him in defense of a civil tort action.


OVERVIEW: The inmate shot and injured plaintiff and plaintiff's father and killed plaintiff's mother. After the inmate was convicted and sentenced for the shootings, plaintiff filed a civil action against him to recover damages for personal injuries, as well as punitive damages. After the inmate's attorneys withdrew from the case, the trial court refused to appoint counsel for the indigent inmate. Instead, the trial court allowed the inmate to travel to the court and defend himself. On appeal of the court of appeals' affirmance of the resulting judgment against the inmate in the trial court, the court ruled that the inmate had no constitutional right to appointment of counsel. The court also found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to appoint counsel for the inmate. The court found that a presumption existed against an indigent litigant's right to appointed counsel where his physical liberty was not at stake. Applying a three-part test, which balanced the private interest, the risk of an erroneous decision, and the government's interest, the court ruled that the presumption was not overcome and that due process did not require appointment of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the court of appeals, ruling that the inmate was not entitled to court-appointed counsel to represent him the civil tort action against him.

 

112 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Guardianship of L.W.


No. 89-1197


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


167 Wis. 2d 53; 482 N.W.2d 60; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 178


September 4, 1991, Oral argument  
April 1, 1992, Decided  
April 1, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Eau Claire county, Gregory A. Peterson, Circuit Judge. On bypass from the court of appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent guardian of the ward petitioned the Circuit Court for Eau Claire County (Wisconsin) for a declaratory judgment. The circuit court granted the guardian the authority to consent to the withdrawal from the ward all life-sustaining medical treatment, including artificial nutrition and hydration. The guardian, appellant guardian ad litem, and respondent hospital appealed.


OVERVIEW: The guardian sought a declaratory judgment to determine whether either the guardian or a court had the authority to consent to withdrawal from the ward all life-sustaining medical treatment, including artificial nutrition and hydration. The court held (1) that an incompetent individual in a persistent vegetative state had a constitutionally protected right to refuse unwanted medical treatment, including artificial nutrition and hydration, from the common law right of self-determination and informed consent, the personal liberties protected by U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and from the guarantee of liberty in Wis. Const. art. I, § 1; (2) that a court-appointed guardian might have consented to withdrawal of such treatment where it was in the best interests of the ward to do so; and (3) that the guardian did not need the prior authority of the court, although that decision might have been reviewed by the court at the instance of parties in interest. The court did not accept the circuit court criteria to guide the guardian's best interests determination. The court held that the best interests determination was to be made on objective criteria as to the personal best interests of the patient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the circuit court.

Demmith v. Wisconsin Judicial Conference


No. 91-0067-OA


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


166 Wis. 2d 649; 480 N.W.2d 502; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 21


January 3, 1992, Oral argument  
March 11, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Action For Declaratory Judgment: Rights Declared. Original action for declaratory judgment, rights declared.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Rights Declared.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought declaratory relief in his challenge to the Uniform Misdemeanor Bail Schedule (UMBS) that was adopted by respondent, the Wisconsin Judicial Conference. Petitioner claimed that the UMBS failed to comply with Wis. Stat. § 969.065, and that § 969.065 violated the separation of powers doctrine and provided for an invalid delegation of judicial power.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was arrested on two misdemeanor charges and was required to remain in jail because he could not bail. He challenged the UMBS and sought to have it declared not in compliance with Wis. Stat. § 969.065. The court held that the UMBS had not complied with § 969.065 because it had not been referred to the judicial conference to develop the misdemeanor bail guidelines and because it did not relate primarily to "individuals." The UMBS relied on the type of offense committed, rather than on the individual defendant. The court found that the legislature and the judiciary shared power in setting standards for bail, so long as the legislature did not infringe on the judiciary's power. The requirement of § 969.065 to relate to individuals had not constituted an undue burden or a substantial interference with the judiciary's function with respect to bail. The court declined to find an unlawful delegation of powers under § 969.065 and stated that requiring the judicial conference to adopt bail guidelines had not constituted an unlawful delegation of judicial powers to law enforcement officers.


OUTCOME: The court held that UMBS had not complied with Wis. Stat. § 969.065 and ordered the judicial conference to consider developing guidelines for persons accused of misdemeanors which related to individuals.

 

114 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Grover


No. 90-1807


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


166 Wis. 2d 501; 480 N.W.2d 460; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 18


October 4, 1991, Oral argument  
March 3, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for reconsideration denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals, 159 Wis. 2d 150, 464 N.W.2d 220 (Ct. App. 1990).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff families and private schools appealed a judgment of a Wisconsin appellate court, which reversed a trial court judgment in favor of defendant school administration organizations. The trial court held that a state parental choice program (MPCP), which permitted selected children from low-income families to attend nonsectarian private schools at no cost did not violate Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18. The families and private schools appealed.


OVERVIEW: Families and private schools that participated in the MPCP filed an action against school administration organization officials alleging that some of their actions of the school superintendent were designed to frustrate the MPCP. The school administration organizations asserted that the MPCP violated Wis. Const. art. IV, § 18. The trial court ruled in favor of the families and private schools, and the appellate court reversed. On appeal, the court held that the MPCP did not violate § 18. The court held that the MPCP legislation was presumed to be constitutional and the school administration organization § 18, did not show that it was not constitutional and, the MPCP legislation was not a private or local bill under the applicable five-factor Brookfield test and was therefore not subject to the requirements of § 18. The court also held in response to the school administration's assertion that the MPCP did not violate the uniformity clause off Wis. Const. art. X, § 3 because the private schools participating in the MPCP did not constitute "district schools" for purposes of the uniformity clause.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals holding that the MPCP violated the state constitution was reversed.

 

115 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Barnhill v. Board of Regents of UW System


No. 89-0372


SUPREME COURT OF WISCONSIN


166 Wis. 2d 395; 479 N.W.2d 917; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 9


October 29, 1991, Oral argument  
February 12, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied on April 21, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals, 158 Wis. 2d 278, 462 N.W.2d 249 (Ct. App. 1990).



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed and the case is remanded to the circuit court for dismissal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, a former employee of a research organization affiliated with a state university, initiated an action against appellants, directors of the organization, and claimed that directors violated employee's right of free speech by terminating employee for disclosing confidential survey questions. The circuit court found in favor of employee and the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), affirmed. The appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Organization was a sub-unit of a state university. Its purpose was to conduct surveys and field research. Organization employed part-time interviewers to conduct the surveys. All of the part-time interviewers entered into an agreement of confidentiality with organization. Employee worked as one such interviewer. In connection with one survey, employee refused to participate for ideological reasons. Employee disclosed the survey questions, prior to the conclusion of the survey, on two different occasions to news sources. Subsequently, organization's director terminated employee's continued employment. On review of the intermediate appellate court's affirmance of the trial court's judgment in favor of employee, the court reversed the decisions. The court held that the directors were entitled to qualified immunity as public officials. Moreover, the court held that directors did not violate employee's First Amendment rights when they terminated his employment, because organization's needs for confidentiality and discipline clearly outweighed employee's interest in disclosing the survey questions during the course of the survey.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the intermediate appellate court and remanded the case to the trial court for dismissal.

Martinez v. Department of Indus., Labor & Human Relations


No. 90-1266


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


165 Wis. 2d 687; 478 N.W.2d 582; 1992 Wisc. LEXIS 3; 126 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P57,461


November 26, 1991, Argued  
January 15, 1992, Decided  
January 15, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 160 Wis. 2d 272, 466 N.W.2d 189 (Ct. App. 1991).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff migrant workers and intervenor, the Joint Committee for Review of Administrative Rules (JCRAR), contested an order of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) reversing the trial court's decision that Wis. Stat. § 227.26 was constitutional. The workers had challenged the action of defendants, the Department of Industry, Labor and Human Relations (DIHLR) and its secretary, which unilaterally enforced a sub-minimum training wage.


OVERVIEW: DILHR promulgated a rule creating a category of employees to whom employers could pay a sub-minimum wage. The JCRAR, pursuant to its statutory review authority under § 227.26, temporarily suspended part of the rule and amended it. DILHR notified Wisconsin employers to ignore JCRAR's changes. The trial court found the statute constitutional because it met the bicameral passage requirements and the presentment clause did not interfere with the separation of powers doctrine. The court of appeals reversed, concluding that § 227.26 intruded on the executive branch. The court held that DILHR exceeded its power when it instructed employers to ignore JCRAR's changes because DILHR, a legislative creation, had no authority to declare JCRAR's rule changes void. There were sufficient procedural safeguards available to prevent unauthorized JCRAR decisions because § 227.26 was carefully drawn to avoid a separation of powers challenge and met presentment and bicameral requirements by imposing mandatory checks and balances on any temporary rule suspension. Further, the rule suspension process provided a legislative check on agency action, preventing potential agency overreaching.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals and reinstated the holdings of the trial court that the statute was constitutional. The court ordered that the workers receive the benefits of the JCRAR decision during the period of July 1, 1989, through March 23, 1990.

Dieck v. Unified School Dist.


No. 89-2356


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


165 Wis. 2d 458; 477 N.W.2d 613; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 760


September 4, 1991, Oral Argument  
December 12, 1991, Decided  
December 12, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 157 Wis. 2d 134, 458 N.W.2d 565 (Ct. App. 1990).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed the decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed a summary judgment entered by the circuit court in favor of defendants, school district, school board, and others, in plaintiffs' action challenging the district's authority under Wis. Const. art. XI, § 3(2), (3) to enter into a lease purchase agreement to finance the acquisition of land and the construction of a new high school.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff taxpayers filed a class action suit against defendants, school district, school board, and others, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief and challenging the district's authority pursuant to Wis. Const. art. XI, § 3(2), (3) to enter into a lease purchase agreement to finance the acquisition of land and the construction of a new high school. The circuit court granted summary judgment in favor of defendants and the court of appeals affirmed. On further review, the court affirmed and held that the district did not incur indebtedness in violation of Wis. Const. art. XI, § 3(2) when it executed the lease agreement. The court found that the agreement included a nonappropriation option that gave the district the right to terminate the agreement by electing not to appropriate funds for rental payments. As such, the district had no legal obligation for unpaid rentals and its funds were not jeopardized beyond the current fiscal year. The court also determined that the district was not required to obtain voter approval under Wis. Stat. § 67.05(6a) (1989-90) or Wis. Stat. § 120.44(2) because it had not engaged in "borrowing."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of defendants, school district, school board, and others, and against plaintiff taxpayers because the district had the right to terminate the agreement by electing not to appropriate funds for rental payments. The court determined that the district had not incurred an indebtedness in violation of the state constitution.

Consolidated Freightways Corp. v. Department of Revenue


No. 89-1720


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


164 Wis. 2d 764; 477 N.W.2d 44; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 750


September 4, 1991, Oral argument  
November 14, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Reversing 157 Wis. 2d 65, 458 N.W.2d 550 (Ct. App. 1990).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner freight corporation appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which upheld the franchise tax assessment applied to the freight corporation by respondent Wisconsin Department of Revenue (department). The department assessed the tax against the freight corporation using the formula provided in Wis. Admin. Code § Tax 2.47 to ascertain the amount of income the freight corporation earned in Wisconsin.


OVERVIEW: The freight corporation argued on appeal that the formula violated Wis. Stat. § 71.07(2)(e), which limited the taxable income derived from business transacted within Wisconsin, the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution; and, the Due Process Clause of the United States Constitution. The freight corporation contended that the formula taxed income earned outside of the state. The court reversed the judgment of the appeals court and held that the assessment against the freight corporation did not violate Wis. Stat. § 71.07(2)(e), because the freight corporation earned income through various activities, including sales, transportation, pickup and delivery, terminal activity, consolidation center activity, line haul movement, and management and taxed income "derived from" the freight corporation's business transactions within Wisconsin that were subject to taxation under § 71.07(2)(e). The court also held that the tax assessment upon the freight corporation's Wisconsin income did not violate the limits of the Commerce Clause, nor the Due Process Clause, because the formula was not facially discriminatory between in-state and out-of-state carriers.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appeals court decision, which upheld the department's assessment of the franchise tax against the freight corporation, with regard to the freight corporation's petition for review of the tax assessment.

Peppies Courtesy Cab Co. v. Kenosha


No. 90-1097


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


165 Wis. 2d 397; 475 N.W.2d 156; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 642


September 6, 1991, Oral argument  
October 16, 1991, Decided  
October 16, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from the Court of Appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County: David M. Bastian, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the Kenosha county circuit court is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On certification from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), appellant taxicab drivers challenged a judgment from the circuit court which found that Kenosha, Wis., Ordinance No. 59-88 was constitutional and not violative of the drivers' inherent rights of due process and liberty interests guaranteed under the Wisconsin and United States Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: Kenosha, Wis., Ordinance No. 59-88 required all taxicab drivers to wear a uniform and comply with certain grooming requirements. The ordinance's constitutionality was challenged. It was alleged that the ordinance interfered with the taxicab drivers' fundamental rights. The circuit court found the ordinance constitutional because it served a legitimate governmental purpose. On appeal, the state's highest court reversed, holding that, although licensing and regulation of public service occupations fell within the police power of the government, the form of regulation chosen was required to bear a reasonable or rational relationship to the public good being pursued by the government and could not unreasonably restrict the particular rights being curtailed. In the instant case, the uniform and personal grooming requirements were implemented to help the city achieve its aesthetic objectives. However, no formal studies had been completed by the city that showed that the taxicab drivers were responsible for tarnishing the city's image. The ordinance lacked a rational basis for accomplishing the government's purpose and was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed.

Hogan v. Musolf


No. 89-1175


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


163 Wis. 2d 1; 471 N.W.2d 216; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 494


May 29, 1991, Argued  
June 26, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Reversing 157 Wis. 2d 362, 459 N.W.2d 865 (Ct. App. 1990).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals affirming an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Judge P. Charles Jones.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the current and former Secretaries of the State of Wisconsin, appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which had affirmed an order of the circuit court that issued an injunction against the collection of state income taxes from plaintiffs, several retired federal employees, in their 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action for violations of 4 U.S.C.S. § 111.


OVERVIEW: The former federal employees filed a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action against the Secretaries that alleged violations of 4 U.S.C.S. § 111 on the grounds that the state income tax imposed on retirement benefits paid to former federal employees, but not former state employees, was discriminatory. The circuit court granted an injunction against the collection of further taxes and established a fund for payments of refunds. The appellate court affirmed, and the Secretaries appealed. The court reversed, holding that the former federal employees were required to exhaust their state administrative remedies prior to filing the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action. In arriving at its conclusion, the court noted that violations of 4 U.S.C.S. § 111 were actionable under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Although exhaustion requirements in § 1983 were disfavored, the former federal employees were required to seek protection of their federal rights by state remedies because they were "plain, adequate, and complete." Moreover, a § 1983 tax claim did not mature until state officials had the opportunity to rectify the alleged violation through state administrative procedure.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the federal employees.

State v. Milashoski


No. 90-0412-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


163 Wis. 2d 72; 471 N.W.2d 42; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 492

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, citing U.S. Const. amend. IV, appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) that affirmed a judgment of a trial court convicting defendant for manufacturing a controlled substance contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 161.41(1)(b), 161.14(4)(n) (1987-1988) after denying a motion to suppress evidence in accordance with Wis. Stat. § 213.095 (1987-1988).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after firefighters removed containers of liquids from his father's house during a fire and had the contents analyzed at the state crime laboratory. Defendant contended that the seizure and analysis were illegal. Defendant also contended that he should not have been fined $ 15,000 because he was indigent. The court affirmed the judgment. The court concluded that the firefighters acted consistently with the public policy on hazardous substances. The court determined that defendant's expectation of privacy in the containers was unreasonable. The court concluded that the warrantless testing of the contents of the unmarked containers was not unconstitutional. The court concluded that the fine imposed on defendant, as modified by the trial court, was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals affirming the trial court's judgment convicting and sentencing defendant for manufacturing a controlled substance.

Madison v. Baumann


Nos. 89-0452, 89-0453


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


162 Wis. 2d 660; 470 N.W.2d 296; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 473


March 26, 1991, Argued  
June 12, 1991, Decided  
June 12, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Reversing and remanding 155 Wis. 2d 388, 455 N.W.2d 647 (Ct. App. 1990).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decision reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) that affirmed the holding of the trial court that appellant's general ordinance regulating noise was unconstitutional. The litigation arose when appellant issued citations to appellee street musicians for violating the ordinance in question when a resident complained of appellees' playing musical instruments and singing in the park late one night.


OVERVIEW: Appellee street musicians were issued citations when a resident complained of appellees' playing instruments and singing in a nearby park late one night. Appellees argued that the noise ordinance on which the citations were based, Madison, Wis., Gen. Ordinance 24.04(1), was unconstitutional because it regulated protected speech. Appellant argued that whether or not the sounds made by appellees were constitutionally protected music, appellees were in violation because the music was noise that tended to disturb the peace. The trial court held that the ordinance was unconstitutional and the appellate court affirmed. Appellant sought review. The court reversed and remanded. The court found that appellant had the right to enact an ordinance that impinged on free speech in the interest of preserving the peace. The court held that the ordinance was not void for vagueness because its strictures were narrowly tailored to apply to noise that "unreasonably" disturbed the peace, and that the reference to reasonableness gave notice, to appellees as well to the enforcers, of what was prohibited conduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision affirming the trial court's holding that appellant city's noise ordinance was unconstitutionally void for vagueness, finding that the ordinance was constitutional because it applied only to noise that unreasonably tended to disturb the peace. The court remanded for prosecution of appellee musicians cited under the ordinance for disturbing the peace by playing and singing outdoors late one night.

 

124 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. R.R.E.


No. 89-1435


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


162 Wis. 2d 698; 470 N.W.2d 283; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 334


April 24, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
June 11, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming in part, reversing in part and remanding 155 Wis. 2d 467, 455 N.W.2d 914 (Ct. App. 1990).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals affirming an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Judge Charles B. Schudson.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed in part, reversed in part, and cause remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed an order of the trial court dismissing defendant's petition for a re-examination hearing. Defendant contended that he was entitled to release because the trial court failed to abide by the 30-day time limit for holding the hearing on his petition as required by Wis. Stat. § 51.20(16)(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect of one count of second-degree murder and one count of attempted murder. Defendant was committed to a state facility. He petitioned the trial court for re-examination, and a hearing was not held within 30 days, as required by § 51.20(16)(c). Defendant claimed that he was entitled to release due to the trial court's failure to hold a timely hearing. The appeals court ruled that he was not entitled to release and dismissed his petition. Upon review, the court determined that the legislature did not intend the release of criminally committed persons without a court determination that the individual could be safely released. Thus, it held that defendant was not entitled to release from his commitment. Nonetheless, the trial court erred by dismissing defendant's petition because the legislature did not intend the trial court to lose competence to exercise its jurisdiction over re-examination petitions that were not timely heard by that court. Dismissal would only serve to punish the already aggrieved defendant, so that the appropriate remedy was to conduct a re-examination hearing as quickly as possible.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the court of appeals' determination that defendant was not entitled to release from his commitment. The court reversed the portion of the court of appeals' decision dismissing defendant's petition and remanded the case to the trial court for a hearing to determine whether defendant was entitled to release.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wholesaler challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) that reversed and remanded the grant of summary judgment in favor of the wholesaler in its declaratory judgment action challenging defendant secretary of revenue's application of Wis. Stat. § 125.33(1)(a).


OVERVIEW: The wholesaler brought a declaratory judgment action seeking a ruling on its definition of trade spending. In re S.Y.


No. 90-0074-FT


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


162 Wis. 2d 320; 469 N.W.2d 836; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 333


February 27, 1991, Submitted on briefs  
June 6, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming 156 Wis. 2d 317, 457 N.W.2d 326 (Ct. App. 1990).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decision affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an alleged mentally ill person, brought a petition to review a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the trial court's judgment on appellee State's petition that appellant was mentally ill and that he was subject to a one-year extension of his commitment because of dangerousness.


OVERVIEW: Appellant waived his right to counsel at a mental health proceeding, and a jury rendered an adverse verdict, finding that appellant was mentally ill and dangerous. The appellate court affirmed the one-year commitment. On review, the court affirmed because (1) the trial court's order allowing appellant to waive his right to counsel was supported by evidence that appellant was competent to represent himself in that he understood his case and the State's burden of proof, that appellant had expressive language and good communication skills; (2) the right to self-representation was guaranteed by Wis. Const., art. I, § 21(2) because appellant was a suitor under that provision in that he was a party to an action; (3) under Wis. Stat. § 51.20(3), the term "adversary counsel" did not imply separate counsel but allowed for pro se representation as a contestant on one's own behalf; and (4) the trial court properly accepted appellant's waiver of counsel because appellant was entitled to a presumption that he was competent at the time of the mental health proceeding and the State had the burden of proving him incompetent by clear and convincing evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

Johnson v. Allis Chalmers Corp.


No. 89-0649


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


162 Wis. 2d 261; 470 N.W.2d 859; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 320


February 27, 1991, Argued  
June 5, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming 155 Wis. 2d 344, 455 N.W.2d 657 (Ct. App. 1990).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals affirming a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County, Judge Michael B. Torphy, Jr.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an accident victim and his wife, challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the dismissal of their products liability action against the manufacturers based on their egregious failure to comply with court orders and procedure.


OVERVIEW: The victim was injured in a farm accident involving a tractor and a bale handler. He and his wife commenced a product liability action against the manufacturers of both pieces of equipment. During the discovery phase, the victim and his wife continuously failed to respond to the manufacturers' repeated requests for discovery. This failure continued even in the face of various court orders compelling compliance and threats of sanctions. The trial court granted the manufacturers' motion for dismissal based on the egregious failure of the victim and his wife to comply with court orders. On appeal, the court agreed that the dismissal of the action was a proper sanction. The victim and his wife offered no credible excuse for the two year delay in delivering the discovery material to the manufacturers. Considering the length of time that had passed since the victim and his wife had been warned of the consequences of failing to obey court orders, the time the trial court allowed them to cure their failure, and their failure to seek either extension or modification of the court orders, this evidenced that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding their actions were egregious.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the products liability action of the victim and his wife, based on their egregious failure to comply with court orders and procedures.

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision of the court of appeals (Wisconsin) that dismissed its cross-appeal of an order entered in the trial court that had dismissed two counts of a securities fraud case. The trial court, in a bench trial, convicted defendant of two other counts of securities fraud in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 551.41(3) and 551.58 and one count of theft by a bailee.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the trial court's judgment of acquittal should be treated as if the trial court had entered a finding of guilty and then set aside the finding on the grounds that a necessary element had not been shown. In essence, the State argued that the trial court had made findings tantamount to a finding of guilt, which pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 974.05(1)(a), authorized it to appeal the ultimate dismissal of the securities frauds count. The court rejected the State's arguments. The court examined the trial court record and pointed out that the trial court had explicitly found defendant not guilty and in its order had acquitted defendant. The court noted that to interpret the law to allow the State to appeal acquittals of counts in an information when defendant appealed convictions of other counts in the same information would inhibit defendant's right to a meaningful appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision that dismissed the State's cross-appeal from the trial court's judgment of acquittal of defendant as to two counts of securities fraud.

In re Paternity of C.A.S.


No. 89-0265


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


161 Wis. 2d 1015; 468 N.W.2d 719; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 306


March 26, 1991, Argued  
May 13, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming 156 Wis. 2d 446, 456 N.W.2d 899 (Ct. App. 1990).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner putative father sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed an order of the trial court that dismissed his petition against respondent mother to be adjudicated the father of two children. The trial court dismissed the petition pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 767.458(1m) on the ground that a judicial determination finding him to be the father of the children would not have been in their best interests.


OVERVIEW: The putative father filed a petition against the mother to be adjudicated the father of the two children allegedly sired by him during her marriage to her husband. The trial court dismissed the petition under § 767.458(1m) on the ground that a judicial determination finding him to be the father of the two children would not have been in the best interests of the children. The court of appeals affirmed the decision. On appeal, the issue was whether the statute itself or the application of the statute infringed on the putative father's constitutional right to a relationship with children born into an extant marital family? The court affirmed the judgment. The court found that he did not have a close relationship with the children. The court concluded, as the trial court did, that the best interests of the children would not have been served by a judicial determination of paternity. The existing family unit should have been kept intact, not for the benefit of the wife of the husband, but for the benefit of the two children, whose interests in the matter was paramount.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals that affirmed an order of the trial court that dismissed the putative father's petition against the mother to be adjudicated the father of the two children.
