State v. Petrone


No. 89-1551-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


161 Wis. 2d 530; 468 N.W.2d 676; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 301


January 25, 1991, Argued  
May 6, 1991, Decided  
May 6, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for reconsideration denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: On certification from the Court of Appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court For Walworth County, John R. Race, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court convicted and sentenced defendant upon a jury verdict finding him guilty of three counts of sexual exploitation of children, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940,203(2). Defendant appealed. The matter was before the court on certification from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction and sentence on several grounds. Defendant challenged various aspects of the seizure of undeveloped photographic film from his home as a violation of U.S. Const. amend. IV. He argued his complaint and information failed to charge the required element of scienter; challenged the jury instruction defining the word "lewd" in Wis. Stat. § 940.203(2); and argued that his presentence report contained inaccurate information, which he was not allowed to challenge. On appeal, the court held that (1) the search warrant, which authorized the seizure of all film used in the taking of photographic pictures involving nude and partially nude female juveniles, included within its scope unmarked and undeveloped rolls of film; (2) although the complaint and information were deficient in charging scienter, they cited the number of the statute defining the crime, and defendant could not show he was prejudiced; (3) the instruction, taken as a whole, gave the jury an adequate definition of "lewd;" and (4) nothing in the record suggested that the trial court abused its discretion when it sentenced defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and sentence.

 

131 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kuntz


No. 88-1565-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


160 Wis. 2d 722; 467 N.W.2d 531; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 33


October 5, 1990, Argued  
April 3, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for reconsideration denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Reversing in part and affirming in part 153 Wis. 2d 772, 452 N.W.2d 585 (Ct. App. 1989).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals which reversed in part and affirmed in part a judgment of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County, Judge Arnold Schumann.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed in part and affirmed in part and the judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Wisconsin appealed from a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed in part and affirmed in part a trial court judgment that convicted defendant of arson to a building, first-degree murder, and burglary/battery. The court of appeals reversed the arson conviction on the ground that the jury instructions created a mandatory conclusive presumption. Defendant raised evidentiary and double jeopardy issues.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's estranged wife's mobile home was set on fire; her daughter was killed. Defendant made a statement after his arrest. The jury was instructed that a mobile home was a building for purposes of Wis. Stat. § 943.02(1), defining arson to a building. Defendant was convicted of arson, committing battery in the course of a burglary, and first-degree murder. The court of appeals ruled that the instruction relieved the State of an element of its burden of proof. The court reversed that ruling and otherwise affirmed the affirmance of defendant's burglary and murder convictions. The instruction was harmless error. Defendant's custodial statement was admissible for impeachment as voluntary and trustworthy even if obtained in violation of Miranda. Evidence of defendant's past uncharged misconduct in burning an ex-wife's belongings was admissible to prove identity; the evidence was prejudicial but highly probative. Wisconsin permitted use for impeachment of defendant's prior misdemeanor conviction even though it did not involve dishonesty. Burglary/battery was not a lesser included offense of first-degree murder; the Double Jeopardy Clause permitted punishment for both offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the court of appeals' decision affirming defendant's convictions for first-degree murder and burglary/battery. The court reversed the court of appeals' decision reversing defendant's conviction for arson.

 

132 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Webb


No. 89-0593-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


160 Wis. 2d 622; 467 N.W.2d 108; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 24


January 4, 1991, Argued  
March 26, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for reconsideration denied; Per Curiam Opinion; ABRAHAMSON, J., HEFFERNAN, C.J., BABLITCH, J., dissent.


PRIOR HISTORY: Reversing 154 Wis. 2d 320, 453 N.W.2d 628 (Ct. App. 1990).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) reversed defendant's conviction for first-degree sexual assault, finding that his Sixth Amendment rights were violated by the circuit court's closure of the preliminary hearing. The appellate court remanded the case for a new preliminary hearing, ruling that defendant's conviction should be reinstated if the new hearing resulted in findings justifying bindover for trial. The state and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: At issue was what relief, if any, should be available to a defendant who was duly convicted at a fair and errorless trial when it was determined on appeal that his preliminary hearing was closed in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VI. The court held that a conviction resulting from a fair and errorless trial in effect cures any error at the preliminary hearing. Accordingly, a defendant who claims that error occurred at his preliminary hearing may only obtain relief before trial. This holding effectively overruled State v. Sorenson, 400 N.W.2d 508 (Ct. App. 1986). The court reasoned that to vacate the judgment of conviction, dismiss the prosecution, and require the state to start anew would result in a substantial waste of judicial and prosecutorial resources. Furthermore, if defendant wanted review of the alleged error at the preliminary hearing, he should have sought immediate review in the appellate court by interlocutory appeal. Finally, no procedural defect of any sort at the preliminary hearing affects the circuit court's jurisdiction to proceed to trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court.

 

133 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Ford v. Kenosha County


No. 89-1046


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


160 Wis. 2d 485; 466 N.W.2d 646; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 20


October 4, 1990, Argued  
March 11, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from the Court of Appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kenosha County.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff arrestee filed a complaint against defendants, court clerical personnel and an assistant district attorney (collectively, court personnel), for liability for an arrest resulting from an erroneously issued bench warrant. The Circuit Court of Kenosha County (Wisconsin) dismissed the complaint for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. A question concerning judicial immunity was certified to the court.


OVERVIEW: After the arrestee wrote a check for insufficient funds and was criminally charged with issuing a worthless check, his attorney appeared in court, and the arrestee paid his fine. Later, the bench warrant was issued, and the arrestee was detained in custody. The state court of appeals certified a question to the court regarding whether the doctrine of judicial immunity extended to the court clerical personnel and the district attorney's office, thereby shielding them from liability for the arrest. The court held that the assistant district attorney, in submitting the bench warrant to the judge as alleged in the complaint, was acting as an advocate and was, therefore, absolutely immune from liability. The clerical personnel, in preparing the bench warrant, which was accepted and signed by the judge, were performing a quasi-judicial act and were absolutely immune under the doctrine of quasi-judicial immunity from any negligence in preparing and submitting the warrant. The court reasoned that, when acting under the direction of a judge, clerics were responsible only when refusing to discharge their duty, when requested by the judge, or when guilty of fraud in collusion with the judge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment dismissing the arrestee's complaint.

 

134 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Milwaukee v. Wroten


No. 89-1628


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


160 Wis. 2d 207; 466 N.W.2d 861; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 18


October 30, 1990, Argued  
March 6, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On bypass from the Court of Appeals.

Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court For Milwaukee County, Leah M. Lampone, Circuit judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff municipality appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) holding that a municipal judge could strike down a municipal ordinance and that the resisting police ordinance under which defendant accused offender was prosecuted was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant accused offender was charged with resisting the police. At a hearing before a municipal judge, defendant contended, successfully, that the ordinance under which he was charged was unconstitutional on grounds of overbreadth. He prevailed over plaintiff municipality's objection that the ordinance was constitutional and that in any event a municipal judge lacked the power to strike down a statute on constitutional grounds. A circuit judge then upheld the municipal judge's decision, and plaintiff appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed. It held that the state law creating the post of municipal judge necessarily imbued such judges with the power to declare laws unconstitutional. In addition, the ordinance in question was unconstitutional, in that it criminalized not only conduct directly interfering with the police but also speech critical of them. It was therefore overbroad, and in its overbreadth it encroached on free speech rights. It was therefore unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment favoring defendant was reversed. Municipal judges can strike down municipal ordinances on constitutional grounds, and the resisting police ordinance in question in this appeal was unconstitutional due to its trammeling free speech rights.

 

135 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Burlington N. R. Co. v. Superior


No. 88-1794


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


159 Wis. 2d 434; 464 N.W.2d 643; 1991 Wisc. LEXIS 2


October 30, 1990, Argued  
January 22, 1991, Decided  
January 22, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming 153 Wis. 2d 206, 450 N.W.2d 486 (Ct. App. 1989).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner city challenged a decision of an appellate court (Wisconsin), which reversed an order of a trial court directing the city to pay postjudgment interest at the annual rate of five percent pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 74.73(1r)(1985-86), on a judgment ordering a refund of taxes collected under a statute that the appellate court declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court reversed the trial court's order and held that the city owed postjudgment interest at the annual rate of 12 percent, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 815.05(8)(1985-1986), not five percent. The city argued that § 815.05(8) did not literally apply to "every" judgment for the recovery of money, that Wis. Stat. § 66.09(1) provided for interest on a judgment against a municipality, and that Wis. Stat. § 74.73(1r) provided for interest at the legal rate and should have been applied under the circumstances. The court affirmed the appellate court's decision and held that Wis. Stat. § 815.05(8) expressly established the postjudgment interest rate for every judgment for which the legislature had not explicitly provided a different postjudgment interest rate and that this interpretation of the statute comported with the language and legislative history of § 815.05(8) and Wis. Stat. § 66.09, which did not establish the applicable rate. In addition, the court ruled that because taxes collected pursuant to a statute that was unconstitutional were void ab initio, Wis. Stat. § 74.73(1r) did not apply in this case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision.

State v. Moats


No. 88-0431-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


156 Wis. 2d 74; 457 N.W.2d 299; 1990 Wisc. LEXIS 269


September 8, 1989, Argued  
June 28, 1990, Decided  
June 28, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from the court of appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth county: James L. Carlson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court for Walworth county is reversed and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Walworth County Circuit Court (Wisconsin), convicting him of first degree sexual assault. Defendant argued that his constitutionally tainted confession was insufficient evidence to support the finding of probable cause at a preliminary examination and to justify his bindover for trial. The court accepted the issue upon certification and took jurisdiction over uncertified issues raised in his appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted after a five-year-old girl accused him of sexual assault. During the investigation, defendant requested the assistance of counsel. However, he was subsequently question without his attorney. The only evidence presented by the prosecution at the preliminary examination was defendant's statement, which was obtained in violation of his rights because his attorney was not present. The court noted that the right to a preliminary examination was not a constitutional right and that the constitution allowed a prosecutor in a preliminary examination to establish probable cause with evidence obtained in violation of the constitution. The court also concluded that defendant was not prejudiced by the trial court's ruling that his statement could be used for impeachment purposes at trial because the court found that the statement was not compelled. Finally the court held that defendant was denied his constitutional right to confront a witness against him when the trial court prohibited the introduction of prior sexual assaults perpetrated on the victim for the limited purpose of establishing an alternative source for her sexual knowledge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and ordered a new trial. The court concluded that the constitutionally tainted statement could be used during the preliminary hearing, but held that the trial court erred in not allowing the defendant to offer evidence at trial that the victim previously had been sexually assaulted for the purpose of showing an alternative source for the victim's sexual knowledge.

Wisconsin Educ. Ass'n Council v. State Elections Bd.

The court concluded that there was no actual controversy between the Board and WEAC.

Gard v. State Elections Bd.


No. 90-0298-OA


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


156 Wis. 2d 28; 456 N.W.2d 809; 1990 Wisc. LEXIS 267


May 30, 1990, Argued  
June 27, 1990, Decided  
June 27, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action for declaratory judgment, rights declared.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Rights Declared. Section 11.26(9)(a), Stats. declared constitutional. The stay of proceedings in State of Wisconsin Elections Board v. John Gard and Friends and Neighbors of John Gard, Case No. 89-CV-219, pending in Oconto County Circuit Court is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, legislator, political party, and campaign committee, filed a petition under Wis. Stat. § 809.70 for a declaratory judgment against respondent Wisconsin State Election Board seeking a declaration of the unconstitutionality of Wisconsin's campaign financing law, Wis. Stat. § 11.26(9)(a), which established a cap on the amount of funds that a candidate could receive from political action and other committees.


OVERVIEW: The Board filed a complaint in the circuit court against the legislature and his committee alleging that they received contributions in excess of the limit imposed by Wis. Stat. § 11.26(9)(a). The court granted a petition filed by the legislator, the committee, and the party for leave to file an original declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of § 11.26(9)(a), and it stayed circuit court proceedings. The court declared that § 11.26(9)(a) did not violate the First or Fourteenth Amendments of the United States Constitution, or the Wisconsin Constitution. The court held that (1) while the legislature's limits on contributions affected the rights of political expression and association protected by the First Amendment, the State had a compelling interest in regulating campaign financing to prevent corruption or the appearance of corruption resulting from public awareness of opportunities for abuse inherent in large individual contributions, and such limits were necessary to serve that interest; and (2) § 11.26(9)(a) did not violate the Equal Protection Clause because its classifications were narrowly tailored to serve a compelling governmental interest.


OUTCOME: The court declared that Wisconsin's campaign financing law did not violate the First or Fourteenth Amendments of the United States Constitution, or the comparable provisions of the Wisconsin Constitution.

Peissig v. Wisconsin Gas Co.


No. 88-1611


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


155 Wis. 2d 686; 456 N.W.2d 348; 1990 Wisc. LEXIS 255


April 24, 1990, Argued  
June 14, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for reconsideration denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: On certification from the Court of Appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Clark County, Judge Michael W. Brennan.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed in part, and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Clark County (Wisconsin), awarded plaintiff injured parties treble damages and double costs and interest in a successful negligence suit against defendant gas company. The gas company appealed contending that the injured parties were not entitled to treble damages and that Wis. Stat. §196.64 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The injured parties were injured in a gas explosion and fire. They sued the gas company alleging that the explosion was caused by the negligent construction or maintenance of the natural gas pipeline feeding into their mobile home. A jury found that the gas company was causally negligent and awarded the injured parties damages. The injured parties filed a motion in the circuit court to treble damages. The lower court granted the motion and also awarded double costs and interest. The gas company claimed the injured parties were not entitled to treble damages and that Wis. Stat. § 196.64 was unconstitutional. The court held that (1) a finding of willful, wanton, or reckless behavior was not necessary to award treble damages against public utilities in negligence actions under § 196.64, (2) where the jury in essence found that the gas company violated Wis. Admin. Code § PSC 135.02, it violated Wis. Stat. § 196.64, (3) § 196.64 did not violate the gas company's equal protection rights, was not unconstitutionally vague, and did not assess an excessive fine, and (4) where the injured parties failed to serve individual offers of settlement, the doubling of costs was unavailable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's finding that willful, wanton, or reckless behavior was not necessary to award treble damages to the injured parties, and that the statute authorizing treble damages was not unconstitutional. However, the court reversed the lower court's decision to assess double costs against the gas company.

State v. Pulizzano


No. 88-0010-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


155 Wis. 2d 633; 456 N.W.2d 325; 1990 Wisc. LEXIS 257


March 7, 1990, Argued  
June 12, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming and remanding 148 Wis. 2d 190, 434 N.W.2d 807 (Ct. App. 1988).

Review of part of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed; and cause remanded for a new trial and further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of part of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed an order and judgment of conviction of defendant for four counts of first degree sexual assault contrary to Wis. Stat. § 940.225(1)(d).


OVERVIEW: During defendant's sexual assault trial, the trial court excluded evidence of a prior sexual assault experienced by one of the complaining child witnesses under the rape shield statute, Wis. Defendant was convicted, but her convictions were reversed on appeal. On further appeal by the State, the court affirmed, holding that defendant was denied her constitutional right to confrontation and compulsory process when the trial court excluded the evidence. Defendant had attempted to introduce the evidence for the limited purpose of establishing an alternative source for the witness's sexual knowledge. The court held that the rape shield statute was constitutional, but that the evidence was so relevant and probative that defendant's right to present it was constitutionally protected. Defendant's offer of proof was adequately supported by a doctor's report. The court also held that the trial court abused its discretion in permitting the prosecutor's closing remarks.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment reversing defendant's convictions.

Schulz v. Ystad


Nos. 88-2018-FT, 88-0952, 88-1631, 88-1594


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


155 Wis. 2d 574; 456 N.W.2d 312; 458 N.W.2d 535; 1990 Wisc. LEXIS 250


March 27, 1990, Argued; March 28, 1990, Submitted on briefs  
June 6, 1990, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for reconsideration denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Reversing 150 Wis. 2d 948, 444 N.W.2d 66 (Ct. App. 1989).

Reversing and remanding 151 Wis. 2d 556, 445 N.W.2d 58 (Ct. App. 1989).

Reversing and remanding 151 Wis. 2d 549, 445 N.W.2d 327 (Ct. App. 1989).

On certification from the Court of Appeals.

Review (No. 88-2018-FT) of a decision of the Court of Appeals.

Review (No. 88-0952) of a decision of the Court of Appeals.

Review (No. 88-1631) of a decision of the Court of Appeals.

Appeal (No. 88-1594) from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Walworth County, John R. Race, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals in In re the Marriage of Schulz v. Ystad (No. 88-2018-FT) is reversed; the order of the circuit court is affirmed. The decision of the court of appeals in In re the Marriage of Thompkins (No. 88-0952) is reversed, and the cause is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion. The decision of the court of appeals in In re the Marriage of Piaskoski (No. 88-1631) is reversed, and the cause is remanded to the circuit court for further [***2] proceedings consistent with this opinion. The judgment of the circuit court in In re the Marriage of Harms (No. 88-1594) is vacated, and the cause is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This matter was before the court on four cases consolidated to consider whether Wis. Stat. § 767.32(1m), which provided only for prospective modification of child support orders, applied retroactively to prohibit reducing or eliminating arrearages that accrued pursuant to orders entered prior to the statute's effective date.


OVERVIEW: In order to remain eligible for federal funding in providing child support enforcement services, the Wisconsin legislature enacted § 767.32(1m) to allow only for prospective modification of child support orders. The court of appeals in three cases held that the statute applied retroactively and certified a fourth case to the court in which the circuit court concluded that the statute applied retroactively. The court held that § 767.32(1m) applied prospectively only and that child support arrearages which accrued pursuant to an order for support entered prior to the effective date of the statute could be modified, reduced, or eliminated in accordance with the law in effect prior to the effective date of § 767.32(1m). It found that § 767.32(1m) was substantive law as the elimination of the right to petition for retroactive modification of support was such a substantial change in the legal rights and obligations of a child support obligor that it could not be characterized as merely remedial or procedural in nature. Further, there was nothing to indicate that the legislature intended the prohibition contained in § 767.32(1m) to reach back to orders entered prior to its effective date.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the statute providing only for prospective modification of child support orders applied only prospectively and reversed the decisions of the lower courts that determined it was to be applied retrospectively to prohibit reducing or eliminating arrearages that accrued prior to the statute's effective date.

 

142 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Eichman


No. 88-1754-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


155 Wis. 2d 552; 456 N.W.2d 143; 1990 Wisc. LEXIS 251


March 28, 1990, Argued  
June 6, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed, and cause remanded to the circuit court for determination of the State's second pre-trial motion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which summarily reversed a trial court's decision to deny the State's motion in limine to admit expert testimony in the State's criminal action against defendant that alleged sexual exploitation by a therapist pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 940.22 (1985-86).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the two issues were whether the State had the right to appeal a pretrial order in a criminal proceeding pursuant to § 974.05(1)(d)2 and whether the circuit court abused its discretion when it denied the State's pre-trial motion to admit expert testimony. The lower court determined that the expert testimony was admissible. The court held that the State had a right to appeal the pre-trial motion because the denial of the motion had the substantive effect of suppressing evidence. Thus, the State could appeal as a matter of right pursuant to § 974.05(1)(d)2, which allowed the interlocutory appeal of the suppression of evidence but not the exclusion of evidence. On the merits, the court determined that the trial court erred as a matter of law when it concluded that expert testimony was not required because what constituted "psychotherapy," as defined by statute, could be understood by the average juror. The expert testimony should have been allowed because the standard to gain admission of such testimony was that it would have assisted the trier of fact to understand the evidence or to determine a fact in issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court and remanded the matter to the trial court.

GTE Sprint Communications Corp. v. Wisconsin Bell, Inc.


No. 89-0272


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


155 Wis. 2d 184; 454 N.W.2d 797; 1990 Wisc. LEXIS 241; 113 P.U.R.4th 476


March 7, 1990, Argued  
May 15, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from Court of Appeals.

Appeal from a declaratory judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Honorable Laurence C. Gram, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court is reversed, and rights declared.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff communications corporation appealed from a declaratory judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied plaintiff's motion for summary judgment to have declared unconstitutional the retail sales tax imposed upon the transfer of origination and termination services (access services) pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 77.51(14)(m) and 77.52(2)(a)4 (1985-86). Defendant was a telephone company, and the State intervened.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff claimed that Wis. Stat. §§ 77.51(14)(m) and 77.52(2)(a)4 violated equal protection because the tax only applied to purchases of access services by inter-local access and transport area (LATA) carriers. Purchases of access services by local exchange carriers, such as defendant, were not taxed because the tax only applied to inter-LATA telecommunications, which local exchange carriers were prohibited from providing. Purchases of access services by resellers were not taxed because of the language "but not for resale" in § 77.52(2)(a)4. The court agreed with plaintiff's argument that there was no rational basis for the legislature's classifying inter-LATA carriers separately from local exchange carriers and resellers for the purpose of taxing the transfer of access services. The court failed to find any substantial distinction between inter-LATA carriers, local exchange carriers, and resellers that justified treating the purchase of access services by an inter-LATA carrier dissimilarly from the same purchase by a local exchange carrier or reseller. Accordingly, the court held that the tax was unconstitutional as a violation of plaintiff's right to equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

144 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Fiedler v. Wisconsin Senate


No. 89-0773-OA


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


155 Wis. 2d 94; 454 N.W.2d 770; 1990 Wisc. LEXIS 239


January 25, 1990, Argued  
May 10, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action for declaratory judgment, rights declared.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Rights Declared.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original action for declaratory judgment, petitioners challenged the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 757.48(1)(a), amended by Wis. Act 355 (1987), which imposed a continuing legal education requirement on attorneys prior to their appointment as guardians ad litem.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners argued that § 757.48(1)(a), as amended, was unconstitutional under the separation of powers doctrine, and that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The court found that the statute improperly intruded on a regulation of the practice of law that was exclusively within the province of the judiciary. Thus, the court held that the statute was void as an unconstitutional violation of the separation of powers doctrine. The court concluded that while the legislature could prescribe minimum standards for the eligibility of persons desiring to practice law, it was the province of the judiciary ultimately to decide the fitness of those who practiced before it and to regulate their activities following their admission to practice. A concomitant of this authority was the power to decide whether special training for a particular area was appropriate. The court noted that it had never authorized the legislature to adopt rules or enact legislation attempting to establish a threshold level of competency to practice in a particular area.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petitioners' request for relief and ruled that the statute was unconstitutional and void.

Employers Ins. of Wausau v. Smith


No. 88-2102


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


154 Wis. 2d 199; 453 N.W.2d 856; 1990 Wisc. LEXIS 105

April 6, 1990, Decided

Appeal and Cross-Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County: Susan Steingass, Circuit Judge.
Employers Ins. of Wausau v. Smith, 443 N.W.2d 314, 1989 Wisc. LEXIS 517 (Wis., 1989)



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state treasurer appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which issued a declaratory judgment determining the rights of plaintiffs and defendant under the Wisconsin Unclaimed Property Acts, Wis. Stat. ch. 177, as they related to uncashed worker's compensation benefit checks.


OVERVIEW: Defendant state treasurer appealed from part of a judgment declaring that the Wisconsin Unclaimed Property Acts (Acts), Wis. Stat. ch. 177, did not apply to uncashed worker's compensation benefit checks in uncontested cases and that the five-year period for the presumption of abandonment applied prospectively only. Defendant contested the part of the judgment declaring that the statute of limitations did not bar defendant's cause of action. On appeal, the court ruled that plaintiffs' statutory obligation represented by an uncashed check in an uncontested case possessed the requisite degree of certainty to come within the Acts' definitions of intangible property. Thus, the court reversed the lower court's holding that Wis. Stat. § 177.02(1) applied prospectively only.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, stating that defendant's cause of action was not barred by the statute of limitations.

Order to Pay Attorneys Fees in State v. Newman


No. 88-1689


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


153 Wis. 2d 1; 449 N.W.2d 601; 1990 Wisc. LEXIS 1


September 7, 1989, Argued  
January 3, 1990, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On bypass from Court of Appeals.

Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Door County, Dennis C. Luebke, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The order of the circuit court is modified and, as modified, is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of the order of the Circuit Court of Door County (Wisconsin), which required the county to pay the fees of respondent attorney for her representation of a criminal defendant. The court granted the parties' joint petition to bypass the intermediate court.


OVERVIEW: The attorney was appointed by the lower court to represent a defendant in a criminal matter. The county public defender's office had declined to represent the defendant, and he had been unable to secure the services of an attorney, at county expense, at the rates published in Wis. Supreme Ct. R. 81.02 (1988). The trial court determined that the defendant was entitled to representation, and that fees in excess of the published hourly rates were warranted. The attorney represented the defendant and the trial court ordered the county to pay them. The county declined to pay the attorney's fees above the published rates. The trial court issued an order commanding the county to pay the fees, and it held the county board members in contempt for refusing to pay the fees. The county appealed, but the court affirmed. The court held that the trial court had the authority to order the county, in extraordinary circumstances, to pay fees in excess of the published rates. The court further held that the trial court's order was appropriate under the circumstances presented to it. Finally, the court granted the county time in which to purge the lower court's contempt order.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order of the circuit court ordering the county to pay the fees and, as modified, affirmed the lower court's judgment.

State v. McManus


Nos. 87-1815-CR, 88-0951


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


152 Wis. 2d 113; 447 N.W.2d 654; 1989 Wisc. LEXIS 102


September 8, 1989, Argued  
November 15, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from the court of appeals.

Case No. 87-1815-CR: Appeal from a judgment of conviction of the Circuit Court for Dane County.

Case No. 88-0951: Appeal from a judgment of conviction of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgments of conviction of the circuit courts in State v. McManus and State v. Pangman are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The action was before the court on certification from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin). Defendants challenged their convictions driving or operating a motor vehicle with 0.1 grams or more of alcohol in 210 liters of breath in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendants contended that the circuit court committed various errors. In affirming, the court held that: (1) § 34.63(1)(b) unambiguously set forth a per se breath violation that rendered irrelevant evidence of the partition ratio utilized by the Intoxilyzer 5000 and a defendant's particular partition ratio; (2) the breath provision of § 346.63(1)(b) did not violate due process or equal protection; (3) by approving the Intoxilyzer 5000 as means of measuring breath alcohol concentration, the Wisconsin Department of Transportation merely acted in accordance with the authority the legislature granted it pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 343.305(6)(b); (4) Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b) was sufficiently definite to give persons of ordinary intelligence who sought to avoid its penalties fair notice of the prohibited conduct; (5) the circuit court did not abuse its discretion in admitting into evidence the result of Intoxilyzer 5000 breath test results; and (6) the circuit court did not abuse its discretion by admitting into evidence expert testimony as to the degree of impairment caused by a breach alcohol concentration of 0.1 grams of alcohol or more in 210 liters of breath.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions.

 

148 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. N.R.Z. v. G.L.C.


No. 88-1635


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


152 Wis. 2d 97; 447 N.W.2d 533; 1989 Wisc. LEXIS 577


September 7, 1989, Argued  
November 8, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from court of appeals.

Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Dane county, Susan Steingass, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the circuit court is reversed, and the cause is remanded to the circuit court with instructions to dismiss the action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant putative father challenged an order from the circuit court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to dismiss the paternity action filed by the state on behalf of respondent mother for lack of personal jurisdiction. The trial court asserted jurisdiction under Wis. Stat. § 767.01(2)(c). The appeals court certified the appeal to the court for review.


OVERVIEW: The mother visited the putative father in Florida and had a baby nine months later. The father visited Wisconsin once for a matter of hours and spoke with the mother. The state provided support to the child and filed a paternity action against the putative father, a Florida resident, on behalf of the mother. The father's motion to dismiss was denied, but on appeal, the court reversed, holding that the father's contacts with Wisconsin were insufficient to satisfy the demands of due process. Section 767.01(2)(c) was not facially invalid because it raised only a rebuttable presumption that the exercise of jurisdiction over a nonresident defendant was constitutional. The putative father rebutted the presumption. His brief visit to Wisconsin was not of such quality and nature that it may be said that he purposefully availed himself of the privilege of conducting activities within the state. Also, the fact that the child resides in this state was not sufficient to require the putative father to answer to suit in this state. The failure to pay support may not be considered a jurisdictional contact with the state until a defendant is found liable for child support under Wisconsin law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order denying the putative father's motion to dismiss, and the court remanded the cause with instructions to dismiss the action.

 

149 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Richards v. Young


No. 87-1874


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


150 Wis. 2d 549; 441 N.W.2d 742; 1989 Wisc. LEXIS 86


June 1, 1989, Submitted on briefs  
June 28, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Reversing 145 Wis. 2d 322, 426 N.W.2d 117 (Ct. App. 1988).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a prison superintendent and a director of prison programs, appealed an order of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals, which reversed the dismissal of plaintiff inmate's action. The action sought to order defendants to make several changes in the administrative rules relating to the hobby program at the prison.


OVERVIEW: The inmate commenced an action against defendants, seeking to make defendants institute several changes in the hobby program at the prison. The inmate also served the state attorney general's office and the fiance committee. However, the inmate did not serve the Joint Committee for Review of Administrative Rules (JCRAR). The trial court dismissed the action on the basis that the trial court did not have subject matter jurisdiction because the inmate did not serve the JCRAR. The inmate appealed. The court held that Wis. Stat. §§ 227.40(1), 806.04(11) clearly required service on the JCRAR in a manner that would allow the JCRAR to discuss the case with the joint committee on legislative organization. Thus, the service had to be made within 60 days after filing the complaint. Wis. Stat. §§ 227.40(1), 806.04(11) were clear and unambiguous. The obvious and ordinary meaning of Wis. Stat. §§ 227.40(1), 806.04(11) were that the summons and complaint had to be served upon the JCRAR within 60 days after filing. Because the JCRAR was not served within 60 days, the trial court could not proceed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the appellate court, which reversed the trial court's dismissal of the inmate's action.

Gerhardt v. Estate of Moore


No. 85-0943


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


150 Wis. 2d 563; 441 N.W.2d 734; 1989 Wisc. LEXIS 87


May 31, 1989, Argued  
June 28, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On remand from United States Supreme Court. Reversing and remanding for further proceedings 139 Wis. 2d 833, 407 N.W.2d 895 (1987).

Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Sauk County, Judge J.R. Seering.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The order of the circuit court is reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nonmarital child, by her guardian at litem, appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Sauk County (Wisconsin), which dismissed the child's action against defendant father for additional child support. The court affirmed the circuit court's order, but its decision was vacated by the United States Supreme Court, which remanded the matter for further consideration in light of a recent decision.


OVERVIEW: The child's mother filed an action against the father, seeking to adjudicate paternity and seeking contribution for the child's support. The mother and father subsequently entered into an agreement, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 52.28 (1967), whereby the father admitted paternity and agreed to a lump-sum payment for support. The father fully complied with the terms of the agreement. However, after the father's obligations ended, the child filed suit to obtain additional support. The court held that: (1) because marital children were not precluded from seeking additional child support notwithstanding a prior court order setting the amount of support, prohibiting nonmarital children involved in lump-sum settlement agreements from seeking additional support amounted to a denial of equal protection; (2) consistent with prior Wisconsin case law prohibiting retroactive increases in child support involving marital children, the child was entitled to seek increased child support only from the date that her action was filed and notice given; and (3) given that the father was deceased and his body cremated, the facts of the case precluded disturbing the admission of paternity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's order dismissing the child's action and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

151 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Migliorino


Nos. 88-0426-CR, 88-1147-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


150 Wis. 2d 513; 442 N.W.2d 36; 1989 Wisc. LEXIS 88


June 1, 1989, Argued  
June 28, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from the Court of Appeals.

Appeal (Case No. 88-0426-CR) from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Honorable Thomas P. Doherty, Circuit Judge.

Appeal from Judgments (Case No. 88-1147-CR) of conviction in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Honorable Patricia D. McMahon, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county, Honorable Thomas Doherty, judge, dismissing the criminal complaint against Monica Migliorino and Edmund Miller is reversed. The cause is remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion. The judgments of conviction by the circuit court for Milwaukee county, Honorable Patricia McMahon, judge, are affirmed. The order of probation issued in the case of State v. Haines, et al., for Carol Robbins is vacated and the matter is remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In separate cases consolidated for appeal, defendant protesters challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted them of criminal trespass to a medical facility in violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.145 and denied their challenge to the constitutionality of § 943.145. The state challenged the order of a different circuit court, which found that § 943.145 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In two separate actions, protesters disrupted the function of abortion clinics and were charged with violating § 943.145. The protesters in both cases alleged that § 943.145 was unconstitutional. Two circuit courts split and one held that § 943.145 was constitutional and the other held that it was not. The protesters and the state appealed. The court affirmed the finding that § 943.145 was constitutional and reversed the decision that held that it was not. Abortion clinics were clearly within the protection of § 943.145. The protestors' free speech rights were not unconstitutionally restricted by § 943.145 because it was content neutral and a reasonable regulation in furtherance of significant state interests. The First Amendment did not forbid the viewpoint-neutral exclusion of the speakers' disruption of a nonpublic forum. Section 943.145 was not void for vagueness. Labor was not provided with additional rights under § 943.145 because it merely restated the rights that labor already possessed under Wis. Stat. 103.53, and there was no conduct that was legal under one section and not the other. The protestor who refused probation was within her rights to choose incarceration.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order, which dismissed criminal trespass to a medical facility charges against the protesters. The court affirmed the order of the other circuit court, which convicted the other protestors of the same charges. The order of probation issued over the objection of one of the protestors was vacated and remanded.

153 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Clearfield v. Cushman


No. 87-0420


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


150 Wis. 2d 10; 440 N.W.2d 777; 1989 Wisc. LEXIS 75


March 1, 1989, Argued  
June 7, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Reversing 143 Wis. 2d 553, 421 N.W.2d 865 (Ct. App. 1988).

Review of a decision by the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town brought an action against defendant landowner to have a mobile home removed from the landowner's property. The Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) reversed the trial court's award of summary judgment to the town, holding that the town's ordinance was a "zoning ordinance" that required approval by the county board and that the town lacked statutory authority to regulate mobile homes outside of mobile home parks.


OVERVIEW: The town alleged that the landowner violated an ordinance that required him to apply for or receive a building permit, established a minimum size for the mobile home, and required the home to have a septic tank or well. The landowner argued that the ordinance was a zoning ordinance that had been preempted by a zoning ordinance adopted by the county. On review, the court held that the landowner only had standing to challenge those provisions of the ordinance that were being enforced against him. The court held that the ordinance was not a zoning ordinance because it did not regulate the use of property by the establishment of zones or districts. Rather, the ordinance established minimal requirements for land to be used as a mobile home site. Because the town was responsible for providing fire protection and assessing taxes, the building permit requirement was valid. The sewage system and well requirement was also valid because the town was responsible for removing sewage that constituted a nuisance. There was no justification for the size requirement for the mobile home, but the court held that the clause was severable from the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the intermediary appellate court which held that the town's ordinance regarding mobile homes was an invalid zoning ordinance and that the town lacked statutory authority to regulate mobile homes outside of trailer parks.

Klinger v. Oneida County


No. 87-2250


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


149 Wis. 2d 838; 440 N.W.2d 348; 1989 Wisc. LEXIS 62

May 26, 1989, Decided

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board of adjustment sought review of a decision of the court of appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed an order granting a variance to respondent applicant from a county zoning ordinance that limited repairs to a nonconforming mobile home.


OVERVIEW: The applicant sought a variance to make repairs to his mobile home. The home did not meet the zoning ordinance set back requirements. After a hearing and two inspections, the board denied his application. The applicant argued that the common-law certiorari standard of review did not apply in the case because the circuit court took evidence on the merits of the administrative decision pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 59.99(10). He argued that even if the evidence before the circuit court was the same as that before the board, the circuit court had to come to its own decision about granting a variance giving little if any deference to the board's decision. The court upheld the judgment of the court of appeals, holding that the circuit court should have applied the common-law certiorari standard of review. The legislature vested discretion in the board and did not intend the circuit court to substitute its discretion for that committed to the board. The applicant acknowledged that he could have constructed a dwelling in conformity to the ordinance. Therefore, the ordinance did not deny him an economically viable use of his property and his constitutional rights were not violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals reversing the circuit court's grant of the variance.

Milwaukee v. Nelson


No. 86-2234-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


149 Wis. 2d 434; 439 N.W.2d 562; 1989 Wisc. LEXIS 51


November 2, 1988, Argued  
May 11, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming 142 Wis. 2d 944, 419 N.W.2d 573 (Ct. App. 1988).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner loiterer sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed an order holding that Milwaukee, Wis., Ordinance 106-31(1)(a) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad and that the ordinance and Wis. Stat. § 800.02(6) contravened U.S. Const. amend. IV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner loiterer was convicted of loitering under Milwaukee, Wis., Ordinance 106-31(1)(a) and brought a declaratory judgment action alleging the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. He also contended that the ordinance and Wis. Stat. § 800.02(6) contravened U.S. Const. amend. IV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11. The trial court agreed with him, but the appellate court reversed. On further appeal, the court affirmed the reversal, holding that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. The court held that the ordinance allowed only for arrest where there was probable cause to believe the ordinance had been violated, and thus, respondent city had not exceeded its power. The court held the definition of loitering was properly limited as to scope, place, or purpose. The court held that neither the ordinance nor § 800.02(6) contravened U.S. Const. amend. IV and Wis. Const. art. I, § 11 because they provided sufficient protection by giving one an opportunity to explain oneself to avoid arbitrary arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the reversal of an order holding a loitering statute unconstitutionally vague and overbroad in petitioner loiterer's declaratory judgment action. The ordinance allowed only for arrest where there was probable cause to believe the ordinance had been violated, and thus, respondent city had not exceeded its power. The definition of loitering was properly limited as to scope, place, or purpose.

 

157 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sher


No. 87-1568-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


149 Wis. 2d 1; 437 N.W.2d 878; 1989 Wisc. LEXIS 38


November 3, 1988, Argued  
April 4, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from court of appeals.

Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order of the circuit court is reversed and the cause remanded for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appeal from an order by the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which dismissed a criminal complaint on the grounds that the six year statute of limitations was not tolled during the time defendant was "publicly a resident" of Florida.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the running of the statute of limitations had been tolled pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 939.74(3) on the theory that defendant was not publicly a resident of the state of Wisconsin for a period of years between the alleged offense and the filing of the criminal complaint. The court concluded that the protection provided by the statute of limitations, which could not be found explicitly or implicitly in the United States Constitution, and which was subject to the control of the legislature, was not a fundamental right. The court found that the legislature's decision to establish a tolling provision for nonresidents was substantially related to the problems of identifying criminals, detecting crime, and apprehending alleged criminals, when nonresidents might have been involved or had vital information. Although the tolling provision of the statute of limitations, § 939.74(3), disadvantaged nonresidents compared to residents, it did not infringe on any fundamental right and it was substantially related to legitimate state interests. The court determined that § 939.74(3) did not violate the Privileges and Immunities Clause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court. The court remanded the cause for further proceedings not inconsistent with the opinion of the court.

Oak Creek v. King


No. 87-1305


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


148 Wis. 2d 532; 436 N.W.2d 285; 1989 Wisc. LEXIS 21; 16 Media L. Rep. 1273


November 30, 1988, Argued  
February 23, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from court of appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Clarence R. Parrish, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which found him guilty of disorderly conduct in violation of a municipal ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was adjudged guilty in the municipal court of disorderly conduct in violation of a municipal ordinance. The circuit court conducted a trial de novo and found defendant guilty of disorderly conduct, and defendant appealed. The court of appeals requested certification to the court which was granted. The court held that defendant's conduct violated the municipal disorderly conduct ordinance because his repeated refusal to obey a detective's reasonable order, combined with his continued penetration into a nonpublic restricted area in the presence of the general public, was conduct of a type which tended to be disruptive of good order and tended to cause or provoke a disturbance, under the circumstances as they then existed at the site of the airplane crash. The court held that the ordinance as applied was not void for vagueness. The court held that denying defendant, as a news gatherer, access to the scene of the airplane crash did not violate his U.S. Const. amend. I rights. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision finding defendant guilty of disorderly conduct in violation of a municipal ordinance because his conduct was of a type which tended to cause or provoke a disturbance, the ordinance as applied was not unconstitutionally vague, and defendant as a news gatherer had no U.S. Const. amend. I right of access to the scene of an airplane crash beyond the general public's right to access.

 

160 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Kukor v. Grover


No. 86-1544


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


148 Wis. 2d 469; 436 N.W.2d 568; 1989 Wisc. LEXIS 22


November 1, 1988, Argued  
February 22, 1989, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for Reconsideration Denied April 12, 1989, with $ 50 Costs.


PRIOR HISTORY: On certification from court of appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County, William C. Sachtjen, Reserve Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), certified by the court of appeals, which found that the Wisconsin system of school finance was constitutional, meeting the requirement of Wis. Const. art. X, § 3 that the establishment of district schools was as nearly uniform as practicable, and did not violate the equal protection provision of Wis. Const. art. I, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The citizens brought an action challenging the constitutionality of Wisconsin's public school finance system alleging that the system failed to provide practically uniform school districts as required under Wis. Const. art. X, § 3, and violated the equal protection provision of Wis. Const. art. I, § 1. The circuit court found the finance system to be constitutional. The court first noted that in its review of the circuit court's findings of evidentiary or historical fact, the court would uphold those findings unless they were clearly erroneous. The court agreed with the circuit court that the school finance system, as set forth in Wis. Stat. § 121, did not unconstitutionally impinge upon the uniformity requirements of Wis. Const. art. X, § 3. The education clause in the constitution providing for a general and uniform public school system only created a fundamental right to basic education. Additionally, there was a rational basis justifying any disparities in per-pupil expenditures resulting from the operation of Wis. Stat. § 121; the rational basis being the preservation of local control over education as mandated by Wis. Const. art. X.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing the citizens' complaint.

Funk v. Wollin Silo & Equipment, Inc.


No. 86-2089


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


148 Wis. 2d 59; 435 N.W.2d 244; 1989 Wisc. LEXIS 17


October 4, 1988, Argued  
February 14, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from the court of appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Rock County, Patrick J. Rude, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment is reversed and the cause is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners brought a complaint alleging damages caused by the negligent construction of a silo by defendant equipment company. Plaintiffs appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their complaint.


OVERVIEW: The owners contracted with equipment company to build a silo on their property. Almost seven years later, owner fell and was injured. He alleged the injuries were proximately caused by the negligence of equipment company and the ladder was defective when it was installed. The lower court dismissed the action finding that under Wis. Stat. Ann. § 893.89, the period within which the action could be brought had expired. Because a case held a somewhat similar predecessor statute unconstitutional, the court expressed doubt whether the deficiencies noted in that case had been sufficiently corrected and certified the case to the court. The court found that owners had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute. The court found that the statute was unconstitutional on equal protection grounds, because it afforded its protection and favors without a reasonable and rational basis. The statute made a distinction between people who plan, design and construct and those who own or occupy the land. The statute set a time limit following the completion of a construction project when no action could be brought but did not state why that time limit was in the interest of the public.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

 

162 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jackson


Nos. 87-1374-CR, 87-1375-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


147 Wis. 2d 824; 434 N.W.2d 386; 1989 Wisc. LEXIS 8


November 3, 1988, Argued  
January 25, 1989, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from court of appeals.

Appeal from judgments of the circuit court for Racine county, Judge Emmanuel J. Vuvunas.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgments of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of judgments entered in the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin) that convicted him, pursuant to his no contest pleas, of attempted robbery as party to a crime and of burglary as party to a crime.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that a police officer did not have specific and articulable facts that amounted to reasonable suspicion of criminal activity; therefore, he claimed that the initial stop of defendant was unconstitutional. The State argued that the reasonable suspicion to suspect defendant of some past or present unlawful criminal activity arose from defendant's actions in fleeing from the police officer that sought to investigate a reported stabbing. Further, the State argued that a fellow officer's report that the individual who had fled from the scene of the alleged stabbing had warrants also justified the stop. The court agreed with the State and rejected defendant's argument. The court pointed out that Wis. Stat. § 968.24, which authorized investigative stops, focused on the reasonableness of the police officer's suspicions under all the facts and circumstances. Here, the police officer was investigating a stabbing report when he saw defendant who immediately ran away. The officer pursued him on foot but lost him. These circumstances made it reasonable for the police officer to form a suspicion that defendant was committing, was about to commit, or had committed a crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments that convicted defendant of attempted armed robbery as party to a crime and of burglary as party to a crime.

Ziegler Co. v. Rexnord, Inc.


No. 86-0462


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


147 Wis. 2d 308; 433 N.W.2d 8; 1988 Wisc. LEXIS 107


September 6, 1988, Argued  
December 22, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On motion for reconsideration, cause remanded for further proceedings 139 Wis. 2d 593, 407 N.W.2d 873 (1987).

On Motion For Reconsideration.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff dealer and defendant grantor both moved the court to reconsider its decision that reversed the decision of the court of appeals and the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings on the issue of whether dealer was grantor's "dealer" as defined in the Wisconsin Fair Dealership Law, Wis. Stat. § 135.01 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Both parties agreed to most of the basic facts of the case and believed that the undisputed facts provided the court with a sufficient basis to determine the good cause issue. The court disagreed and found that the undisputed facts of the record provided an insufficient basis upon which the court could determine the good cause issue. Therefore, the court remanded for further proceedings on both the issue of whether a dealership existed and on the issue of good cause. The parties could present more evidence in support of the motions for summary judgment, and then the trial court could determine whether there was sufficient evidence to demonstrate that there remained no genuine issue of material fact. The court held that the grantor's economic circumstances may constitute good cause to alter its method of doing business with its dealers, but such changes must be essential, reasonable and nondiscriminatory. Only the trier of fact could determine what was essential, reasonable and nondiscriminatory under the facts of this case.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the trial court to determine the issues of dealership and good cause in the order which will most effectively conserve judicial time.

 

164 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Milwaukee v. K.F.


Nos. 87-0936, 87-0937


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


145 Wis. 2d 24; 426 N.W.2d 329; 1988 Wisc. LEXIS 74


May 31, 1988, Argued  
July 20, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On bypass of the court of appeals.

Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Christopher R. Foley, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The order of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant youths challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied a motion to dismiss, found that appellants violated a curfew, found the ordinance constitutional, and ordered suspended sentences. Appellants asserted that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad under the First and Fourteenth Amendments of the United States Constitution and similar provisions of the Wisconsin Constitution.


OVERVIEW: While attending a public dance sponsored by a minority university organization to promote higher education, appellant youths were arrested for violating a city youth curfew. Their sentences were suspended, but they challenged the constitutionality of the ordinance. The court found that a function in which such a large number of young people were assembled unequivocally constituted the act of congregating as used in the ordinance and that the building was public within the terms of the ordinance. The court found that although some adults were present, the individualized supervision contemplated by the ordinance was absent. The court found that appellants were within the regulated age and involved in conduct in a place unambiguously proscribed by the ordinance, so they did not have standing to challenge it as unconstitutionally vague. The court found the city's interest in protecting young people and curtailing juvenile crime compelling and that the ordinance was drawn as narrowly as practicable. The order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order, finding the curfew ordinance constitutional. The court found the ordinance supported by the compelling interest of the city in controlling the nighttime activities of young people in order to protect them and the community from juvenile crime. Appellant youths did not have standing to challenge the ordinance for vagueness, and it was not overly broad.

Brookfield v. Milwaukee Metropolitan Sewerage Dist.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sewerage district challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Waukesha County (Wisconsin) striking down, at plaintiff municipalities' behest, a state statute authorizing defendant to charge communities within its region for providing services.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff municipalities brought suit against defendant sewerage district, claiming that a state statute authorizing charges to communities included with defendant's regional area was unconstitutional. A trial judge held that the statute was indeed unconstitutional, and defendant appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the statute was indeed unconstitutional, inasmuch as the state constitution required statutes having private or local effect to be passed in bills with an unmistakably clear title. The statute in this case violated that constitutional provision, and hence it was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, as the statute in question was unconstitutional due to its lack of an unmistakable title, as required for laws having private and local affect.

State v. Thomas


No. 87-0729-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


144 Wis. 2d 876; 425 N.W.2d 641; 1988 Wisc. LEXIS 65


June 1, 1988, Argued  
June 28, 1988, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion For Reconsideration Granted on August 23, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY: On certification from the court of appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county, Judge Laurence C. Gram.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of first-degree sexual assault of an eight-year-old child. Defendant also appealed from an order denying post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the use of a videotaped deposition of the child's testimony at trial, pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 967.04(7)-(10), and the placement of a screen between himself and the child during the deposition, as an unconstitutional denial of his right to confront his accuser. The court concluded that §§ 967.04(7)-(10), as it pertained to child-witnesses under 12 years of age, did not deprive defendant of his right to confrontation. The court held that defendant failed to demonstrate that Wis. Stat. § 967.04(7)-(10), as it pertained to children under 12 years of age, denied an accused the fundamental protections of the right of confrontation. Accordingly, the court upheld the statute as constitutional. The court rejected defendant's argument that the statute was facially invalid. Finally, the court found nothing of a prejudicial nature to defendant in the entire tape.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the denial of post-conviction relief.

 

167 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mitchell


No. 86-0879-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


144 Wis. 2d 596; 424 N.W.2d 698; 1988 Wisc. LEXIS 68


April 26, 1988, Argued  
June 24, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Reversing 139 Wis. 2d 856, 407 N.W.2d 566 (Ct. App. 1987).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals that reversed defendant's conviction for first-degree sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction for first-degree sexual assault was reversed by an appellate court. On further appeal, the court reversed the appellate court's judgment. Defendant was not entitled to a Franks hearing on his motion to suppress test results for gonorrhea. Although defendant disputed an affidavit statement that a doctor said the first test for gonorrhea, which was negative, was incorrectly performed, ample evidence remained without the challenged statement to establish probable cause to issue a warrant for a second test, which was positive. It was error to allow testimony that the complainant was a virgin. The evidence of "prior sexual conduct" barred by Wis. Stat. § 972.11(2)(b) included lack of prior sexual conduct. Because the evidence of the complainant's prior sexual conduct did not fall within the three exceptions listed in the statute, the evidence was inadmissible. However, the error was harmless. The complainant's identification of defendant as her assailant was the primary issue at trial. The complainant was eleven years old, consent was not an issue, and the jury would not have given more credence to her testimony merely because she testified that she was a virgin.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that reversed defendant's conviction for first-degree sexual assault.

 

168 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Racine Steel Castings v. Hardy


No. 86-1016


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


144 Wis. 2d 553; 426 N.W.2d 33; 1988 Wisc. LEXIS 53


April 25, 1988, Argued  
June 16, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Reversing 139 Wis. 2d 232, 407 N.W.2d 299 (Ct. App. 1987).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged the Court of Appeals' (Wisconsin) affirmance of a trial court's judgment that Wis. Stat. § 102.29(3) was unconstitutional and that respondent employer was entitled to subrogation against proceeds of the employee's medical malpractice claim. The trial court held that § 102.29(3) denied equal protection to employers whose employees' work-related injuries were aggravated by doctors, chiropractors or podiatrists.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured at work and a surgery rendered him a quadriplegic. He filed a negligence claim against the doctor and obtained a settlement. The employer sought subrogation of workers' compensation benefits that it had paid against the proceeds. However, § 102.29(3) barred employers from recovering worker's compensation sums from amounts awarded in a malpractice action for the aggravation of an injury by a physician, chiropractor, or podiatrist. The employer alleged that § 102.29(3) violated the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. Amend. XIV because there was no rational basis for barring reimbursement from awards against a physician, chiropractor, or podiatrist, while permitting such reimbursement from awards in all other third-party actions, including those against other health care providers. The appellate court held § 102.29(3) unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed. While § 102.29(3) was under-inclusive, the imperfect exclusion of the other providers had a rational basis in that those named generally had a greater likelihood of injury in the event of malpractice because they were the best equipped to assess disability and treat work-related injury.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that was in favor of the employer and found the subrogation statute constitutional.

State ex rel. Wisconsin Senate v. Thompson


No. 87-1750-OA


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


144 Wis. 2d 429; 424 N.W.2d 385; 1988 Wisc. LEXIS 56


October 20, 1987, Argued  
June 14, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Action For Declaratory Judgment.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- It is declared and adjudged: (1) That those parts of enrolled 1987 Senate Bill 100 passed by the legislature but vetoed by the governor pursuant to art. V., sec. 10 of the Wisconsin Constitution, were, in accordance therewith, duly vetoed and returned to the legislature with the governor's objections thereto, and were then refused passage. (2) That by virtue of passage by the legislature and approval in part by the governor, 1987 Wisconsin Act 27 was validly enacted, and, upon the publication thereof, in accordance with sec. 21, art. VII, of the constitution, and sec. 991.11, Stats., became and now is in force and effect as law. No questions concerning the validity of 1987 Wisconsin Act 27, other than those relating to the approval, enactment, and publication thereof, are now determined. Relief denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In this original action for declaratory judgment and supplemental injunctive relief, petitioners, congressional members of the Wisconsin legislature and taxpayers, sought a declaration that respondent Wisconsin governor exceeded his constitutional partial veto authority when he vetoed phrases, digits, letters, and word fragments in the 1987-89 biennial budget bill.


OVERVIEW: The congressional members sought a declaration that the governor exceeded his partial veto authority when he vetoed phrases, digits, letters, and word fragments in a budget bill. The governor interposed four affirmative defenses, arguing the members lacked (1) capacity or (2) standing to sue; (3) the separation of powers would be violated by allowing the legislative branch to sue the executive branch before the judicial branch; and (4) no justiciable controversy. The court rejected all the affirmative defenses, at least in part because the congressional members were also suing as taxpayers. The court proceeded to a resolution of the merits. The court found the governor properly exercised his partial veto authority under Wis. Const. art. V, § 10 with respect to the 37 identified vetoes challenged in this case. Under Wisconsin law, the governor was entitled to exercise his veto power by removing provisos and conditions to an appropriation so long as the net result was a complete, entire, and workable bill which could have been passed in the first instance. Moreover, he had the power to reduce appropriations by striking numbers or digits. The governor's vetoes were proper.


OUTCOME: The court declared the rights of the parties and declared that the congressional members were not entitled to the prayed for relief.
