Kohnke v. St. Paul Fire & Marine Ins. Co.


No. 86-0988


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


144 Wis. 2d 352; 424 N.W.2d 191; 1988 Wisc. LEXIS 58


April 25, 1988, Argued  
June 8, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming 140 Wis. 2d 80, 410 N.W.2d 585 (Ct. App. 1987).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed and the cause remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a medical facility and its insurer, appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed the judgment of the circuit court granting defendants' summary judgment motions and finding that plaintiff patient's claim for injuries he allegedly sustained when he was five months old was barred by the personal injury statutes of limitation, Wis. Stat. §§ 330.205 and 330.33 (1959).


OVERVIEW: In October 1961, a doctor negligently performed a bilateral hydrocele repair on the patient, rendering him sterile. He was five months old. The patient did not discover the injury until December 1983, when he consulted a physician because he and his wife had been unable to conceive a child. The patient filed a complaint, within one year of discovering his sterility, against the medical facility where the doctor had worked and its insurer. The circuit court granted summary judgment to defendants, but on appeal it was reversed. The court affirmed the appellate court's decision. The court found that §§ 330.205 and 330.33, in effect at the time of the patient's treatment, controlled the statutory limitation period to be applied. The court determined that the later-created discovery rule applied because it specifically applied to all legislation without provision for diligent discovery of latent injury. The court concluded that because the patient timely filed his claim within three years of discovering his injuries, his action was not barred. The court noted that defendants were not denied due process because their right to a statutory bar did not vest prior to the filing of the claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals and remanded the matter to the circuit court.

 

171 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Ripley v. Brown


No. 86-2027


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


143 Wis. 2d 686; 422 N.W.2d 608; 1988 Wisc. LEXIS 35


February 2, 1988, Argued  
April 26, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Reversing and remanding 141 Wis. 2d 447, 415 N.W.2d 550 (Ct. App. 1987).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decision reversed and cause remanded to the circuit court with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant sought to have a portion of Wis. Stat. § 59.12, which allowed the officer of county surveyor in counties of under 500,000 population to be an appointive position, rather than an elective office, declared unconstitutional. Defendants, county and county clerk, appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed a summary judgment dismissing the applicant's petition.


OVERVIEW: The applicant sought to have his name added to the ballot for the position of county surveyor. However, the county had appointed a county surveyor and was not putting that position on the ballot. The applicant argued that Wis. Stat. § 59.12, which allowed the office of county surveyor in counties of under 500,000 population to be an appointive position, rather than an elective office, was unconstitutional. The court disagreed. The court found that the county surveyor was not a "principal head" of county government who exercised governmental and political powers. The office of county survey was a "minor" one. Some evidence that the county surveyor was not a political or governmental county officer was found in the fact that the county surveyor, unlike most principal heads of county government, was not required to keep offices at the county seat. Because the county surveyor was a "minor" officer, the legislature could direct, under Wis. Const. art. XIII, § 9, that the position be filled either by election or appointment. Thus, the statute was not unconstitutional and the appellate court's decision was reversed.


OUTCOME: The decision of the appellate court was reversed and the cause was remanded to the trial court with directions to dismiss the applicant's petition.

 

172 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. McCoy


No. 86-1992-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


143 Wis. 2d 274; 421 N.W.2d 107; 1988 Wisc. LEXIS 13


February 3, 1988, Argued  
March 22, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming 139 Wis. 2d 291, 407 N.W.2d 319 (Ct. App. 1987).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) that affirmed a circuit court judgment, entered after a jury trial, that convicted him of violating Wis. Stat. § 946.715(1)(a) by intentionally concealing two of his minor children from their other parent. The court of appeals held that § 946.715(1)(a) was not unconstitutionally vague and that the circuit court committed no reversible error in instructing the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant testified that he concealed his two older children from his wife for more than a year because she had been abusing them so frequently and severely that he feared for their safety. The wife testified that she did not abuse the children. The court affirmed the judgment. Defendant's constitutional challenge to § 946.715 presented a compelling basis for review although he raised it for the first time on appeal. The phrase "imminent physical harm" in § 946.715 was not unconstitutionally vague. Although it was not defined in the statute, its terms were commonly used and understood by the general populace and it gave reasonable notice of proscribed conduct to persons bent on obedience and to those charged with enforcing it. The circuit court did not err in instructing the jury. Its use of the phrase "reasonably necessary" and the word "immediate" did not establish too stringent a test and a reasonableness standard was appropriate. The circuit court did not unduly limit the meaning of "imminent physical harm" by failing to describe it as including continuing or projected harm or by failing to include emotional as well as bodily harm in its definition of "physical injury."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the intermediate court of appeals that affirmed the circuit court judgment convicting defendant of intentionally concealing his two minor children from their other parent.

 

173 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re K.C.


No. 87-0052


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


142 Wis. 2d 906; 420 N.W.2d 37; 1988 Wisc. LEXIS 29


December 1, 1987, Argued  
February 25, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On bypass from court of appeals.

Appeal from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee county: Frederick P. Kessler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The order of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents of incarcerated juveniles sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which ordered them to pay respondent Wisconsin Department of Health and Social Services for the care and maintenance of their children while in the Department's custody at a secured correctional facility under Wis. Stat. § 46.10 (1985-86).


OVERVIEW: The Department brought suit against the parents pursuant to § 46.10 to require them to pay the Department for the care and maintenance of their children while in the Department's custody at a secured correctional facility. The trial court ordered the parents to pay the Department and denied the parents' motions to dismiss the suit, holding that § 46.10 was constitutional. Upon review the court affirmed, holding that there was a rational basis for the legislature's decision to charge for the cost of care and maintenance received by juveniles while exempting adults from similar liability. The court held that while the incarceration of adults was designed primarily to protect the public and punish the individual, the confinement of juveniles focused primarily upon rehabilitating the juvenile. The court held that the difference in the nature of the confinement provided a rational basis for § 46.10. The court thus held that § 46.10 did not violate the parents' equal protection rights. The court also held that because § 46.10 only continued the parents' continuing duty to support their children under Wis. Stat. § 49.90 (1985-86), the parents were not deprived of their due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which required the parents to pay the Department for the care and maintenance of their children while in the Department's custody at a secured correctional facility.

Appleton v. Menasha


No. 86-2228


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


142 Wis. 2d 870; 419 N.W.2d 249; 1988 Wisc. LEXIS 30


January 5, 1988, Argued  
February 19, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from court of appeals.

Appeal from an order of the circuit court of Outagamie county, James T. Bayorgeon, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The order of the circuit court is reversed and the cause is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Third-party plaintiff taxpayer sought review of an order entered in the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin), which denied the taxpayer's motion to intervene in a proceeding filed by plaintiff City of Appleton against defendant Town of Menosha pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 66.03(5) (1983-84) and dismissed the taxpayer's third-party complaint seeking a declaration of rights to determine the constitutionality of § 66.03(5).


OVERVIEW: The city commenced an action against the town, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 66.03(5) (1983-84), requesting the circuit court to apportion assets and liabilities attributable to the city's annexation of land from the town. The taxpayer, a town resident, filed a motion to intervene and filed a third-party complaint challenging the constitutionality of § 66.03(5). The city claimed that, because the town could not challenge the constitutionality of the statute, the taxpayer was similarly barred. On appeal of the circuit court's order denying the motion to intervene and dismissing the third-party complaint, the court held that the taxpayer had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute because he had a direct and personal pecuniary interest in the action and his action was not coextensive with, or limited by, the town's rights. Noting the distinction between derivative and non-derivative taxpayer actions, the court ruled that the taxpayer was bringing the action on his own behalf and on behalf of taxpayers similarly situated and that his action was non-derivative.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order denying the taxpayer's motion to intervene and dismissing his third-party complaint and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State ex rel. Teunas v. County of Kenosha


No. 86-1425


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


142 Wis. 2d 498; 418 N.W.2d 833; 1988 Wisc. LEXIS 2


December 1, 1987, Argued  
February 11, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification by court of appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the circuit court for Kenosha county, Jerold W. Breitenbach, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the cause is remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant resident challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin) declaring the county's obscenity ordinance, Kenosha County, Wis. Municipal Code § 9.10.2, constitutional, with the exception of § 9.10.2(2)(c), (d), which were found invalid and severed from the ordinance. Respondent county cross-appealed from the portion of the judgment declaring the subsections invalid and granting a permanent injunction.


OVERVIEW: The resident was the owner of a retail establishment in the county and alleged uncertainty regarding his ability to lawfully engage in the sale of certain video tapes. The trial court found that the county board had acted pursuant to its statutory authority under Wis. Stat. § 59.07(64) in passing the obscenity ordinance to preserve good order. The court further found that although the obscenity ordinance dealt with matters of statewide concern, the ordinance was valid as the state had not acted in that area and because the ordinance attempted to deal only with a matter of local concern. The court of appeals certified issues of the case, and on appeal, the court only reached the first of the issues. The court held that county board did not have the statutory authority to enact the obscenity ordinance, as the authority of county boards was limited. The court found that the intent of the legislature in referring in § 59.07(64) to "public peace and good order" was consequently not to be so broadly interpreted as to include the power to regulate obscenity, an area contemporaneously categorized by the legislature as conceptually distinct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding the subsections of the ordinance invalid, but the court reversed that portion of the judgment finding the remainder of the ordinance valid. The matter was remanded with instructions to vacate the injunction and enter a judgment enjoining the enforcement of the ordinance without qualification.

 

176 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Kerkman v. Hintz


No. 86-0215


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


142 Wis. 2d 404; 418 N.W.2d 795; 1988 Wisc. LEXIS 5


November 3, 1987, Argued  
February 11, 1988, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming in part, reversing in part and remanding 138 Wis. 2d 131, 406 N.W.2d 156 (Ct. App. 1987).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed in part, reversed in part, and the cause is remanded for a new trial on the question of negligence only.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a chiropractor and his insurer, challenged an order of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) that reversed a trial court judgment finding defendant chiropractor liable for malpractice in treating plaintiff patient for soreness in shoulders, neck, and hands. Plaintiff, the patient's wife, filed a claim for loss of consortium.


OVERVIEW: The patient consulted with a chiropractor, who performed adjustments on his back. He later went to his family doctor and had two back operations. Two medical experts testified that the chiropractor had not conducted a proper diagnosis of the patient. On appeal, the court affirmed in part as to the remand for a new trial and reversed in part as to the damage award for the patient and his wife. The court abrogated the prior case law that held a chiropractor to a medical standard when diagnosing a patient's ailment. The legislature recognized that the practice of chiropractic was distinct from the practice of medicine. The court found that a chiropractor should not be held to a medical standard. It held that a chiropractor had a duty to determine whether the patient presented a problem which was treatable through chiropractic means, refrain from treatment when a reasonable chiropractor should be award that a patient's condition would not be responsive to further treatment, and inform the patient if the ailment was not treatable through chiropractic means. A chiropractor was held to the degree of care that was exercised by a reasonable chiropractor under like circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part as to the remand for a new trial on negligence. The court reversed in part as to the issues of the patient's damages and his wife's claim for loss of consortium.

State ex rel. Jones v. Gerhardstein


No. 85-1718


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


141 Wis. 2d 710; 416 N.W.2d 883; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 724


September 8, 1987, Argued  
December 21, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming 135 Wis. 2d 161, 400 N.W.2d 1 (Ct. App. 1986).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, state agency and county agency, sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed the trial court's judgment and found the treatment authorization provisions of Wis. Stat. § 51.59 unconstitutional on equal protection grounds. The trial court had dismissed respondent patients' habeas corpus petition for declaratory and injunctive relief from involuntary drug treatment, which commenced the case.


OVERVIEW: The patients had been involuntarily committed to the agencies for psychiatric treatment and were given psychotropic drug treatment without the right to exercise informed consent to the treatment. They sought declaratory and injunctive relief from the statute authorizing the treatment, Wis. Stat. § 51.59. The agencies asserted jurisdictional and mootness grounds and argued that the statute was constitutional. The court rejected the agencies' arguments and found that the patients' petition had been properly filed and served and that it was not moot because of the pressing nature of the issue. The court agreed with the appellate court's determination that § 51.59 was unconstitutional because it violated constitutional guarantees of equal protection. The court specifically pointed to the lack of rational basis for the disparity of treatment of the patients, who were involuntarily committed, and the class of persons held in precommitment detention under §§ 51.15(8) and 51.20(8)(c), who did have the right to refuse psychotropic medication. The court held that competency to choose psychotropic drug treatment should be presumed without a probable cause showing of incompetence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision reversing the trial court's dismissal of the patients' petition and declaring the statutory treatment authorization provisions unconstitutional on state and federal constitutional equal protection grounds.

State v. Anderson


No. 86-0612-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


141 Wis. 2d 653; 416 N.W.2d 276; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 717


September 9, 1987, Argued  
December 10, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming 137 Wis. 2d 267, 404 N.W.2d 100 (Ct. App.).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals reversing the judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee county, Judge Gary Gerlach.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State sought review of the decision from the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which reversed the judgment from the circuit court convicting defendant of possession of a short-barreled shotgun, under Wis. Stat. § 941.28, and possession of a firearm by a felon, under Wis. Stat. § 941.29(2), and ordered a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of a short-barreled shotgun, under Wis. Stat. § 941.28, and possession of a firearm by a felon, under Wis. Stat. § 941.29(2). On appeal, defendant argued that the circuit court erred in excluding statements by a third party, because the statements were admissible under Wis. Stat. § 908.045(4). The intermediate appellate court reversed defendant's convictions and ordered a new trial. On further, the court affirmed the decision from the intermediate appellate court. The court held that the standard of corroboration required by § 908.045(4) was corroboration sufficient to permit a reasonable person to conclude, in light of all the facts and circumstances, that the statement could be true. The circuit court erred by excluding the third party's statements against penal interest and the ruling was not a harmless error. There were more than sufficient facts and circumstances for a reasonable person to conclude that the third party's statements could be true.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from the intermediate appellate court reversing defendant's convictions of possession of a short-barreled shotgun and possession of a firearm by a felon, and ordering a new trial.

Guertin v. Harbour Assurance Co.


No. 85-2316


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


141 Wis. 2d 622; 415 N.W.2d 831; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 719


October 6, 1987, Argued  
December 3, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming 135 Wis. 2d 334, 400 N.W.2d 56 (Ct. App. 1986).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner individual sought review of a decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals, which affirmed a grant of summary judgment in favor of respondent company in the individual's personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: An individual, a Wisconsin resident, challenged a grant of summary judgment to a company on his personal injury action for injuries he sustained in Illinois. On appeal, the court affirmed the grant of summary judgment and held that the trial court correctly applied Wis. Stat. § 893.07. The court found that § 893.07 required the application of the shorter statute of limitations period, where the cause of action arose in another state. The court also found that § 893.07 used the place of injury only to determine which jurisdictions were to be compared in establishing the shorter limitation period. The court further found that § 893.07 obviated the uncertainty where more than one statute of limitation applied to a given case. The court also determined that a rational basis existed for the distinction made under § 893.07 relating to persons injured outside the state. Thus, the court ruled that the individual was not denied equal protection by the application of § 893.07 to his case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment.

State ex rel. Journal/Sentinel, Inc. v. Jennings


No. 87-2086-W


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


141 Wis. 2d 618; 415 N.W.2d 518; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 713



November 25, 1987, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for reconsideration denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: On petition for supervisory writ.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner newspaper appealed from a judgment of the court of appeals (Wisconsin) that denied the newspaper's petition for a supervisory writ of mandamus to compel respondent judges to permit the newspaper to inspect a minor settlement approved by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) in an action and which the trial court ordered sealed.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court ordered sealed a minor settlement in litigation involving certain religious figures. The newspaper filed in the court of appeals a petition for a supervisory writ of mandamus to compel the judges to allow the newspaper to inspect the settlement. The court of appeals denied the petition on the ground that it presented an issue publici juris, which the court of appeals did not have original jurisdiction to entertain. The court held that the court of appeals erred where it concluded that it lacked jurisdiction to consider the supervisory writ petition because of the publici juris nature of the issue it presented. The court held that the matter presented by the petition arguably came within the supervisory jurisdiction of the court of appeals. The court found that the issue of the newspapers' right to inspect the court-approved settlement and supporting documents of record arose in the context of an action in the circuit court, the record of which remained under the control of that court. The court held that the fact that the petition presented an issue publici juris in no way affected the supervisory jurisdiction of the court of appeals to decide the issue.


OUTCOME: The court remanded to the court of appeals a judgment that denied the newspaper's petition for a supervisory writ of mandamus to compel the judges to permit the newspaper to inspect a minor settlement approved by a circuit court.

State ex rel. Stevens v. Circuit Court for Manitowoc County


No. 87-0203-W


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


141 Wis. 2d 239; 414 N.W.2d 832; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 707


September 8, 1987, Argued  
November 4, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from the court of appeals.

Petition For Supervisory Writ.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The petition for supervisory writ is granted. The order of the circuit court is vacated and the cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned the court of appeals (Wisconsin) for a supervisory writ claiming that Wis. Stat. § 970.03(4) violated his Sixth Amendment right to a public trial. He challenged the circuit court's order, which excluded the general public except the news media, from the preliminary examination in a sexual assault case at the request of the State's complaining witness under the mandatory exclusion provision of Wis. Stat. § 970.03(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with seven counts of first degree sexual assault. Under the mandatory exclusion provision of § 970.03(4) and on behalf of the complaining witness, a 14 year old girl, the State requested that the preliminary examination be closed. Defendant objected to closure. The circuit court concluded that allowing the media to attend would accommodate defendant's constitutional rights, while protecting the juvenile victim from unnecessary emotional trauma. On appeal defendant argued that his Sixth Amendment right extended to the preliminary examination and that the § 970.03(4) mandated exclusion unconstitutionally infringed upon that right. The court granted the petition, holding that a preliminary examination was sufficiently analogous in the purposes and aims which supported the public trial requirement that a qualified Sixth Amendment public trial right had to adhere when closure was sought under § 970.03(4). Therefore, the court overruled prior case law which concluded that a qualified right to a public preliminary examination was not constitutionally guaranteed. The circuit court lacked an analysis of a factual basis, utilizing factors to support its order.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition for supervisory writ and vacated the order of the circuit court. The cause was remanded.

In re Bar Admission of Crowe


No. 87-0161-BA


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


141 Wis. 2d 230; 414 N.W.2d 41; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 706


September 9, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
October 22, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of Board of Attorneys Professional Competence decision.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant sought review of a decision of the Board of Attorneys Professional Competence (Wisconsin), which did not recommend the admission of the applicant to the practice of law in the state on proof of practice elsewhere because he failed to meet the requirements of either Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 40.05(1) or (2).


OVERVIEW: During the five-year period relevant to the application for admission to practice law in Wisconsin on proof of practice elsewhere, the applicant engaged in the private practice of law for 10 months in Tennessee, the only jurisdiction in which he was admitted to the bar. He then worked for three years as an attorney for an Illinois corporation. Thereafter, he served as corporate counsel for a Wisconsin company. The Board determined that the applicant's employment in Illinois did not satisfy the requirements of Rule 40.05(1)(b) and denied admission. On review, the court affirmed. Because the applicant's legal work for the Illinois corporation occurred in jurisdictions in which he was not admitted to the practice of law, that work must have been the kind generally engaged in by attorneys in the private practice of law in order to meet the practice requirements of Rule 40.05(1)(b). The court agreed with the Board's conclusion that the applicant failed to establish that the legal work for the corporation was that of a person primarily engaged in the active practice of law. The court held that Rule 40.05 did not unconstitutionally discriminate against non-residents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Board's decision to decline to recommend the admission of the applicant to the practice of law in Wisconsin.

State ex rel. Smith v. Oak Creek


No. 85-1470


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


139 Wis. 2d 788; 407 N.W.2d 901; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 687


May 28, 1987, Argued  
June 26, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming 131 Wis. 2d 451, 389 N.W.2d 366 (Ct. App. 1986).

Review of a decision of the court of appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Decision affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bar owner sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the lower court's order dismissing the bar owner's petition for certiorari review of a decision by respondent Common Council of respondent City of Oak Creek denying the bar owner's request for renewal of an alcoholic beverage license on the ground that he was a habitual law offender.


OVERVIEW: The Common Council denied the bar owner's request for renewal of his alcoholic beverage license on the basis of information revealed in his voluntary testimony as a witness in the trial of another. In that testimony, the bar owner admitted that he had used, purchased, and sold illegal drugs on several occasions. The bar owner sought certiorari review of the Council's decision and a mandatory injunction ordering the Council to renew the license. The lower court dismissed the bar owner's petition and the appellate court affirmed. The bar owner sought review. The court rejected the bar owner's argument that the provision in Wis. Stat. § 125.04(5) permitting denial of licenses for persons who were habitual law offenders was applicable only if the person had been repeatedly convicted. The court stated that what the statute required was that offenses had been committed and that the law had been violated; it did not require that there have been convictions for each or any offense. The court also rejected the bar owner's argument that it was unfair to deny the license based on his voluntary testimony, noting that he had acknowledged that his testimony could cost him his liquor license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court decision that affirmed the lower court decision dismissing the bar owner's request for certiorari review of the Common Council's decision denial of his application for renewal of his alcoholic beverage license.

Ziegler Co. v. Rexnord, Inc.


No. 86-0462


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


139 Wis. 2d 593; 407 N.W.2d 873; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 682


May 29, 1987, Argued  
June 25, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for reconsideration filed.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the court of appeals.

Review of the decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed; the judgment of the circuit court is reversed and the cause is remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff distributor filed a complaint against defendant manufacturer after the manufacturer refused to renew a distributorship agreement. Each moved for summary judgment in the circuit court. The Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) affirmed a grant of summary judgment in favor of the manufacturer. The distributor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The distributor asserted that as a matter of law the manufacturer had no good cause for refusing to renew the dealership. The manufacturer asserted that as a matter of law the distributor was not a dealer within the meaning of the Wisconsin Fair Dealership Law, as codified Wis. Stat. ch. 135 (1985-86). The court concluded that (1) the court of appeals and the circuit court erred by examining only one factor (the fixed percentage test) of the business relationship to determine the requisite community of interest, (2) summary judgment could not have been granted by applying the correct legal test (the two guideposts for determining community of interest were continuing financial interest and interdependence) because material facts were in dispute, and (3) there was no need to reach the issue of whether the manufacturer had good cause for refusal to renew the agreement because the court would not decide the constitutionality of the statute when other grounds for decision were present.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals and the circuit court was reversed and the case was remanded for a determination of the community of interest issue under the correct legal standard.

In re Petition to Review State Bar Bylaw Amendments


No. 86-1479-OA


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


139 Wis. 2d 686; 407 N.W.2d 923; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 692


April 1, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
June 24, 1987, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, 25 lawyers licensed to practice law in the State of Wisconsin, sought review of a bylaw adopted by the Board of Governors of the State Bar of Wisconsin to establish a procedure by which a member would challenge the amount of the legislative activities dues reduction determined by the State Bar.


OVERVIEW: The Wisconsin Supreme Court adopted SCR 10.03(5)(b), which instituted a dues reduction plan for State Bar members who objected to State Bar legislative activity. The rule authorized members to deduct from their dues prior to payment a pro rata portion of the amount budgeted by the State Bar for legislative activities. The State Bar adopted a bylaw that established a procedure by which members could challenge the amount of the legislative activities dues reduction. Twenty-five members of the State Bar petitioned to the state supreme court for a review of the bylaw, contending that the procedure did not meet the constitutional requirements of a dues arbitration procedure. In rejecting petitioners' contention, the court agreed with the position of the State Bar that there was no constitutional requirement for an arbitration procedure in connection with the dues reduction plan but that the arbitration procedures established by the bylaw met the appropriate legal requirements by providing for prompt resolution of a dispute via arbitration and by satisfying the requirement that adequate explanation of the calculation of the dues reduction be given to members.


OUTCOME: The petition was rejected, and the State Bar was directed to propose additional provisions to the dues reduction arbitration procedure.

State v. Horn


No. 85-0246-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


139 Wis. 2d 473; 407 N.W.2d 854; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 693


March 4, 1987, Argued  
June 23, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming 126 Wis. 2d 447, 377 N.W.2d 176 (Ct. App. 1985).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This was a review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), affirming a judgment and order of a circuit court convicting defendants of criminal trespass contrary to Wis. Stat. § 943.13(1)(b) (1981-1982). The trial court also entered an order denying defendants' motion for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, who were church pastors and a pastor's wife, protested abortion at the facility. They were twice arrested for trespass. Defendants sought protection from private interference with their speech activities. The court concluded that defendants' actions were not constitutionally protected. The trial court properly granted the State's motion in limine, suppressing any evidence related to a "free speech defense." The dispositive factor in ruling on the availability of the "free speech defense" was whether there was any State interference with the alleged speech activities. The actions of the State in enforcing trespass laws had no relevance in determining the nature of ownership and the character of the intrusion in this free speech context. If enforcement of trespass laws by the State automatically meant that private interference with speech activities became "tinged" and was thereby transformed into governmental interference, this would have the effect of precluding private property owners from enforcing their rights to be free from trespassing speech activities on their property.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was affirmed.

Bachowski v. Salamone


No. 86-0281


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


139 Wis. 2d 397; 407 N.W.2d 533; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 676


February 10, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
June 19, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review of a decision of the court of appeals.

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals affirming an order of the Milwaukee County Circuit Court, Judge Leander J. Foley, Jr., presiding.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review of an order of the court of appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the constitutionality of an injunction in favor of appellee neighbor that enjoined the individual from harassing the neighbor, from having any contact with the neighbor, or coming on the neighbor's property.


OVERVIEW: An individual challenged a decision affirming the issuance of an injunction against her enjoining her from harassing her neighbor. On appeal, the court reversed the decision. The court held that Wis. Stat. Ann. § 813.125 provided sufficient notice and was neither vague or overbroad. The court found that § 813.125 precluded a judge from granting an injunction unless reasonable notice was given. The court also found that although the key words of § 813.125 were not expressly defined, to a person of ordinary intelligence the words harass or intimidate clearly connoted more than mere bothersome or annoying behavior. The court further found that the zone of conduct regulated by § 813.125 was clear and did not by its terms, sweep within its ambit actions which were constitutionally protected so as to render it unconstitutionally overbroad. Yet, the court determined that due to the disparity between what was alleged in the petition and what was offered and proven at trial, the proof was insufficient as a matter of law to support the issuance of the injunction. Thus, the court ruled that § 813.125 was improperly applied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order.

State v. Sarlund

Appeal from a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County, James C. Boll, Circuit Judge.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which vacated defendant's conviction for violating an injunction that was issued pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 813.125 upon finding that Wis. Stat. § 813.125 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court subsequently vacated defendant's conviction upon finding that defendant's plea of no contest was not knowingly and voluntarily made and that § 813.125 was unconstitutional. The court remanded the case to the trial court for a hearing to determine the whether defendant's plea was knowingly and voluntarily made.

189 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Grant


No. 85-1137-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


139 Wis. 2d 45; 406 N.W.2d 744; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 672


November 25, 1986, Argued  
June 11, 1987, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion for reconsideration denied.


PRIOR HISTORY: Review of a decision of the court of appeals.

Review of an unpublished decision by the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault and robbery. The crimes occurred late at night in the victim's home. On appeal, the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) determined that reversible error occurred when the jury was permitted to hear other acts evidence of defendant's arrest for prowling shortly after the instant crimes. The appellate court declined to find that harmless error occurred. The State sought review of this decision.


OVERVIEW: At issue was whether the appellate court properly applied the harmless error test in reviewing the trial court's erroneous decision to admit other acts evidence of defendant's prowling arrest. The court overturned the appellate court's decision. Under the harmless error test, the reviewing court must set aside the verdict unless it is sure that the error did not influence the jury or had such slight effect as to be de minimus. The reviewing court must determine whether there is a reasonable possibility that the error contributed to the conviction. In assessing this, the focus should be on whether the error undermines the appellate court's confidence in the outcome of the case. Trial error is analyzed in the context of the entire trial. When the erroneous admission of other acts evidence is involved, an assessment of the evidence untainted by the error should be conducted. Here, identification was the major issue at trial. The victim provided extensive testimony indicating that she had the ability to get a thorough look at defendant and that he was the perpetrator. There was no reasonable possibility that the error contributed to the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court.

State ex rel. Department of Dev. v. State Bldg. Com.


No. 86-1137-OA


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


139 Wis. 2d 1; 406 N.W.2d 728; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 671


January 7, 1987, Argued  
June 9, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Action for declaratory judgment.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Rights declared. Section 560.04(3), Stats., (1985), is unconstitutional as it violates Article VIII, sec. 10, of the Wisconsin Constitution.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The matter was before the court on an original action for declaratory judgment brought by petitioner Wisconsin Department of Development against respondent State of Wisconsin Building Commission, questioning whether Wis. Stat. § 560.04(3) (1985), which authorized the State through the Department to make loans to private real estate developers for privately owned low and moderate income housing, violated Wis. Const. art. VIII, § 10.


OVERVIEW: Wis. Const. art. VIII, § 10 prohibited the State from contracting any debt for works of internal improvement. In its declaratory judgment as to Wis. Stat. §560.04(3) (1985), the court found that the questions to be answered in any challenge to legislation under that constitutional provision were whether the object sought to be accomplished was an internal improvement, and whether it called for the State to contract any debt to carry it out or caused the State to be a party in carrying on such works. The Department and the Commission agreed that because bonds were to be paid off from revenue generated in the pay back by the borrowers and because the State did not guarantee payment to the bondholders in the event of default, the State was not contracting any debt. However, the court determined that the authority given to the Department in Wis. Stat. § 560.04 (1985) could not be sustained. The court rejected the reasoning that the State was not involved in housing, but instead was providing a solution. The court found that the State was financing housing rather than acting through an independent authority, which had previously been accepted as not violating the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that statute in question violated the State's constitution.

 

191 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Dowd v. New Richmond


Nos. 84-1538, 85-0140


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


137 Wis. 2d 539; 405 N.W.2d 66; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 658


February 6, 1987, Argued  
May 11, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On review of a decision of the court of appeals.

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, accused and wife, sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which affirmed the trial court's summary judgment dismissal of their complaint against respondents, city, witnesses, and complainants, seeking damages for civil rights violations and awarded attorney's fees to the city.


OVERVIEW: A complaint was filed alleging that the accused had sexually molested complainant's foster child. The charges were subsequently dismissed, with the last charges being dismissed at the prosecutor' request after it appeared that the State's alibi rebuttal witnesses had given perjured testimony. Petitioners then brought suit to recover damages for violations of their civil rights by respondents making false criminal charges and allegedly conspiring to present perjured testimony at the criminal trial. The trial court granted summary judgment dismissing petitioners' claims. The court of appeals and the court affirmed the dismissal. The court found that the grant of summary judgment to the city was proper because the allegations did not refer to any specific facts that could establish the existence of a policy or custom of inadequate training or supervision. As to the witnesses, the court held that there was no remedy for their testimony at the criminal trial, as witnesses were shielded by absolute immunity. Further, there was insufficient evidence to establish that the witnesses overtly conspired to deprive the accused of his right to due process by manufacturing false evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals, which affirmed the trial court's summary judgment dismissal of petitioners' civil rights complaint against respondents and the award of attorney's fees to the city.

 

192 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. McCoy v. Wisconsin Court of Appeals, Dist. 1


No. 86-0172-W


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


137 Wis. 2d 90; 403 N.W.2d 449; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 648


January 5, 1987, Argued  
April 9, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for declaration of rights.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Rights declared.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a public defender assigned to handle the appeal of a defendant's criminal conviction, filed a declaratory judgment action and challenged the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 809.32(1), the so-called "no-merit brief" requirement.


OVERVIEW: Upon determining that a criminal appeal would be frivolous, it was necessary for appointed counsel to submit a brief to the court of appeals, which included an explanation as to why any issues which might arguably support an appeal lacked merit, in accordance with Wis. Stat. § 809.32(1). The public defender challenged the constitutionally of the statute based upon his contention that the provisions of the statute violated a defendant's constitutionally-protected right to counsel under U.S. Const. amend. VI and Wis. Const. art. I, § 7. The court entered a declaratory judgment upholding the constitutionality of the statute. In reaching its decision, the court held that a defendant was not deprived of any of his constitutional rights as a result of the statute. Furthermore, the court held that statute was not a requirement that an attorney engage in a protracted argument in favor of the conclusion reached. Therefore, the court affirmed the constitutionality of the procedure.


OUTCOME: The court entered a declaratory judgment, holding that the statute was constitutional.

 

193 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Paternity of D.L.T.


No. 85-0367


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


137 Wis. 2d 57; 403 N.W.2d 434; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 647


January 7, 1987, Submitted on briefs  
April 8, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from the court of appeals.

Appeal from an order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha county, Patrick L. Snyder, Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Order reversed and cause remanded with directions to dismiss the state's complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which reversed an order of a court commissioner who had dismissed respondent State of Wisconsin's paternity action because the period of limitations had run. The court considered the appeal on the certification of the court of appeals pursuant to Wis. R. Civ. P., Wis. Stat. § 809.61.


OVERVIEW: On May 19, 1984, a paternity action was commenced by the State against the father of a child born out of wedlock on January 14, 1976. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 990.06 (1975), the statute of limitations for the cause of action in 1976 was five years. The limitations period was extended to 6 years in 1980 and to 19 years in 1984. On appeal of the circuit court's decision, the State argued that the 1984 amendment revived its cause of action by setting aside the strictures of § 990.06 and that the language expressly provided for the abrogation of the rule of statutory construction stated in the statute. The court held that the action was barred by the statute of limitation because the State's cause of action accrued upon the birth of the child and the statute of limitations then in effect was five years. The court determined that the express language of the 1984 amendment made the newly enacted period of limitations retrospectively applicable to causes of action for paternity that had accrued but which had not at the time of the new legislation been time-barred. The legislation did not, however, revive a barred cause of action.


OUTCOME: Order reversed and cause remanded with directions to dismiss the state's complaint.

 

194 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Amendment of SCR 70.36: Judges' Certification of Status of Pending Cases


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


136 Wis. 2d 394; 402 N.W.2d 358; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 712



March 12, 1987, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was a report of the Director of State Courts (Wisconsin) which concerned the administration of Wis. Sup. Ct. R. 70.36 establishing time periods for judges of the circuit court to decide matters submitted for decision and requiring circuit judges to certify monthly their compliance with the requirements of Rule 70.36. The court also considered a Legislative Council Law Revision Committee's request to amend the rule.


OVERVIEW: The adoption of Rule 70.36 occurred in the context of a judicial disciplinary proceeding concerning, in part, a judge's failure to comply with Wis. Stat. § 757.025 prohibiting a judge of a court of record from receiving any salary unless the judge first executed an affidavit stating that no matter submitted in final form to the court for decision remains undecided for more than 90 days. The court in a previous decision had held that the statute was an unconstitutional interference with the judicial branch of government and adopted the rule establishing substantially the same requirements, with the exception of the salary withholding provision. The petition of the Committee sought the restoration of the salary withholding provision by inclusion in the court's rule. The court held that in light of the availability of the remedial measures, the imposition of which was discretionary with the court as circumstances warranted, the addition of a proposed salary withholding provision, which would apply to every failure of a judge to comply with the time periods and certification requirements of the rule without regard to the cause thereof, was neither necessary nor desirable.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for the inclusion of a salary withholding provision and adopted the amendments to the rule suggested by the director of state courts that the certification under the rule be made by certificate rather than by affidavit and that notice of an extension of time to comply with the rule obtained by a circuit judge be given by the circuit judge rather than by the chief judge of the judicial administrative district.

 

195 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Liberty Homes, Inc. v. Department of Industry, Labor & Human Relations


No. 82-2427


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


136 Wis. 2d 368; 401 N.W.2d 805; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 640


September 4, 1986, Argued  
March 9, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming 125 Wis. 2d 492, 374 N.W.2d 142 (Ct. App. 1985).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals modifying the judgment of the circuit court for Dane county, Judge W.L. Jackman.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant three mobile home builders sought review of a judgment by the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin) that upheld the validity of Wis. Adm. Code, § Ind. 14.03, which regulated the indoor air quality of new mobile homes, in favor of respondent Wisconsin Department of Industry, Labor and Human Relations (DILHR).


OVERVIEW: The mobile home builders filed a declaratory judgment seeking to have § Ind. 14.03 declared invalid because the rule was factually unsupported. They argued because the .4 ppm standard and the test method of § Ind. 14.03 prescribed to assure compliance were not supported by credible evidence, the rule violates their constitutional right to due process of law. The trial court held that § Ind. 14.03 was constitutionally valid, as did the court of appeals. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court noted that the determinative question was whether the DILHR's promulgation of the rules was rationally connected to the facts in the record. The court held that there were facts of record that reasonably supported the DILHR's choice of the .4 ppm standard and the NIOSH P and CAM 125 test procedures. Thus, the court concluded that the rule was reasonably related to the legitimate governmental objective of safe and sanitary design and construction of mobile homes and therefore did not violate the mobile home builder's due process rights. The court noted that record indicated that the agency thoroughly reviewed available medical and scientific evidence and alternative resolutions of the problem.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the constitutionality of the statute that regulated the ambient indoor air quality of mobile homes.

 

196 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Chappy v. Labor & Industry Review Com.


No. 84-2320


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


136 Wis. 2d 172; 401 N.W.2d 568; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 561


January 6, 1987, Argued  
March 6, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Affirming 128 Wis. 2d 318, 381 N.W.2d 552 (Ct. App. 1985).

Review of a decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The decision of the court of appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a company owner and companies, sought review from a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Wisconsin), which had affirmed a decision in favor of appellees, the state labor review commission and an employee, on the company owner's suit seeking to challenge an award of increased temporary total disability benefits to the employee under Wis. Stat. § 102.43(7)(b) (1979-80).


OVERVIEW: The company owner argued that the retroactive application of the statute was unconstitutional in that it violated the contract clause and the right to due process when it increased the company owner's workers' compensation payments. The state labor review commission argued that the company owner could not challenge the constitutionality of the application of the statute because he had already waived the challenge by making the payments. The court found that: (1) the company owner could challenge the constitutionality of the provision and its applicability to him; (2) the legislature had intended the provision to have retroactive effect; (3) the provision did not violate the contract clause of the constitution because the state had the right to require employers to increase workers' compensation to account for inflation; (4) the legislation was reasonable; and (5) the company owner's due process rights had not been violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment affirming the decision in favor of the state labor review commission and the employee on the company owner's challenge the increased temporary total disability benefits.

 

197 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Unnamed Petitioners v. Connors


No. 86-0290-W


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


136 Wis. 2d 118; 401 N.W.2d 782; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 565


September 4, 1986, Argued  
March 6, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Accepted for review upon the court's own motion.

Petition For Supervisory Writ.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner professional football players sought a writ of prohibition to prohibit respondent trial judge from holding a Wis. Stat. § 968.02(3) hearing to determined if a criminal complaint could be filed even though the district attorney refused to issue a complaint.


OVERVIEW: The football players were accused of assaulting a female dancer at a nightclub. The district attorney decided not to issue a criminal complaint on the basis of his perceived inability to prove their guilt. The matter was assigned to the trial judge for a § 968.02(3) proceedings. The football players filed a petition for a writ of prohibition to prevent the proceedings from taking place. The court granted the writ of prohibition. The court held that § 968.02(3) was unconstitutional because it allowed the trial judge to permit the filing of a complaint after the district attorney, in the exercise of his discretion, found that no criminal charge should issue. The court reasoned that § 968.02(3) allowed a complete and direct substitution of a judge's decision for the action of a duly appointed or elected prosecutor. The court found that § 968.02(3) unconstitutionally constituted a substantial encroachment upon the discretionary power of the executive branch to prosecute or not. The court noted that in cases where the district attorney was unavailable to act, the trial judge could appoint one pursuant to Wis. Stat. Ann. § 59.44(1).


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of prohibition.

 

198 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Treiber v. Knoll


No. 85-2115


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


135 Wis. 2d 58; 398 N.W.2d 756; 1987 Wisc. LEXIS 548


October 28, 1986, Argued  
January 6, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On bypass of the court of appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County: Leo B. Hanley, Reserve Circuit Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court is reversed and the cause is remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county treasurer sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted judgment for plaintiff estate in its action seeking a declaratory judgment that Wis. Stat. § 814.66(1)(a) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The estate sought a judgment that § 814.66(1)(a) was unconstitutional. Section 814.66(1)(a) established the filing fees to be collected by the register in probate proceedings concerning decedents' estates. The fees were based on the size of the estate. The court reversed and remanded the trial court's decision. The disputed assessment, although designated a fee in the statute, was in reality a tax upon the disposition of one's property upon death. Where the amount of an exaction was in no way dependent upon the amount of services provided by the judge or register in probate, but depended entirely upon the valuation of the estate, then the exaction was a tax. Because a tax measure was involved the presumption of constitutionality was strongest. All probate litigants had an ascertainable estate which, through probate, was distributed to the decedents' heirs or beneficiaries, as well as creditors, and thus were similarly situated. The tax treated those similarly, therefore there was no equal protection violation. The exaction, paid equally by all estates, taxed in proportion to the relative distributive benefits received from the judgment of the probate court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's decision.

 

199 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stoehr


No. 85-1090-CR


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


134 Wis. 2d 66; 396 N.W.2d 177; 1986 Wisc. LEXIS 2068


October 1, 1986, Argued  
November 25, 1986, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification from court of appeals.

Appeal from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County: James W. Karch, Judge.



DISPOSITION: By the Court. -- The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant under Wis. Stat. § 946.13(1)(b) (1983-84) of performing, in his official capacity as a public officer, a function requiring the exercise of discretion on his part with regard to a contract in which he had a direct or indirect private pecuniary interest. Defendant claimed the state failed to prove that he had a corrupt motive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a public officer, promoted and maintained an adult education system. As part of a program to provide vocational assistance to foreign nations, defendant received honorariums for work he allegedly performed during vacation time or his own available time. Defendant was convicted under Wis. Stat. § 946.13(1)(b) (1983-84) of performing, in his official capacity as a public officer, a function requiring the exercise of discretion on his part with regard to a contract in which he had a direct or indirect private pecuniary interest. The court affirmed, determining that the legislative history indicated that § 946.13(1)(b) was a strict liability crime and the state did not have to prove that defendant had a corrupt motive. Defendant was not entitled to an instruction on the statutory defense of privilege because he failed to produce sufficient evidence to show that his conduct was an apparently authorized fulfillment of any duties of public office, an element of the statutory defense of privilege under Wis. Stat. § 939.45(3) (1983-84). Section 946.13(1)(b), which authorized a prison term as a penalty, did not violate due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for performing, as a public officer, a function requiring the exercise of discretion with regard to a contract in which he had a direct or indirect private pecuniary interest because the offense was a strict liability crime in that the state did not need to prove scienter. Defendant failed to present enough evidence at trial to warrant a jury instruction on a statutory privilege defense.

 

200 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Swan v. Elections Bd.


Nos. 84-1344-W, 84-1345-W


Supreme Court of Wisconsin


133 Wis. 2d 87; 394 N.W.2d 732; 1986 Wisc. LEXIS 2060



October 16, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Review of a decision of the court of appeals.



DISPOSITION: Decision vacated and petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Election Board petitioned for a review of the decision of the Wisconsin Court of Appeals, which directed the Board to certify petitioner, a potential political candidate, as a candidate for the Democratic Party nomination for state senator. The potential candidate had challenged Wis. Stat. § 8.30(4) as unconstitutional because it did not permit an unpardoned felon to be placed on the ballot for a state or local office.


OVERVIEW: The potential political candidate had been convicted of two federal felonies and had served his sentence. The Board's staff denied his certification as a candidate to be placed on the ballot. A petition was filed on his behalf in the appellate court, asking that it exercise original jurisdiction because the matter was publici juris. He asked that the finding that § 8.30(4) was unconstitutional be implemented by a writ of mandamus, which the appellate court granted. The Board challenged the decision. The court held that the appellate court had no original jurisdiction over the matter. Wis. Const. art. VII, § 5(3) provided the jurisdictional basis for the appellate court. The appellate court had no original jurisdiction other than by prerogative writ. The provision did not grant the appellate court supervisory jurisdiction over matters pending before administrative bodies. The circuit courts had jurisdiction over actions to review agency decisions. The appellate court was not granted the power to issue a prerogative writ in a situation where there was no basis for the exercise of its supervisory or appellate powers. The court of appeals was a court of limited writ jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the appellate court's decision and dismissed the petition.
